FORWARD BY THE PRESIDENT

It is my pleasure in this, my second year as President of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, to write a few words at the beginning of what I think will prove an extremely interesting and factual account of the life of a Club of which we are all very fond. Many of you who have been as fortunate as I in enjoying the fellowship and companionship which have always been the mark of the Overseas tradition, will realise how sad I feel that Overseas is now drawing to a close. Over the years, I have made many friends and acquaintances through the rugby, soccer, hockey and cricket sections, as well as amongst the many social members who have played a distinct role in supporting our club.

Not least of these is my good friend, Norman Morgan. Norman was a member of the Club first of all in 1948 when he completed his first tour here in Malta. He was a rugby-playing member until 1950. He then left the island, only to return in 1956, when he became an even more active member of a Club which became his first love. In 1958, during what was to be a reformation of the Club, he undertook no less than three tasks, those of Honorary Secretary, Team Secretary and Membership Secretary. On leaving the island in 1959, he thought his association with Overseas might be at a close, but this was not to be for in 1965 he returned and immediately became a member of the Bar Management Committee. In 1966, he was made assistant Secretary and the following year, became the Club's extremely active Honorary Secretary. It was during this year that he completely organized a magnificent rugby tour to Sicily. This will long be remembered by those who participated.

On 11th September, 1969, Norman Morgan was awarded what was for him the ultimate honour by the Club - that of Honorary Life Member. Norman again left the island, and, following the withdrawal of the British Services from Malta in January, 1972, thought that this was the end of the Overseas. However, on his return to the island for yet another tour in 1973, he was pleased to see the Club functioning as strongly as ever. He again took up the gavel and became Secretary of Rugby and Cricket Sections, as well as becoming a Vice President and Membership Secretary.

It was during this time that he decided to write this History of the Club and after 5 years of heartache, toil, thousands of letters and phone calls, this wonderful document is the end result. It is a fitting tribute to Norman himself who, along with his and our dear friend, Jack Sharp, must together share the title of 'Mr. Overseas'. Our heartfelt thanks, Norman, for your hard work and efforts on our behalf.

T. N. RICKETTS.

P R E F A C E

The Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, Malta, was formed in November, 1946. For 27 years 'Overseas' was purely a rugby club and known as the Overseas Rugby Club or Overseas R.U.F.C. It was not until 1973 that 'Overseas' became a 'Rugby and Sports Club'. Readers must keep this in mind. This history deals almost exclusively with rugby matters up to 1973 and therefore the Club will be referred to by its former name to that point.

A further point to keep in mind is that no record remains of any minutes kept until 1954. I have been informed by Secretaries of the Club prior to 1954 that records were in fact kept and passed on to their successors. It will remain a mystery. Minutes remain of one meeting held on the 27th November, 1954, and then another blank until minutes were kept of a meeting of the 6th September, 1958. Minutes have been kept, and remained in safe keeping of the Club, continuously since September, 1958. No copies of correspondence were retained until 1956. During these early years I was a member of Overseas from November, 1948, to March, 1950, and again from November, 1956, to July, 1959. This still left gaps in knowledge of the Club and even as I started to write this history, I searched and corresponded with former members, including two who were founder members in 1946. Even so, there are still periods when information on the Club is slight, and it is to be hoped that if any former members reading this history can fill in any blanks, he (or she) will contact me or the Overseas Club.

Events in this history will be written in chronological order within the year they happen. On the other hand, any subject considered to be of sufficient importance, and which covers a number of years, I will complete that part of the history whilst writing about the year in which it was initiated. Monetary values will be written in sterling, Lsd or decimal, or Maltese currency, according to the system in use during the period being written about. Malta retained our (U.K.) pre-decimal sterling coins up to the 16th May, 1972, when they changed to their own decimal coins, i.e. 100 cents to the Maltese pound. I have attempted to compile a year by year list of games and results, also to make a chart of all Officials and certain details of the Club from its inception. These are not complete, especially for the years before 1958/59. I have also collected team photos of Overseas XV's and I believe, from correspondence with ex members in an attempt to trace back copies, that I have a copy of a team photo for every year in which one was taken.

Throughout this history the 'Services' are continuously mentioned and unless specifically stated otherwise, this refers to the British Armed Forces. This is obvious to anyone who has lived in Malta, but perhaps not otherwise.

Extraordinary General Meeting on Future of the Club 165

Part I

The Formation of Overseas R.F.C.

The idea of forming a civilian rugby club in 1946 was first mooted by sportsmen who were attached to, or associated with, what was then the naval 'Dockyard', and details of its beginning come mainly from two of its founder members, Mr Trevor Lewis and Lt. Cdr. R. Meredith (Rtd). Trevor claims to be the original member of Overseas. A civilian with Admiralty, he arrived in Malta in February, 1946, and immediately started looking for a game of rugby. Having no team of his own, he haunted the Marsa in hopes that teams would arrive short. Eventually, he spoke to the Commodore Superintendent of the Dockyard, Commodore D. Orr-Ewing, on the subject, and the Commodore suggested that Trevor form his own rugby team. This was the beginning. With the complete backing and authority of Commodore Orr-Ewing, signals were sent to Dockyard, Civilian and Service Units querying initial support for starting a rugby club. There was an immediate response from 20 to 30 interested sportsmen, including Mr Fred Hitchcock, who, with Trevor, became one of the inaugurating Officials of the Club.

Ray Meredith arrived in Malta in March, 1946, and as an Instructor Lieutenant, R.N., he was appointed to re-open H.M. Dockyard Children's School in two semi-detached villas, 'Sunshine' and 'Sea Foam', at Tal H’biex. Ray tells of an informal meeting held towards the end of 1946 in the bar of Queens Hall, Old College Street, Sliema, when a group of cricket and tennis players discussed forming a Dockyard Rugby Club. I assume that this informal meeting was the response to Trevor's initial signals. It was then realised that there would not be sufficient playing membership in the Dockyard and it was decided to call a meeting of all interested in playing rugby, to include all U.K. and Commonwealth personnel who were working in Malta, and who were unattached to Service Units.

The formation meeting called was the first Annual General Meeting of the Club although at this stage it would be premature to call it the 'Overseas'. This first A.G.M. was held in November, 1946, in the A.S.V. (Admiralty Salvage Vessels) Club in Regent House, Tower Road, Sliema. Regent House stood at the junction of Tigne Street and Tower Road and was pulled down in 1953 to make way for Bisazza Street. The entrance to Regent House was approached up an open and fairly wide iron staircase. This meeting place was described in some detail by Trevor and also confirmed by Ray. I personally remember Regent House, although I did not know of its connection with Overseas at the time. In the local newspaper 'Times of Malta', 25th October, 1946, an advert was inserted saying 'Regent House Sliema, Grand re-opening, Thursday, 31st October (1946), Select Dances and Variety Turns, formal dress optional', although this does not necessarily mean that the ASV Club was not in residence before or during renovation of Regent House. Approximately 25 men attended the formation meeting - 23 or so being prepared to play. Mr Fred Hitchcock was elected as Chairman, a position he held with distinction until he left Malta in June 1952. Ray Desucribes the type of person who attended this meeting as 'personnel from the Yard, R.N., who

    came under the Commodore Superintendent of the Yard like
    himself, Land's Department, Dingli w/toutation, and the odd
    body seconded to Malta for Army duties etc'.

    The formation meeting was opened by Fred Hitchcock and
    Trevor Lewis, and on addressing those attending Fred outlined
    the general concept to form a Rugby Club of U.K. personnel or
    personnel attached to small units, civilians, etc. In Trevor's
    own words: 'From there the Club was formed'.

    The names of the first Officials of the Club, elected in
    November, 1946 also names of the first members, although I
    cannot confirm that they all attended the formation meeting,
    were as follows:—
    
    President              Commodore D. Orr-Ewing
    Chairman               F. Hitchcock
    Hon. Secretary         D. Calnan
    Hon. Treasurer         R. Price
    Hon. Social Secretary  R. Meredith
    Team Captain           H. Hodges
    Vice-Captain           R. Tallick
    Selection Committee    T. Lewis
    Committee - D. Hope, J. Dyer, Over, W. Wainwright.
    Members - R.H. McIntosh, T. May, Yates, D. Carrol,
              Robinson, D. Walker, Brocklehurst, Ramage,
              Thirscutt, P. Cheeseman.

    During this first season, although deeply involved in the
    Club's formation, Trevor Lewis declined all Offices. This
    was due to the fact that he lived at Mdina. However, he did
    serve on Committees, and with move of residence to Sliema he
    took up Office of Hon. Secretary for the two seasons, 1947/49.
    He left Malta in June, 1949.

    NAME OF THE CLUB
    From the response received at the formation meeting it 
    was decided that there was sufficient interest and playing 
    strength to form the Club. The name of the Club was discussed, 
    and in view of the diversity of employment of the interested 
    parties, it was decided that an all embracing title should be 
    assumed. Both Trevor and Ray say that it was decided to call 
    the Club the 'Overseas Rugby Football Club' and from then one 
    would assume that it was at this first A.G.M. that the name 
    'Overseas' was decided upon. However, in my initial searches 
    for information and old members to write to, I contacted the 
    person who had owned and managed the Queens Hall, Old College 
    Street, Sliema, a Mr Paul Magro. From its earliest days the 
    Club had held dances at the Queens Hall. Mr Magro informed me 
    that Lt. R. Meredith (RN), who used to live in a flat belonging 
    to him, had arranged Overseas dances in the Queens Hall in 1947. 
    Fortunately, Paul Magro had kept his old registers and we found 
    that these dances, on different dates, were listed as being held 
    by both the Overseas RFC and the Dockyard RFC. Mr Magro confirmed 
    that all the dances were organised by the same people. So, nothing 
    loath, I contacted Mr C.O. Borg (Lino to his associates) in the 
    Office of Inland Revenue, Succession and other Duties Branch, 
    Monte di Pieta Buildings, 46, Merchant Street, Valletta, as I 
    had been informed that the Club would have had to apply there 
    for a permit to hold entertainment at the Queens Hall. Lino was

exceptionally helpful and the resulting information is given below. It would suggest that initially there was some confusion over the name of the Club.

Date Club applying for Permit Permit No Applicant on behalf of the Club
11.2.47 Dockyard Rugby Club 34 Lt. R. Meredith
17.3.47 Overseas RFC 132 R. Meredith
2.5.47 Dockyard Rugby Club 253 R. Meredith
31.10.47 (Name not given) Rugby Club 259 R. Meredith
12.3.48 Overseas Rugby Club R. Meredith
7.5.48 Overseas Rugby Club R. Meredith
26.11.48 Overseas Rugby Club R. Hitchcock

The dance held on the 17th March, 1947, was on St. Patrick's night and an article was inserted in the Sunday Times of Malta on the 23rd March, 1947. This did nothing to clear the matter as it said that the dance was organised by the 'Rugger Club' by Lt. Cdr. Meredith who also acted as M.C. On the other hand, the 2nd A.G.M. of the Club, which was held at the Queens Hall on the 7th October, 1947, was also registered with the Inland Revenue Office, presumably for a spirit licence. On this occasion the Club applying for the licence was given as the 'Overseas Rugby Club', and it would appear to confirm that, from this date at least, the Club was officially known by this name. This is partially borne out by details given to me by Mr Lino Borg appertaining to dances. When I joined the Club in November, 1948, there was no suggestion that the Club had been known as anything but 'Overseas RFC'.

THE FIRST PRESIDENT

Commodore D. Orr-Ewing, Overseas' first President, was deeply involved in setting the Club on its feet in this first season, making arrangements to provide pitch, posts, flags, strip, etc. He provided the 'physicals' whilst Trevor Lewis, initially on his own, then with Mr Fred Hitchcock and the Club Committee, brought the team together. The Commodore left Malta on the 19th December, 1947, after serving there for nearly two years. Unfortunately, he died in 1964, but his son, Mr C. Orr-Ewing, kindly supplied details of the Commodore's rugby playing days. It is very impressive. He was a Cambridge Blue in 1919, played for the Royal Navy a number of times, played for Hampshire and was a Scottish trialist. Also, when he was in South Africa, he played for a team called the Villagers.

Mr A.R.T. Wright, the Rugby Football Union historian, was more specific about Commodore Orr-Ewing's naval rugby record. He told me that the Commodore represented the Royal Navy in Inter-Service matches from 1920 to 1926 inclusive, and again in 1930, also that he played for the United Services Portsmouth. Further research by Mr Wright resulted in his finding a 1964 Harlequin F.C. member's list in which the Commodore was recorded as being a Life Member of the Club. Mr. Wright was also able to provide the following brief history of the 'Villager R.F.C.', the team for which the Commodore played in South Africa:

"The Villager R.F.C. is a Club founded in 1876 in Western Province, South Africa. Service men from the British Isles have played for this Club including V.G.E. Luddington (R.N. and England) and H.W. Stephenson (R.N. and Ireland)."

Mr. F. Hitchcock, Chairman, was one of the mainstays of Overseas from its inception to the time he left Malta in June, 1952. In fact, it has been generally believed over the years that he was the Founder Member. Almost true, but not quite. When starting research into the Club's beginning, I myself believed Mr. Hitchcock to be the initiator of the Club and attempted to trace him. This was to lead to a dead end as far as the Club's history was concerned, but it resulted in gathering very interesting information as regards rugby in Malta pre-war. Fred Hitchcock had been a U.K. Based Industrial (Foreman Electrician) in H.M. Dockyard, Malta, and armed with initial information from Montgomery House, Floriana, Malta, I wrote to Defence Accounts Office, Worcester, England. The DAO informed me that Fred had died in August, 1958. However, from two other sources I was informed of his possible connection with the pre- war "Exiles" and "E.R.A." Club(s), and the possible link between these club(s) and Overseas. When referred to appertaining to the pre-war period, the two clubs "Exiles" and "E.R.A.", always seemed tied together as one club. Further enquiries proved that no connection existed between Overseas and the Exiles/E.R.A.s, But I believe readers will be interested in the information gathered.

First, Commander E. Hamilton-Hill R.N. (Retd) informed me that the formation of Overseas Rugby Club stemmed from the run- down of the Exiles (Cable & Wireless) and the E.R.A. Club which used to run its own rugger side. At the same time the Commander stressed that his was a hazy recollection. Lt. - Cmdr R. Meredith informed me that Mr. Hitchcock was the oldest member at the meeting (November, 1946) and was a former playing member of the pre-war Exiles and E.R.A. Rugby Clubs. In further correspondence Lt. Cmdr Meredith shed more light on who the Exiles and E.R.A.s were by saying, "Mr. Hitchcock played for the 'Exiles' E.R.A.'s in Dockyard Appointments and that Cable & Wireless were the mainstay of the Club, together with Naval Officers on posts like the R.N. School and the Dockyard (Technical College)." I do know that the E.R.A. Rugby Club existed in Malta, as a separate Club, at least from after the war up to the 1954/55 season. Overseas played the E.R.A. club twice during the 1954/55 season, after which there is no further record of the E.R.A.s as rugby opponents.

In following up the "Exiles" club, I first contacted Officials at what was formerly Cable & Wireless, Mercury House, St. George's Road, St. Julians, Malta. Cable & Wireless in Malta became Telecommunication Corporation early in 1975. Here I was given the greatest help by Messrs. G.A. Cassar Trigona, M.Bonnici, A. Tortell and a former member of Cable & Wireless Staff, Mr R. Scerri. Between them they gave me the backgrounds to the Exiles Club, Malta. Mr Scerri, an all round sportsman & a younger man and Malta tennis champion for many years, remembered Cable & Wireless "Exiles" rugby team. He advised me to write to the Exiles Club, London, and to a Mr. A. J. Hatfield who had been a playing member of the Exiles rugby team and prominent in the organisation of the Exiles Club, Malta, in the 1920's. The Exiles Club,London, had no records or photos which would help, and none of the Club members who had been in Malta in the 20's could help answer my queries. However, corresponding with Mr. Hatfield gave me the following interesting information, and I copy his own words:

"The Exiles Club (London) was formed by the Eastern

Telegraph Company in 1921 and from that date E.T.C. sides played team games in all parts of the world. My own experience of rugger in Malta was from 1925 to 1927. We had a good side and could hold our own with such battleships as the 'Iron Duke', 'Valiant', 'Empress of India', 'Queen Elizabeth' and so on and in 1927 we won the Command Cup, defeating the R.A.F. Kalafrana, Border Regiment and, in the final, the Kings Own (Liverpool) Regiment. But from that time automation caught up with us and our cable staff dwindled sadly so that we were unable to raise any more teams. Personally, I moved on to Suez and Aden where we still maintained strong teams until 1929/30 when we amalgamated with the Marconi Company, Post Office and sundry other companies to form Cable & Wireless.

"When I returned to Malta in 1936 I found that the Exiles Club could produce no rugby team of its own and the Club could only make a showing at tennis - at which Mr. Robert Scerri excelled.

So, I think I can say quite definitely that the Exiles Club had no hand in the formation of the Overseas Rugby Club. We never raised a rugby team in Malta after 1927. I am afraid I didn't know Mr. H. Hitchcock and I do not think he was connected with the Exiles Club, as membership was restricted to the Cable Company's staff.

We played at the Marsa Club of which we were all members. The reason for this was that the Eastern Telegraph Company owned all the land that is now the Polo Ground. This land was presented to the Marsa Club on the condition that all U.K. based members of the Company should be automatic members of the Marsa Club and Tigne Bathing Club. That must have been some time after 1868 when the first cable was laid to Malta. The name "Exiles" was not used until about 1921 when the Club was formed in London and branches abroad took the same name. I think 1921 to 1927 about covers our rugger activities in Malta although we ran soccer teams considerably earlier under the name E.T.C."

The above information from Mr. Hatfield would prove that any amalgamation of the Exiles Club and the B.R.A. Club, and therefore the period when Mr. Hitchcock was a playing member of same, could possibly only have been between 1927 and 1936, i.e., when Mr. Hatfield was away from Malta. Otherwise, surely Mr. Hatfield would have known of any such amalgamation. Mr. Hitchcock was 40 years of age in 1936. Unfortunately, I do not know when he first served in Malta.

Overseas Colours

The first jerseys used by Overseas in 1946/47 were naval ratings summer shirts, tough linen, and provided by Commodore Orr-Ewing. The same season a set of jerseys, navy blue and white hoops, together with stockings and balls, were purchased through NAFFI. Navy blue and white have continued through the years to be the traditional colours of Overseas XVs. Ray Meredith informs me that the money, raised by holding dances, paid for this equipment, and at the same time helped the Club to become solvent.

First Season

Training sessions for at least the first season were held

6

twice a week, Tuesday and Thursday evenings, under lights on the tennis courts behind the Queens Hall, Old College Street. There was no coach and there was no organised training, it was a matter of fitness and occasional ball handling. Some dozen matches were played, January to March, 1947, with only one lost to the Air Arm Kalafrana. Ray Meredith has provided a team photo, taken behind the Queens Hall, for 1946/47.

WRITTEN RECORD OF OVERSEAS

Notices of the early life of the Club including its formation, social activities, fixtures and results, were published in Dockyard Temporary Memoranda (Malta). Unfortunately, all D.T.M.s were destroyed, possibly before, but definitely at the time of the British Forces withdrawal in 1972, and no record remains from this source. Likewise, all written records of 1946/47 kept by Trevor Lewis and Ray Meredith were disposed of before I wrote to them asking for details of the Club’s formation. Full searches were made through various records for any information about Overseas RFC, also for any connection between Overseas and clubs already mentioned, i.e. Dockyard, Exiles and RFA. All searches proved negative. A full list of departments and secretaries who carried out these searches on behalf of the Club have been given under ‘Acknowledgements to Non-Members’ at the front of this history.

OVERSEAS XVs HOME GROUND

Initially, in 1946/47 Overseas played on a makeshift pitch at Ta’ Qali airfield which was soon abandoned in favour of a pitch at Luqa airfield. The Commodore and Trevor Lewis, and, I assume, with other club Officials, selected a piece of ground at Luqa, and the Commodore negotiated with R.A.F. Officials that this would become Overseas’ home pitch. This pitch was situated to the Luqa side of the runway, approximately in front of what is now the civilian terminal (1977). The pitch had a light covering of grass but it was hard, almost gravel, and aircraft often stopped play. The players changed in one of the nissen huts in R.A.F. Site one, Luqa, by courtesy of the R.A.F., although during 1949/50 season we were able to make use of the newly built and improved changing facilities at Luqa Site two. In those days very few of the players owned cars and a bus was hired from Captains Garage, Tigne Street, Sliema, to take them to the Site and then to the pitch. The team photo of 1948/49 shows the bus and Luqa Site number two airman’s quarters in the background.

Trevor Lewis informed me that during the first season the Commodore decided we must have our own pitch, and in conjunction with Officials from the Civil Engineering Department from the Dockyard, Overseas selected a piece of ground at Ta’ Qali and preparations were made. Ta’ Qali was a Naval Air Station at the time. It was agreed that the only type of grass was a special kind from Texas and this was delivered by courtesy of the U.S. Air Force en route to one of their bases. This pitch had to lay unused for 2 to 3 years in order to bind the grass. Trevor, who left Malta in June, 1949, does not know if we ever played on it. No record remains of this particular pitch, and no other member I have contacted, and who followed on after the first season, can remember hearing about it.

Overseas continued playing at Luqa during 1948/49 and for the first half of 1949/50 season, after which we moved to Ta’ Qali.

It is difficult to be precise as to when we moved to Ta' Qali. I can confirm that we played at Luqa on the 27th November, 1949 against H.M.S. Falcon. On the 10th December, 1949, we played at Ta' Qali against the Med. Fleet. Also during the latter half of the 1948/49 season and the first half of the 1949/50 season we played once or twice at the Marsa, whether this was our home pitch, or the only pitch available at the time, I cannot be certain. During this period our away games against H.M.S. Falcon, the Fleet Air Arm Team, were played at Hal Far. At this time the runway was still in use and we occasionally had to take down the goal posts during a game when aircraft landed.

The use of the pitch at Ta' Qali started after Commander R.V. Brockman (now Vice-Admiral (Ret'd)) had scoured the island for a suitable piece of grass on which to play rugger. The area at Ta' Qali was decided on although it was hardly suitable as there were thousands of tiny shells. These were gradually cleared by the efforts of working parties, organised by Commander Martin Price R.N., the Commanding Officer at Ta' Qali, and the players.

New pitches were laid at Ta' Qali in 1952. It is recorded in the Times of Malta, 22nd November, 1952, that four full sized rugby football grounds had been constructed at R.N. Air Station (H.M.S. Goldfinch), Ta' Qali, to be shared with the R.A.F. and Army. By 1958/59 there were 6 full sized grounds at Ta' Qali allocated to different services. Two of these grounds were well laid near the perimeter road and were kept for Inter Service games and other special matches. The other four pitches were rougher, especially through continued use, but certainly an improvement on Luqa. The Australian Air Force was stationed at Ta' Qali from June, 1953 to approximately 1955, after which it was handed over to the R.A.F.

Overseas used Ta' Qali as their home ground from 1950 to 1960. From 1960 to the present date, our home ground has been at the Marsa. This final move was made when Marsa Lodge became our Club House. The rugby playing area at the Marsa was renovated in 1960 and the four pitches were known as Army 1 and 2 and Navy 1 and 2. Previously, the whole of the Marsa rugby playing area had been completely re-laid in late 1956.

Before the start of each rugby season Overseas received permission to use the pitches from the proper authority. This had been given by the Commanding Officer of the R.A.F. Station, Ta' Qali, and with the move to the Marsa, up to 1971/72, from the General Officer Commanding via the Secretary Army Rugby Football (Malta). In 1972 the whole of the Marsa playing area was taken over by the Maltese Government, and from this point we have played rugby at the Marsa by kind permission of the President of the Malta Sports Board.

During the early years, at least up to 1950, when the grounds were too hard to play rugby, the Overseas rugby team on the odd occasion played hockey against the rugby opponent of the day. On the odd occasion we played against civilian clubs. Imagine 11 rugby players, only one or two with knowledge of hockey, wielding sticks. We never won but we scared the living daylights out of the opposition!

1947 - 1952

ANNUAL GENERAL MEETING, 1947

After hours of searching through old copies of the Times of Malta in the Offices of Allied Malta Newspapers Ltd., St. Paul’s Street, Valletta, and the Public Library, Queen’s Square, Valletta, for written word of the beginning of the Club, the following notice appertaining to the second A.G.M. was found in the copy of the 30th September, 1947.

THE OVERSEAS RUGBY FOOTBALL CLUB

There will be a General Meeting of the Overseas Rugby Football Club on Tuesday, October, 7th, at 7p.m., at Queens Hall, Old College Street, Sliema.

The United Kingdom civilian personnel interested in the 1947-48 season are cordially invited to attend.

The Club is open to service personnel, particularly those of small units, which are themselves unable to field rugby teams.

From this notice it can be seen that although Overseas is a civilian club, the only one resident in Malta at that time, or since, notice of A.G.M.'s has always been directed to both civilian and service personnel. Having said this, it must be stated that the golden rule of the Club has always been, written or unwritten, that where there is a clash of fixtures, a service man's loyalty is first to his Service team.

For the 1947/48 season, the only Officials elected at the A.G.M. known for certain are as follows:

  • President: Commander E.A. Hamilton-Hill R.N.(Rtd)
  • Chairman: F. Hitchcock
  • Hon. Secretary: T. Lewis
  • Hon. Social Secretary: R. Meredith

COMMANDER E.A. HAMILTON-HILL, PRESIDENT 1947 to 1956

Cmdr. E.A. Hamilton-Hill was President of Overseas for 9 years, 1947 to 1956, after which he was forced to withdraw because he could not give the necessary time to the Club. Even so, the Commander remained a staunch supporter of the Club until he left Malta in 1971, and as Managing Director of Rediffusion(Malta) and Malta Television Services he never failed to broadcast details of the Club's A.G.M. and other big events when requested to do so. He was awarded the O.B.E.

Commander Hamilton-Hill's rugby playing record is impressive. As a flank forward, besides playing for the Royal Navy, he played for Harlequins, 1929 to 1939; Surrey, 1930 to 1938; and for England, 1935/36, vs Ireland, Wales and New Zealand(3caps).

COMMITTEE 1948 to 1952

At the A.G.M., 26th October, 1948, the following known Officials were elected:

  • President: Commander E.A. Hamilton-Hill
  • Chairman: F. Hitchcock
  • Hon. Secretary: T. Lewis
  • Hon. Treasurer: W.M. Wren

Trevor Lewis resigned in February, 1949, prior to leaving Malta, and Fred Burch took over as Secretary. This Committee, first with Trevor, and then with Fred, remained together as a Committee until the end of the 1951/52 season, when all except the President returned to U.K. They proved a very popular and capable Committee, and all members who knew them remember them with affection.

TREVOR LEWIS, FOUNDER MEMBER

Trevor Lewis left Malta in June, 1949. It was mainly due to his love of rugby and desire for a game that started the idea of a Club being formed for all rugby enthusiasts who had no team of their own. Backed by Commodore D. Orr-Ewing, and an equally keen body of sportsmen, first from the Dockyard, the Overseas Rugby Club was formed.

OBJECT OF THE CLUB, 1951

The following notice was inserted in the Times of Malta on the 22nd November, 1951:

OVERSEAS R.F.C.

The object of this Club is to provide Rugger for United Kingdom civilian personnel and members of small units who would not otherwise get a game. Prospective members are cordially invited to contact Mr. Burch, Flat 5, Tigne Street, Sliema.

OVERSEAS ON THE FIELD, 1947 to 1952

For information about the Club I have corresponded with past members whose service to the Club covers the years, 1946 to the present date, and except for a small gap in 1953, their membership overlaps. As this gap seems to occur when changes are becoming apparent in the Club, I will first concern myself with the period, 1947 to 1952.

For this period, following Trevor Lewis and Ray Meredith, for invaluable information, I am indebted to Cdr. E.A. Hamilton-Hill, R.N.(Rtd) (1947–71), Mr G. Holt (1947–51), Lt. Cdr. W.M. Wren, R.N.(Rtd) (1948–52), Mr J. Gray (1948–52), Capt. J. Asbury R.N.(Rtd), and Mr W.M. Polkinghorne (1950–53, 1958–61). Jimmy Gray was the First Officer on the R.F.A. Blue Ranger. One other person I would like to mention is Fred Burch. Fred was contacted via the M.O.D. Worcester, in June, 1975, and a letter was received from him in which he expressed his pleasure in hearing from his old club again. I wrote direct to Fred on the 16th July, 1975, and sad to relate he had passed away on the 10th July. His widow, Vera, herself an Overseas close supporter, sent my letter, requesting information of the early days of the Club, on to Trevor Lewis.

The Club continued through 1947/48 with a fair amount of playing success. Unfortunately, many of the original members, including Ray Meredith, left Malta in the summer of 1948. Over the years, this continuing loss of playing strength, as civilian and service members finished their tour of duty in Malta and returned to the U.K., or other place of duty, was to prove the main factor which affected the Club’s fortunes. However, at that time good players were easier to replace. There is no record of playing results for 1947/48, but some results, noted

in diaries were kept for 1948-51 seasons. These are incomplete. During this early period Overseas could field two reasonably strong teams, both on the same day. There was no shortage of opponents, although then, as now, the only civilian opponents were touring sides. There was a reasonable fleet in Malta, and we played many teams from H.M. ships and Shore Establishments, besides army and R.A.F. Most of our games were played on Sundays. Our standard was good. The highlight of the rugby season was the game against the Mediterranean Fleet. Before proceeding on its Spring cruise to Gibraltar and there playing against the Home Fleet, the Med. Fleet used to play the Overseas XV as a trial match. It was a means of blooding (not literally) the navy team. There is a record of one such match at Tal Qali on the 11th December, 1949, with the score, Overseas 3 - Med. Fleet 8. Overseas used to help the mid- shipmen of the Med. Fleet in the same way.

One person who played occasionally for Overseas between 1949 and 1951 is the present First Sea Lord, Admiral Sir Terence Lewin. Admiral Lewin was a very keen rugby enthusiast, as indeed he still is, and he kindly replied to my enquiry with the following: "I served in HMS Chequers based in Malta from August 1949 until October, 1951. During that time I played for anybody that was running a side and turned out several times for the Overseas, roped in, as far as I can remember, by Bill Wren; this was because my ship was not big enough to run a side of its own. I was, however, at the same time playing for the Flotilla side and also for the Royal Navy."

George Holt writes of the period 1950-51 when Jack Asbury was Team Captain. George has no doubt that under Jack Asbury's leadership the team standard improved. He cites two games in this season when Overseas played against two touring sides, the French Air Force from Tunisia and the Grenadier Guards from Tripoli. The games were watched by the Queen, Princess Margaret and Lord Louis Mountbatten. The French beat Overseas by the odd try and George Holt blames himself for this (one of those memories). The first half was played with the smaller French rugby ball and the second half with larger type that we use. The try was scored when a Frenchman holding the small ball in the palm of his hand waved it in front of George. George was mesmerised by it and tackled the spot where the ball had been, instead of the man.

Information about the Overseas XV in the 1951/52 season comes from a copy of the R.A.F. news sheet called 'Luqa Lens' dated January, 1952. This particular copy was passed on to me by Trev Rickettes, the present President of Overseas, and although it is appertaining to R.A.F. rugby, it is also part of Malta and Overseas rugby, and I quote:-

LUQA LENS

January, 1952

Congratulations to the Station Rugby Team on putting up such a fine showing this season.

Up to date the team has played thirteen matches, won 11 - lost 2, with a total of 228 pts for, and 62 pts against - a very creditable performance indeed.

The teams holding the honours of beating Luqa are H.M.S. Euryalus and Overseas, both by very close margins.

CLUB ACTIVITIES AND CHARACTERS, 1947 to 1952

In those early days we had no Club House and Committee Meetings were held in Official's homes. The meeting place for members, in and out of season, was Charlie's Bar, Tower Road, very near the junction of Tower Road and Tigne Street. Here members who were about to leave Malta were entertained and presented with tankards. I am also told that many a committee Meeting ended there.

Very much part of the Club was the weekly Stag night and these took place at such places as the Strand Palace, Valletta, and Jimmy's Bar, Birzebuggia, when such crazy games as tie biting were played. They also took place at a bar on the water's edge at St. Paul's Bay. The evening started off with a meal and then to the serious business. Another game played was aircraft hangers. One of the highlights of these affairs was one evening when the naval element decided to re enact the shipwreck of St. Paul using a kitchen table top. There was nearly a nasty accident involving one of the local fishing boats, and disaster was only averted when Jack Asbury, like a good Captain, regained order from the near shipwreck. A bus was usually hired to take the members back round the Island to their various places of residence.

The main social functions were the dances held at the Queen's Hall. In those early days they were for U.K. members only and usually evening dress was worn. Each season a fancy dress dance was held during Carnival time which traditionally was just before Lent. George Holt recalls one particular dance which was held at the Phoenicia Hotel, a Rugger Ball, probably at Christmas 1950. On this occasion a set of rugger posts, painted in red and white stripes, was set up before the band and two sets of jerseys were strung across the room. During the evening, Jimmy Gray (well someone had to do it) climbed up the posts and ruined a good suit on the still wet posts. Jack Asbury also recalls a combined Rugger Ball with Overseas and the three Services in 1950/51 at the Phoenicia Hotel which was attended by Prince Phillip and the then Princess. A mini rugby ball was given to each attender. It is possible that these dances were one and the same.

During the summer months buses were hired from Captain's Garage to take members and their families to the beaches. The wives had what was called a 'Cackle Club', meeting in each others homes in turn. In the absence of a Club House all this helped to bind the Club together.

As with all Clubs, Overseas had its characters, and perhaps during this period the most talked about, usually with affection, was Doc. Doyle. As a doctor on board the R.F.A. Fort Duquesne he certainly did not look the part. Modest and unassuming, he dressed in a cloth cap and a raincoat two sizes too large. He carried his first aid kit to matches in a pussers attache case and on one occasion he dashed onto the field, opened his case, and to everyone's delight empty cist bottles fell out. Two other stories are

12

told about Doc Doyle and one of them concerns me. One occasion, early in 1950, whilst playing at Ta' Qali, I was knocked unconscious. The game was being reffed by a Major who was the family doctor at Mtarfa Hospital. Doc, complete with his attache case, rushed onto the field and proceeded to stick a needle in. The Major was aghast, and apparently looked at Doc in horror asking him who he thought he was and what he thought he was doing. Doc reckons he saved my life, bless him. This story has been told to me by three ex members of the day. The other story is that on one occasion Doc decided he was ill, made a chit out for himself, and off he went to Bighi Hospital. Jimmy Gray and one or two other Overseas members visited him and they were told that no such person was in hospital. Eventually he was found in the seaman's ward and duly transferred to a private ward. Doc Doyle would have said he was happier in a seaman's ward.

During these early years there were many good players but I think the two most worthy of note are the English internationals, R. Stirling, and D.T. Wilkins. Wilky was a Fleet Air Arm pilot on board the aircraft carrier H.M.S. Ocean, and Bob Stirling was a Fl. Lt. in the R.A.F. both serving in Malta in approximately 1948. They both played for England, 1951-53, and Bob Stirling played a final year when he Captained England in 1953/54. Men off H.M.S. Ocean gave Overseas a great deal of support both on the field and socially.

Other members well remembered from this period, not necessarily in order of joining the Club, and not previously mentioned are as follows:-
T. Percy, Grimhoff, Anderton, L. Lees, D. Gillard, Riley, K. Nichols, Montgomery, Jock Muir, S. Bucktan, T. Parry, P. Perry, Stewart, L. Bellamy, T. Healey.

1953 - 58

Due more to circumstances than any desire for change on the part of succeeding Overseas Committees, 1952 seemed to be the end of an era for the Club. Perhaps it was partly due to the fact that all of the original Committee, including the Founder Members, had now left Malta. Nevertheless, the aims and objects of the Club remained the same. This was confirmed by the notices in newspapers, and objects of the Club being presented to joining members.

For information about the years, 1953 to 1956, I am indebted to Mike Phillips, Treasurer, 1953-56, and to John Chapman, Secretary, 1954-56. From 1953 to 1956 at least they did function as a Committee, although I am told that things were very informal, not many meetings took place and there is no record of any A.G.M. On the other hand, the only remaining written record of a pre 1958 Committee Meeting, is that of a meeting which took place on the 27th November, 1954. All meetings were still held at the homes of Officials, or at a 'bar just off Sliema Front (Tower Road) opposite the Lotto Office'. This could be Charlie's Bar again.

At the meeting mentioned above it was confirmed that the Club colours were still navy blue and white hoops, with a second set of jerseys, colours red and white hoops. With effect from the date of the meeting, the fee for club Membership was: Playing Members, £1 per annum and 1/- per game. Non Playing Members, 10/- per annum. Present at the meeting were Messrs J. Chapman, Hon. Secretary, R.W.M. Sanderson, Captain, M. Phillips, Hon. Treasurer, and T. Clark, Committee Member.

The main change during this period was the gradual decline in the number of non service members in the Club. One tries not to make a distinction between service and civilian members as ail are part of the Club, but one is forced to at times, and it will be shown that, at least in 1956, team sheets had names of players selected with their units side by side. In 1954 the only civilian members were Mike Phillips and John Chapman. When I joined the Club in November, 1956, I was the only civilian member. Another change which took place was a variation of the name of the Club. With Overseas playing at Ta' Qali, it became a habit of the players to call in at the Melita Hotel, San Anton Gardens, after a game. Both John and Mike mention this fact, also the fact that the Melita Hotel played a great part in the social life of the Club during the period 1954 to 1956. Perhaps this was also true prior to 1954. I know that after 1956 the players still used the Melita Hotel for drinks after a match although, it was not part of the main social life of the Club. When the variation in the name took place it is difficult to say, both informants are vague on this point, but definitely at the start of the 1956/57 season, the Club was known as the Overseas R.F.C. (Melita's). Official circulars were headed 'The Overseas Rugby Football Club (The Melita's)', or, 'Melitas, Overseas Rugby Club, Malta' and often referred to as the 'Melita's'.

Although it was intended to hold an Annual General Meeting at the start of the 1956/57 season, it did not in fact take place as the Suez crisis had set things so far back. The Secretary for 1956/57, Jim Osbourne, did send a letter to players of the previous season, asking them to attend a get

Together at Montgomery House, Floriana, on the 19th October, 1956, in order to form plans with a view to calling an A.G.M. No record remains of this get together, and possibly the Suez crisis forced its cancellation.

Although Overseas was still a civilian Club in name at the beginning of the 1956/57 season, it was virtually a service side and there was no Club life. There was no Club House and no Committee. There was no A.G.M. to appeal to civilians, and information and enrolment forms were distributed through service channels. In fairness to Jim Osbourne, there were no other civilian members to bring into the team, and the objects and functions of the Club, as promulgated to members and units, prove that it was still a Civilian Club and not just a Service team. At the start of the 1957/58 season another civilian, Jim Swain, joined the Club. The following team sheet shows the variation in the name of the Club, make up of the team and units in which players served.

The Overseas Rugby Football Club (The Melita's)

The undermentioned have been selected to represent the Club against the Naval Shore Establishments XV on Sunday, 2nd Dec 56 at Ta Quali kick off 1500hrs. All players are requested to be at the pavilion by 1445hrs. Shirts will be provided by the Secretary but players are requested to provide their own shorts, boots and stockings.

Capt Osbourne RAPC

Lt Templeton RN

Surge/Lt Marks RN (Captain)

Lt Dicketts RM

Mr Morgan Dingli

Cpl Graham REME

Cpl Musto RM

Capt Bobby REME

Personnel unable to play are requested to inform the Secretary by return post or by telephone. It would be appreciated if those willing to play would also confirm to the Secretary. The Secretary can be contacted as under:

Command Pay Office Floriana Telephone Fortress 191 (Between 0800hrs and 1330hrs)

25 Buskett Road, Rabat. Telephone Rabat 147 (out of office hours)

Hon. Sec.

Overseas Rugby Football Club

NOTICE INSERTED IN NEWSPAPER, 1954

The following notice was inserted in the Times of Malta on the 15th October, 1954:-

OVERSEAS R.F.C.

The Overseas Rugby Club in Malta exists mainly for the benefit of U.K. based Service and Civilian members of units, ships, etc. unable to form a XV of their own.

Matches are played weekly, Saturday or Sunday, usually at Ta' Qali.

Anyone interested is invited to contact Mr J.H. Chapman, Tel. No/ Dockyard 7276 for details, as it is hoped to start play in the very near future.

OBJECTS AND MEMBERSHIP, 1956

The following information was given to all members and prospective members at the beginning of the 1956/57 season:-

The object of the Club is to help foster the true 'Rugger' spirit on the island by providing facilities for:-

(a) All Service and Civilian Rugger players who are unable to play for any other Rugger team, i.e. Members of Units unable to field a side.

(b) All Service and Civilian Rugger players, who, although committed to play for a unit during the week, wish to play 'Club' rugger over the weekend.

(c) Non-playing rugger enthusiasts who may support the club and join in its social life.

It is appreciated of course, that in the case of (b) above, the Service units have first call on their players.

The Club colours are (a) navy blue and white hoops (b) red and white hoops.

Membership was divided into three categories:-

(a) Full Member

Annual subscription of 30/- : no match fees, This type of member whose subscriptions were fully paid on leaving the Club received an inscribed tankard as follows:-

1 season's membership    ½ pint tankard

2 or more season's membership 1 pint tankard

(b) Associate Member

No Annual subscription - match fee 1/- per game

(c) Non-playing Member

Annual subscription 10/-

Presenting a tankard seemed a novel way of getting members to pay subscriptions, although it would appear that the attraction was not big enough (or some members did not drink). There is a record of 8 members not paying subs for season 1955/56,

Expenditure on tankards at the end of the 1955/56 season was £10, i.e. 3 pint and 6 half pint tankards. The practice was discontinued after 1957/58 season. In later years, over different periods, tankards have been presented to leaving members, but never tied to membership subscriptions.

The significant point of the above is that the object of the Club is now to provide rugby for all Service and Civilian players, not to 'U.K. based only'.

OVERSEAS ON THE FIELD, 1953-58

Overseas teams played through seasons 1953-58 with a high degree of success. Mike Phillips describes 1953-56 as '3 jolly good seasons' rugbywise, and this can also be said of the 1956-58 seasons. All games, at least during 1954-56 were played on a Sunday. The intention for 1956-58 was to play on Saturdays, with the odd game on Sundays, and if membership allowed, subject to the availability of a ground, to run both a Saturday XV and a Sunday XV. We did not in fact succeed in turning out two XVs, and kept mainly to Saturday games. Complete lists of games and results for 1954/55 and 1955/56, provided by John Chapman, have been included at the back of this history. Fixtures and results for the remainder of this period are either skimpy or not available. John Chapman also provided names of a successful team for 1953/54, also a list of players selected for Overseas teams during the same period, both included in the following pages.

One of the outstanding players and personalities of Overseas during the 1953-56 period was John Mark, the athlete who, whilst at Cambridge carried the Olympic flame into the arena for the London Olympics (1952). A highlight during a game in 1955/56 is described by John Chapman as follows: "Overseas in 1955-56 lost to an R.A.F. (Malta) representative side 14-3. The R.A.F. side wanted a trial match prior to a short tour in French North Africa. Overseas spent about 90% of the match defending their own line. Then, from a kick out John Mark deceived the R.A.F. with his kick direction and sped after it like a whirlwind to score a try." Mike Phillips tells of one occasion when John Mark went over the line with 3 men hanging on to him. Perhaps something most rugby players have seen before, but a feat we always remember. Other remembered stalwarts of this era are 'Doc' Taylor, Mike Aldridge, Tony Clarke, Jock Stewart and John Kirkup.

In 1956/57 the first half of the season was affected by the Suez crisis and little thought was given to rugby. The rugby pitches at the Marsa were covered with tents and equipment not to mention heavy military vehicles, and the pitches were ruined. The only pitch at the Marsa which could be played on was the one nearest and parallel to the Stadium. At least one game was played on this pitch by the 'Forts' whilst tents and equipment still covered the rest of the pitches. For the most part of what remained of this season all games were played at Ta' Qali, whilst the whole of the rugby playing area at the Marsa was being re-surfaced. The first game for Overseas in the 1956/57 season was on the 2nd December against the Forts at Ta' Qali.

I personally remember seasons 1956/57 and 1957/58 with pleasure. During the first season I used to turn up for any

Service game played during the week with my kit, and again during the second season with Overseas Team Captain, Jim Swain, hoping teams would turn up short. We must have played for all teams on the Island, sometimes on opposite sides.

During the same two seasons important changes took place regarding teams on the Island. Both changes, the formation of two new teams, the Naval Shore Establishments (Forts) and the Nomads, affected Overseas very much. They further weakened the Overseas XV at the same time providing much needed extra opposition.

NAVAL SHORE ESTABLISHMENTS (THE FORTS) R.F.C.

The Naval Shore Establishments (The Forts) R.F.C. was formed at the beginning of the 1956/57 season. Previously, all naval players without a service team had been able to play for Overseas, now their allegiance was to the Forts. All persons stationed at or attached to Naval Shore Establishments, W/T Stations etc., excluding H.M.S. Falcon (Hal Far), were automatically Associate Members of the Forts. Either by representing the Forts at rugby or by subscribing the sum of 2/- to Club Funds they became Full Members.

THE NOMADS

At the beginning of the 1957/58 season the small army units based on Malta joined together to form a team called the Nomads, later to be called the Signets. This change did not affect Overseas quite so much as the Forts did in the previous season. The Nomads was only a team whereas the Forts formed a Club. Nevertheless, Overseas Members who played for the Nomads, or the Forts, owed their allegiance first to the Service team.

SOCIAL ACTIVITIES, 1953-58

Between 1953 and 1956 the Melita Hotel played a great part in the social life of the Club. Not only did Overseas players stop at the Melita after a game at Ta' Qali, but at least one successful Club dinner was held there. The only other reported social activity during this period was a combined Overseas/E.R.A. Rugby Ball held at the Phoenicia Hotel. This function was a success with the inevitable rugby posts, made with bamboo and paper, at each end of the ball room, with the respective club colours.

Between 1956 and 1958 there was almost no social activity. First, the Suez crisis made it impossible for the first half of the 1956/57 season, and secondly, perhaps the main reason, was that being by this time virtually a Service team, the Service men had their own organised functions. The Secretary, Jim Osbourne, wrote that he would organise social functions according to demand, and this proved negative. The end of season dinner which was to have been held at the Mocambo Restaurant, St Paul's Bay, on the 2nd March, 1957, was cancelled due to lack of support.

OVERSEAS CLUB BADGE

Both John Chapman and Mike Phillips speak of a Club blazer badge which was designed by Mike and produced for the

Club Members in 1954/55. This was a splendidly worked badge in gold and different coloured wire thread, and made to order by an elderly Maltese lady who was renowned for similar work for Service badges. The motif depicted a rugby ball in the top left corner over 'Seas' in the bottom right corner, with a thick band of blue, bordered each side by a thin white stripe (Overseas colours), going from top right to bottom left. In the middle of the seas was a Maltese Cross in Maltese national colours, one half of the cross red and the other half white.

In 1975/76 this design was used to produce a wooden plaque, a photo of which is shown at the back of this history.

Most Successful Team for Season 1953/54

Full Back               Liddel

Left Wing                 Chapman

Left Centre               Norseworthy

Right Centre           Hall

Right Wing              Blackmore

Fly Half               Sanderson

Scrum Half           Howells

Right Prop           Regan

Hooker                Claset

Left Prop                Phillips

Second Row        Commins
