PLAYERS AT VARIOUS TIMES (1953-56) As given by John Chapman

Robertson, Sanderson, Howells, Clark, Claset, Fogden, Camplin, R. Commins, M. Phillips, Evans, Morrison, Kirkup, Capstick, Allison, Wright, P. Aldrich, T. Young, Thompson, Cardno, M. Bobby, J. Osbourne, Vallings.

At least M. Bobby and J. Osbourne played in 1956-58.

PART II

1958/59

REFORMING OVERSEAS ON A CLUB BASIS

During the close season, on the 20th May, 1958, the Hon. Secretary of the Overseas, Captain Jim Osbourne, left Malta. During the evening of the 20th he called at my house whilst I was at work and left all the worldly possessions of the 'Overseas' in my care. My wife suggested that he should wait until I came home and ask me himself if I wanted to be 'Caretaker Secretary' before he left. Jim blithely told my wife that he was in transit that night and he was off. When I returned home from work I was the Caretaker Secretary, like it or not. The Club assets at that time consisted of £11 in cash, two sets of jerseys, two rugby balls, a battered type- writer, a lacer, pump and some forms. The only Minutes left with me were those of a single meeting held on the 27th November, 1954.

With no Committee to work with, and no Service attachment, I decided immediately to reform Overseas on a Club basis, to the same ideals and outlook as I had known in 1948/50. Perhaps this had been in Jim Osbourne's mind when he left Overseas in my care. Fortunately, such rugby stalwarts as Major G.C.D. Scott Lowe, Jim Swain, the previous year Team Captain, and Jim Stalworthy were around at the right time. The Major, Army R.U. (Malta) Chairmen, readily agreed to be President of the Overseas Club. Circulars re Overseas, with the Major's authority, were put out to Service Units and at the same time contact was made with Civilian firms such as Wimpeys. At that time the main Wimpey construction unit was at Has Saptan.

It is a peculiarity of rugby in Malta, that even as Servicemen like to join the Overseas, the only civilian club on the island, the very existence of a civilian club depends so much on the help of the Services and also on Servicemen joining the Club. For instance, all rugby pitches were on Service property. We in the Overseas have been thankful of the good relations which have always existed.

The first meeting of the 1958/59 season was held at 77, Grenfell Street, St. Julians, on the 6th September, 1958. The three members present were Messrs. N.C. Morgan, Secretary, N.J. Swain, Fixture Secretary, and J. Stalworthy, Committee Member. Jim Stalworthy turned down the Office of Treasurer, but agreed to act as Chairman. At this meeting it was agreed to drop the issue of inscribed tankards to those leaving the Club and so enabling subscriptions to be lowered. The second meeting was held on the 11th October, same address, when we were joined by Bill Polkinghorne, another rugby stalwart. Bill agreed to act as Treasurer. At the second meeting it was decided, that although it was only by nominating ourselves as Officials of the Club could it be restarted on a 'Club Basis', we must legalize ourselves in positions held, by being elected at a General Meeting, or others elected to take over. It was therefore decided to call an Annual General Meeting at the first available date.

ANNUAL GENERAL MEETING

Annual General Meeting held on the 20th October, 1958, at the Queen's Hall, Old College Street, Sliema. Notice of this meeting was given in the 'Times of Malta' on the 15th October, also it was broadcast on 'A' programme of rediffusion in "What's On".

TIMES OF MALTA, WEDNESDAY OCTOBER 15, 1958

OVERSEAS RUGBY UNION

FOOTBALL CLUB

N.C. Morgan, Hon. Secretary, Overseas Rugby Football Club, notifies:

The Overseas Rugby Union Football Club will be holding its Annual General Meeting at the Queen's Hall, Old College Street, Sliema, at 7 p.m. on Monday, October, 20.

All past, present and prospective members are cordially invited, together with anyone interested in club rugby.

Membership is open to U.K. based civilian and Service personnel.

At this A.G.M., the President, Major G.C.D. Scott Lowe, explained that the main reason for the A.G.M. was to put facts before Members and to call for volunteers for all offices. The following Officials, including the 'Resident' Committee, were elected:-

  • President Major G.C.D. Scott Lowe, T.D.
  • Hon. Secretary Mr. N.C. Morgan
  • Hon. Treasurer Mr. H.W. Polkinghorne
  • Hon. Social Secretary Mr. J.E.M. George
  • Team Captain and Hon. Fixture Secretary Mr N.J. Swain
  • Team Trainer Mr. E.H. Stacey (Ex Wasps player)
  • Social Committee
    • Mr. J.E.M. George (Secretary)
    • Mrs M. Rushworth
    • Mr. V.A. Palmer
    • Mrs. M. Polkinghorne

A proposed set of club Rules had been attached to the Agenda of the A.G.M. for members to peruse. These rules were adopted without alteration and have acted as the Club Constitution over the years, only being altered, as expedient, by the required two-thirds majority at an A.G.M.

FIRST RULES FOR OVERSEAS CLUB

  1. That the name of the Club be: - "THE OVERSEAS RUGBY UNION FOOTBALL CLUB, MALTA".
  2. That the object of the Club is to help foster the true "Rugger" spirit on the island by providing facilities for:
    1. All Service and Civilian rugger players who are unable to play for any other rugger team, i.e. members of units unable to field a side.
    2. All Service and Civilian rugger players who,

21

although committed to play for a unit side
during the week, wish to play Club Rugger
over the weekend.

  • (c) Non-Playing Rugger enthusiasts who may
    support the Club and join in its social life.

It is understood, in the case of (b) above, that
Service Units have first call on their players.

  1. That the Club colours be navy blue and white hoops.
  2. That the Officers of the Club shall consist of The
    President, Chairman, Hon. Secretary, Hon. Treasurer, Hon.
    Fixture Secretary, Hon. Team Secretary, Team Captains. These
    Officers to hold office for one year and be elected by members
    at an Annual General Meeting.
  3. That the management of the Club shall be entrusted to
    a General Committee consisting of such Officers as shall be
    elected at the Annual General Meeting. Liaison with the
    representatives of the three Services shall be effected.
  4. That the General Committee shall have the power to
    administer the funds and property in execution of the Club's
    aims. No expenditure or debts shall be contracted other than
    by resolution and majority vote.
  5. That the General Committee shall have the powers to
    fill any vacancies which may arise in their number during the
    course of the year, and have full power to co-opt as may be
    found expedient.
  6. That the General Committee shall have the power to
    delegate any of its duties to such other Committees as may
    be necessary.
  7. A quorum for a General Committee shall be two thirds
    of the Committee.
  8. Annual General Meeting to be held in October. Items
    to be included are Statement of Accounts, Report of the
    Committee and election of Officers for the ensuing year.
  9. Members to be given 14 days notice of General Meetings.
    Items for inclusion on the Agenda to reach the Hon. Secretary
    7 days prior to the meeting. Extraordinary General Meetings
    may be called by ten or more members or by a majority vote
    of the General Committee.
  10. That the sanction of two thirds of the members present
    and voting at the Annual or Extra-Ordinary General Meeting is
    required for the passing of any resolution to alter the rules.
    Any other resolution shall be passed by a simple majority.
  11. Membership
    • (a) Full Members: Annual Subscription 10/-
      and match fee of 1/-
    • (b) Non-Playing Member and Associate Member:
      Annual subscription 5/-
    • (c) Temporary Membership 1/- per match.
    Members referred to in paragraphs (a) and (b) above
    have full privileges.
22

14 That a copy of those rules be affixed in the Membership Card of the Club or otherwise forwarded to each member.

PLAYING SEASON

The President was a tower of strength for Overseas behind the scenes and was an active supporter on the touch-line. He did not manage to get to any ordinary Committee Meetings (these were usually Chaired by Bill Polkinghorne), at least during the 1958/59 season, although initially the 'Resident' Committee met him in his office in South Street, Valletta, on two occasions. The Major was in charge of army rugby and through him we were allowed to use a pitch at Ta' Qali once a fortnight as our 'home ground', and many facilities were put at the disposal of Overseas.

For the 1958/59 season the grounds at Ta' Qali came under a Joint Services Committee and they refused to let teams play on the pitches until the rains softened and protected them. At this time there were 6 pitches at Ta' Qali, two of them being kept for special matches. At the beginning of the season the pitches at the Marsa had just been relaid and were not in use. We had been granted permission by the R.A.F. authorities to use one of the huts at Ta' Qali for changing in and to make use of the washing facilities on the camp. Our first 'run around' of the season was on the 1st November on the football pitch at St. Andrews, next to St. Andrews Children’s School. Our first game, a trial match, was on the 8th November, versus H.M.S. Falcon at Hal Far, and our last game of the season was at Ta' Qali on the 8th March, 1959, versus the Forts. The playing season of 1958/59 was typical for Malta. A short rainy season could curtail the playing season drastically, sometimes by March the grounds were dry and cracking. It was dangerous for players and the grass so lightly embedded that it could be scurfed off. On the other hand, on the odd occasion, with an extended rainy season and the help of watering the pitches, touring sides have been played in early May. Initially all Overseas first team games were played on Saturdays as it was believed most Service opposition was available on that day. By the end of the season it was agreed that opposition could always be found on a Sunday and at the same time, fewer, if any Overseas members were committed to play for their units.

Good co-operation existed between the Overseas and the Forts. The Overseas agreed not to circulate propaganda to Navy units, although we were free to approach the Marines. The Dockyard was open to either. Fortunately, the Fleet Auxiliaries were left to the Overseas and at this time there was a considerable fleet constantly in and out of Malta. Mr G. Chere, Assistant S.N.S.O., in charge of Fleet Auxiliaries, took blocks of Club and enrolment forms to give to the Captains of the following ships when in port:- Tide Flow, Tide Surge, Retainer, Wave Prince, Brown Ranger, Blue Ranger, Fort Duquesne and Eddy Cliffe. The Tides and Waves had approximately 100 U.K. personnel on board. Good co-operation also existed between the Overseas and the Nomads (Sienets), Secretary Tom Baron, but here there was no problem re division of membership. 'Nomads' was the name of a team only, no Club

23

was formed. A point to note was that as from the 22nd December, 1958, HQ3 Commando could not field a team, and 7 of their players joined Overseas. From this date up to the end of the season we could field a Saturday and a Sunday Team.

On the 5th January, 1959, two representatives of the Forts, Jack Gibbons, Secretary, and Hugh Kay, Treasurer, proposed that the two Clubs, Overseas and Forts, should be merged as one socially, using Fort's Club House in Argotti Street, Floriana, registering as perhaps the Malta Rugby Club, whilst keeping the playing sides entirely separate. The idea being to improve both Clubs socially and financially. At an Overseas Committee Meeting held on the 15th January, 1959, this proposal was discussed from both the short and long term views. It was unanimously agreed to remain as a separate unit socially as well as a team and to continue to use our own Club.

Through the good offices of Major Scott Lowe 3members of the Overseas, Messrs Polkinghorne, Morgan and Swain, attended a Combined Services Rugby Football Referee's Course which took place between the 5 - 7 November, 1958, at 69 AEC, Beacon House, St. Andrews. The course was entirely theoretical and no practical refereeing was undertaken. Inclemental weather at the time of the course stopped the practical part. After the theory exam, held on the 7th November, at Beacon House, we were able to referee Service games on the island.

In the words of the Team Captain, Mr N.J. Swain, 1958/59 was an enjoyable season for the Overseas. Jim Swain was a great Club man and Team Captain. What he did not know about the blind side of the referee was not worth knowing. Leading scorers were Brian Hodgins with 73 points, including 15 tries, and Geoff Rushworth with 55 points, including 13 tries. A point worth noting is that both men were wing threequarters. The season was very short due to dry grounds.

PLAYING RECORD FOR 1958/59

P 15    W 6    L 8    D 1    Points for 236    Against 170

CLUB HOUSE - GERRY'S BAR

From the beginning of the 1958/59 season a look out had been kept for likely premises for a Club House. On the 28th September, 1958, the Treasurer of the Forts, Sub. Lt. Hugh Kay, informed Overseas that there was a room vacant adjoining and belonging to Gerry's Bar, at the corner of Manoel Street and Gzira Road, Gzira (Behind Marshall Court). The room had originally been a small café and was fitted out with a small bar. It had a main entrance into Manoel Street and a connecting door into the main bar. A preliminary meeting to discuss details took place on the 20th October, 1958, between Gerry, the Proprietor, and Messrs N.C. Morgan, H.W. Polkinghorne, General Committee, and Mr & Mrs G. Rushworth, Social Committee. A Committee Meeting was held at Gerry's Bar on the 24th November 1958, to discuss the matter in Committee and enable the full Committee to look at the premises. It was decided to hire the room as a ClubHouse on a temporary basis as from the 1st December, 1958. The Club House was small, but a start. We did not register as a Club, Gerry's Bar was already licensed.

24

for liquor and we were using his premises, also buying our stock from him at little over cost price. Bill Polkinghorne was elected Bar Manager with Club and Bar Accounts to be kept separate. Rent of the room was £10 per month. It was decided to open the Club House on Monday, Saturday and Sunday evenings at 7.30 p.m. and on any day after an Overseas match at 5.30 p.m. The Sunday evening opening was soon dropped.

The Club House was closed for the close season as from the 2nd March, 1959, when a final get together was held. All stock was sold at a very much reduced price on this night, a good time was had by all. One or two privates were calling their Commanding Officer by Christian name, and one Captain I know drove three soldiers home like long lost buddies. I do not know what happened next day.

The Club House at Gerry's Bar was a partial success. It was too far away from the grounds for many players to make use of it after a game and it could have been used more when open of an evening (the old cry). From the income point of view the rent was too high and there was little or no profit from the bar during the first season. However, the Committee agreed that a Club House was essential, and that it had contributed a part in reforming and keeping the Club together. The Bar Manager, Bill Polkinghorne, and the Committee, men and ladies, had worked hard, putting in many hours in an attempt to make the Club House popular.

At a pre season meeting held on the 6th October, 1959, the Committee were of the opinion that Gerry's Bar was suitable for a Club House. Unfortunately, continued poor usage of the Club House by members throughout the 1959/60 season suggested otherwise. In spite of lack of bar business the Club House managed a profit of £3.14s, thanks to the Bar Manager, Geoff Rushworth, and the Bar Committee, Messrs T. Goswell, V. Morris and A. Pagan.

AFFILIATION TO THE RUGBY FOOTBALL UNION

On the 16th January, 1959, the first approach to the Rugby Football Union was made requesting affiliation. Mr. F.D. Prentice, then Secretary of the R.F.U., replied to our letter on the 30th January, 1959. Mr Prentice commented on the fact that we were the only Civilian Club in Malta and presumed, correctly (except for touring sides), that our matches were against Service teams. He suggested that when there were one or two Clubs in Malta playing Rugby Union Football, the Union of these Clubs should be called the "Malta Rugby Union" and then it would be possible for his Committee to consider affiliation.

Unless no record has been kept of any other attempt, the next approach to the R.F.U. for affiliation was on the 28th December, 1961, by the Overseas Secretary, Mr. C.V. Morris. No copy has been kept of this letter. In his reply of the 13th December, 1961, Mr Prentice thanked Mr. Morris for his letter and the Fixture Card which he had enclosed. Mr. Prentice regretted that there was little likelihood of there being another Rugby Club in Malta but nevertheless enclosed a nomination form for Membership to the Rugby Football Union. Mr. Prentice ended his letter by saying that our application would then be placed before the Committee of the R.F.U. at a later date for election to membership for season 1962/63. Mr. Prentice's letter of the

13th December was read out at Overseas Committee Meeting of the 21st December, when Mr. Morris said he would forward application to the R.F.U. after first obtaining the signatures of the Secretaries of the Navy and Army Rugby Unions. The request for signatures of the Secretaries of the two Unions was not in Mr. Prentice's letter of the 13th December. Possibly it had been on the application form.

No more was heard of the matter until the Overseas Annual General Meeting held on the 15th October, 1964, when members expressed the view that the Hon. Secretary should write to the R.F.U. regarding membership. Mr. Morris wrote again on the 17th October, 1964. No copy of this letter was kept. On the 28th October, 1964, Mr. R.E. Prescott, Secretary of the RFU replied:--

"At the Full Committee Meeting of the Rugby Football Union held last Friday, it was agreed to support the recommendation of the Overseas Liaison Sub-Committee that the Overseas Rugby Union Football Club, Malta, be accepted into membership with the Rugby Football Union.

Under separate cover we will be sending you all the necessary information, etc.."

Following this letter there was complete silence from the R.F.U. Mr. Morris wrote to the R.F.U. on the 8th December, 1964, and on the 21st September, 1965, asking for the 'necessary information' and asking for official notification of Club's Membership to the R.F.U. Finally, on the 29th September, 1965 Mr. Prescott wrote apologizing for the fact that notification of Membership had apparently not been sent and enclosing a letter to the effect that the Overseas was accepted into Membership with the R.F.U. as from the 1st September, 1965.

CLUB BANK ACCOUNT

The first Club Bank Account was opened with Barclays Bank, Prince of Wales Road, Sliema, immediately after Committee Meeting on the 23rd March, 1959. Signatures required for withdrawals to be those of the Hon. Treasurer and the Hon. Social Secretary. Various bank changes are given under 'Overseas Funds, 1974/75'.

CLUB TELEPHONE

A telephone was installed at the home of the Club Secretary on the 12th March, 1959, under the name 'Overseas Rugby Union Football Club' (Sliema 2892), seven months after requesting it from the G.P.O. Valletta. The original idea was that each retiring Secretary would have the phone transferred to the succeeding Secretary or whoever was acting as Team Secretary. When the phone was first installed the Hon. Secretary was acting in both capacities. Transferring the phone proved impracticable either because of technical reasons or the fact that an incoming Secretary already had his own phone. On two occasions when the Club phone could not be transferred to the new Secretary, the Club phone was transferred to another member of the Committee. On both occasions that particular number lapsed as far as the Club was concerned. It became the practice,

When an incoming Secretary had his own phone, to have it transferred to the Club's name. Finally, the identity of a Club telephone was 'lost' at the time of the British Forces withdrawal in January, 1972.

SOCIAL EVENTS

Two dances were held during the 1958/59 season at the Queen's Hall, Old College Street, Sliema, with the main object to improve the Club's financial position. A great deal of hard work was put in by John George, Social Secretary, and his Committee, Mr & Mrs G. Rushworth, Mrs M. Polkinghorne, initially Mr. V. Palmer, and members of the General Committee. The first on the 6th December, 1958, and the second on the 7th February, 1959, with profits of £20 and £17 respectively. Not a great deal of profit for the amount of work and Committee hours spent planning, but it kept the Club solvent.

MEMBERSHIP

The total Membership of the Club for 1958/59 season was 56 including 4 Lady Members. The Membership was made up of 21 Full Members, 16 Non Players and 19 Temporary Members. Temporary Members, i.e., players paying 1/- per match, had previously been known as Associate Members. The change was made to stress the fact that Temporary Members could not expect the same privileges as Full Members. The ladies played a vital part in re-building the Club.

I was due to leave Malta in July, 1959, and Mr N.J. Swain took over as Caretaker Hon. Secretary on the 27th April, 1959.

1959/60

Annual General Meeting, Queen's Hall, Old College Street, Sliema, 26th October, 1959.

The Following Officials were elected:

  • President: Major G.C.D. Scott Lowe, T.D.
  • Hon. Secretary and Mr. N.J. Swain
  • Hon. Team Secretary: Mr. H.W. Polkinghorne
  • Hon. Treasurer: Mr. C.V. Morris
  • Hon. Fixture Secretary: Mrs. M. Rushworth
  • Hon. Social Secretary: Mr. G. Rushworth
  • Club House/Bar Manager: Mrs M. Rushworth(Secretary)
  • Team Captain Mr. N.J. Swain
  • Social Committee: Mrs. M. Rushworth(Secretary) and Messrs. D. Milton, C. Easter and D. Isted.
  • Bar Committee: Messrs G. Rushworth (Manager), T. Goswell, V. Morris and A. Pagen

The meeting was presided over by the President and Chaired by Mr. Polkinghorne. A point of interest is the election of a woman to the Office of Social Secretary. This was the first and only time that a woman was elected at the A.G.M. as an Officer of the Club. Later in the Club's history it would have taken a brave man to even propose that a member of the fairer sex be elected.

When Mr. Polkinghorne, Treasurer, gave his statement of accounts for the 1958/59 season it showed a credit balance of £40.10s. A definite improvement on the £11 we started the season with. A great deal of hard work but plenty of fun.

The President, Major G.C.D. Scott Lowe, left Malta in February, 1960.

A Cocktail Party was given in his honour at the residence of Mr. & Mrs. N.J. Swain on the 15th February, 1960. The President was toasted 'Godspeed' and presented with an illuminated vote of thanks, made artistically on vellum by a Tal Handaq artist. The Major was a very kind and human person and Overseas have a great deal to thank him for.

During this season, Viv Morris, Hon. Fixture Secretary, who was a teacher at the R.N. School Tal Handaq, interested the staffs of the Service Schools and the senior pupils at Tal Handaq in the Overseas Club. This was the start of very close ties between the Club and the teachers and pupils. Progressively, as the number of Civilian players on the island declined, the Club became more dependent on support from the schools. In April, 1969, Tal Handaq changed its name to the Services Secondary Comprehensive School and became known as S.C.S. Tal Handaq. In November, 1959, the yearly subscription for schoolboys was set at 2/6d with a match fee of 1/-.

The Hon. Secretary, Mr N.J. Swain, left Malta in May, 1960 and on the 25th April, 1960, Mr. C.V. Morris took over as Caretaker Secretary. Besides being Hon. Secretary and Team Secretary for the season 1959/60, Jim Swain had been Team Captain for 3 seasons 1957-60, and Fixture Secretary for the 1958/59 season. Quite a character on and off the field. Jim played a great part in reforming Overseas at the beginning of the 1958/59 season.

28

Playing Season

Permission was given by the R.A.F. for Overseas to use the grounds and changing facilities at Ta' Qali for the 1959/60 season. The season started with a trial at Hal Far on the 28th October. The first game took place at Ta' Qali on the 21st November against the Nomads with Overseas the victors by 6 points to 3 and the final game was on the 5th March when Overseas drew 6-6 with H.M.S. Ark Royal.

From the playing point of view the season was not a success. At a meeting on the 14th December, 1959, the Committee stated how perturbed they were at the continuing losses on the field. In the words of the Hon. Secretary, the Club had taken a pounding on the field of play and it was especially disappointing as the objects of the Club had been adhered to more so than previously. The dearth of playing members was mentioned. It was decided to play all games on a Sunday. This meant that members who were in the Services could play for Overseas regularly and so we could put out a stronger side. Most Service games have always been during the week or on a Saturday. The leading scorer for the season was Geoff Rushworth and this with only 15 points, i.e., 4 tries and one penalty. As a winger of some repute Geoff must rarely have seen the ball except in defence.

The opponents of the 1959/60 season were as follows:--

  • 35 Squadron (R.A.F.), Nomads, Hawks (Small units R.A.F.) H.M.S. Ausonia (Depot Ship), H.M.S. Forth (Depot Ship), H.M.S. Falcon (Hal Far), Forts, Royal Fusiliers, 22l Squadron (R.A.F.),
  • 45 Cdo R.M., H.M.S. Daring and H.M.S. Ark Royal. The main point is that at least eight of these teams were resident in Malta at that time and our fixture list has always been based on this. Possibly also one or both of the above mentioned R.A.F. squadrons were based in Malta at the time. Most certainly it was not as impressive a list as at 1946/47, when the Club first started, but the number became less as the years passed and more British Servicemen were withdrawn.

Playing Record for 1959/60

Pld 16 - W 2 - L 11 - D 3     Points for 60     Against 282

Social Events

Two dances were held during the 1959/60 season at the Phoenicia Hotel. Once again a great deal of hard work by the Social Secretary, Mrs. M. Rushworth, and the Social Committee, Messrs D. Milton, C. Easter and D. Isted. Bad attendance and profit tax cut down profit on the two dances to £5. At this stage in the Club's life one must realize that dances were run, not only for the social side, but also to help to keep the Club solvent. Later in its history the Club could afford to subsidise a dance if necessary. At the end of the season the credit balance of the Club stood at £45.16s

Two very hard working and valuable members of the Club, Geoff Rushworth, Club House Manager, and Margaret Rushworth, Social Secretary, left Malta during the summer of 1960. Both had given a great deal of time and effort into organising social events during the 1959/60 season, and Margaret had served on the Social Committee during the 1958/59 season.

During the meeting the Hon. Secretary, Mr C. Vivian Morris, paid tribute to Major Scott Lowe who had been President of the Club for two seasons. He expressed the wish of all Members that Major Scott Lowe would be speedily returned to good health in his retirement.

In November, 1960, in appreciation of his services to 'The Overseas' Cmdr. E. Hamilton-Hill(retired) was made an Hon. Member of the Club for the 1960/61 season. Commander Hamilton-Hill had been President of the Club for 9 years, 1947 to 1956. In a letter to Mr. C.V.Morris, Cmdr. Hamilton-Hill commented on the number of years he had been associated with the Club. Indeed, over the years, as Managing Director of Rediffusion (Malta) Limited, he never failed to comply with a request by the Club to broadcast information, especially reference the A.G.M., over the rediffusion network.

CLUB HOUSE - MARSA LODGE

At the end of the 1959/60 season, although the Club House at Gerry's Bar just managed to pay for itself, in spite of the high rent, the search for a new home began. In the close season of 1960 arrangements were being made to have premises at Rocky Vale, Spinola, St. Julians, as a Club House. Fortunately,as it turned out, these arrangements fell through. At the A.G.M. on the 10th October, 1960, the President, Lt. Col. T.G. Chambers, promised he would enquire into the possibility of having army premises. Immediately, Capt. John Day, Secretary Army Rugby Union (Malta) and Captain of the Nomads R.F.C., became actively engaged in looking for a suitable Club House for the Nomads/Overseas. On the 18th October, 1960, Lt. Col. Chambers wrote to the Overseas Hon. Secretary, Vivian Morris, informing him that Capt. Day had received permission to use a club room at Marsa (Marsa Lodge).

At an Overseas Committee Meeting on the 27th October, 1960, John Day outlined the facilities which were available at Marsa Lodge and said he would arrange for furnishings and bar fittings to be installed. He pointed out that the Nomads would probably have some difficulty in running the Club themselves and thought that the General Management of the Club

and Bar could be better organized by the Overseas in view of their Social and Bar Committee organization. Needless to say, the Overseas Committee accepted the kind offer. At the same meeting it was decided that the running of the Bar should be undertaken by a joint Bar Committee of Overseas and Nomads. Messrs. B. Headland (Nomads) and S. Ward (R. Sigs) were elected as Associate Members of the Club House Committee to supervise Club Bar, particularly for mid week games. It was agreed that all money from Bar sales should be handed to the Hon. Treasurer and put into the Overseas account in Barclays. The first Bar Manager was Mr. T. Goswell.

The Marsa Lodge was to be 'home' for Overseas for 11½ years, in fact until the British Forces withdrawal in January 1972. The formal opening of the Club House was on the 3rd December, 1960, when H.M.S. Ausonia beat Overseas 17 - 0 in a practice game. The situation was ideal - a Club House within the playing area. As Vivian Morris printed in a rugby news letter dated the 6th March, 1961, the Club House quickly became the rugger centre on the island. The Club House consisted of a large Bar room and an equally large second room normally closed off from the Bar room by a sliding partition. This second room was used on occasions for dances and many other types of functions. On two sides of the building were changing rooms and showers which Overseas teams could use on request. It was decided that the Club House would be opened on a Saturday or Sunday afternoon after an Overseas game at the Marsa, and on request by one of the Service teams during the week, normally on a Wednesday. During the first season the normal Club Night was on a Wednesday evening when many functions were arranged to make it popular and going concern. From the second season onwards the normal Club Night was on a Thursday evening. The Nomads also held functions separately or in conjunction with the Overseas.

The Maltese caretaker, 'George', was an army pensioner who lived in a small cottage behind the Club House. The Overseas 'inherited' George with the Club buildings and he soon became part of the Overseas. It was a little difficult to communicate because of language problems but we managed. The Overseas Committee paid him £1 a week to clean the Club rooms. In January, 1965, this was raised to £2 a week. After a game George was always there clearing glasses away from which he earned the princely sum of 2/6d. George was 'retired' by the army in October, 1967, and consequently he was forced to vacate his cottage and so he had to leave us.

On the 16th December, 1960, Tony Goswell resigned as Bar Manager. As a Flying Officer in the R.A.F. his duties often took him away from Malta. Mr. D. Isted became the New Bar Manager.

Novel methods were used to decorate the Club rooms. On the 3rd February, 1961, Capt. J.C. Griffiths, R.A.O.C., on behalf of the Club, wrote to approximately 36 well known rugby clubs in U.K., including Twickenham and Murrayfield, asking for any old rugby posters advertising matches to decorate the club room walls and give them a rugby flavour. I do not know what success he had. John Griffiths was co-opted onto the Bar Committee on the 1st February, 1961. At a Club dance held at the Marsa Lodge on the 28th January, 1961, the walls were gaily decorated with rugger jerseys of various teams on the island.

On the 11th January, 1961, the Bar Manager opened a separate Bar account at Barclays. However, at the end of June, 1961, the Bar and General accounts at Barclays were made into one. For the first season the Bar net profits were shared with the Nomads R.F.C. and for this purpose the Bar account was audited up to the 23rd March, 1961. The net profit to each Club was £19.

On the 15th June, 1961, the Overseas Committee decided that in future the Bar profits would be shared between Overseas and the Joint Services Rugby Sports Fund. The period during which the profits would be shared ran from the 1st October to the 31st March, i.e. the playing season. The Overseas Club would make the Club room available during this period for any Social/Playing functions. Capt. J. Day, army representative on the Overseas General Committee, was the prime mover of this decision and so it must have been the wish of the army authorities that profits be shared in this way.

On the 24th September, 1961, Lt. Col. T.G. Chambers, as Chairman Army Rugby (Malta), wrote to Mr. C.V. Morris, Hon. Secretary Overseas, setting out the conditions required for Overseas to continue to use Marsa Lodge. This communication was referred to as Sigs/426. Lt. Col. Chambers asked that the following condition be recorded in the minutes of the next Overseas A.G.M.

"A formal request must be made annually on behalf of the Overseas Rugby Club (Malta) for the continued use of the Marsa Club House by the Overseas Rugby Club. The Chairman Army Rugby (Malta) will in turn approach the General Officer Commanding and will communicate to the Overseas Rugby Club the General Officer Commanding's decision. The request should be made in September of each year and will cover the period 1st October to 30th September following receipt of the request."

"The first request will be due in September, 1962."

Sigs/426 remained in force until the 3rd November, 1967, when the Overseas were allowed to use Marsa Lodge as an 'Encroachment'. More of that later.

In consequence of the different method of sharing profits the representatives of the three Services were asked to sit on the Overseas Bar Management Committee in lieu of the Nomad R.F.C. representatives. These Service representatives were elected at the A.G.M. They were given authority by the Overseas full Committee to open the Club House on occasions when an elected member of the Bar Committee was not present for Service games.

Each year, as soon as possible after the 31st March, an Extra-ordinary General Meeting was held to present the Bar account for the 6 months ending the 31st March. The Bar and General Accounts were audited for the year on the 30th September. On the occasion of the Bar account for the 6 months ending the 31st March being presented, a cheque for the Joint Services Sports Board's share of the net Bar profits was handed to the Secretary Army R.U. (Malta). The Secretary Army R.U. in turn shared this amount between the three Services.

via the Joint Service Sports Board. After a difference of opinion between the Overseas Club and the Secretary of the J.S.S.B. in May, 1963, this method of payment of the Services' share of the profits was changed. The difference of opinion was due to the fact that the Secretary Army R.U. (Malta) had approached the Overseas Hon. Secretary before the end of the 1962/63 playing season and asked for an advance of approximately £40 to assist with the expenses incurred by the army rugby team which visited Tripoli early 1963. The Secretary J.S.S.B. objected on the grounds that Inter Service Sports Board had not been approached for, nor approved, this expenditure. All ended well, but from the 31st March, 1964 each Service representative was presented with an individual cheque for a third of the J.S.S.B.'s share of the profits.

From 1961/62 to 1966/67 Overseas and the J.S.S.B. each enjoyed net Bar profits as follows:-

1962£104. 7s. 9d
1963£122. 18s. 8d
1964£46. 10s. 0d
1965£118. 14s. 0d
1966£75. 17s. 10d
1967£111. 5s. 0d

The drop in profit for 1964 was due to a number of reasons including an increase in Bar Stewards wages, small profit margin and less consumption (impossible). The last two mentioned reasons were remedied.

During the 1961/62 season we obtained the services of Mr. Victor Dimech as a paid Bar Steward. Victor served the Club for 4 years before he left Malta on the 4th October, 1965 to live in U.K. He was succeeded as Bar Steward by Mr Angelo Galea who served the Club until it finally closed. In 1964 it is recorded that the Steward's wage was 3/- an hour and overtime as 4/- an hour. It is also recorded that the hours of opening were as follows:- Thursday, 7.30p.m. (Steward 7pm) – 12 midnight. If a Committee Member was present, and the Members present wished, The Club House could remain open until 1.30a.m. After midnight the Members present had to pay a levy of not less than a total of 6/- to pay the Steward. Wednesday. When requested by a Service team, 3p.m. to 7p.m. Saturday, 2.30p.m.(Steward 1.30p.m.) to 7p.m. Sunday, 4.30p.m. to 6.30p.m. Need I say that the Club rarely closed before 1.30a.m. on a Friday morning. One of the most hilarious games played on a Thursday night was liar dice. How the intellectuals at this game managed to plan and catch an unwary member two and a half times round the table I do not know. I also do not know how some of the schoolmasters taught the next morning - I believe they had some understanding pupils.

In 1964 it was estimated that something in the order of twenty fifteen made use of the Club House each week during the playing season. By this time the original furniture was worn out and sadly in need of replacement. In December, 1964, we purchased surplus furniture from the S.N.S.O., Naval Stores, Malta.

With the Club House and Bar being open three or four times a week during the playing season and with all labour being voluntary, except for the Bar Steward, it is obvious that there were problems in safeguarding the bar takings, especially during the busy periods on Wednesday and Saturday afternoons.

Whilst Victor Dimech was the Bar Steward he accepted responsibility. When Angelo Galea became Steward, however, he was not willing to accept responsibility for the takings in the same way, and a new system had to be devised by Ralph McGillivray, Bar Manager (1964/66), and Peter Bennie, Treasurer (1965/67). Individual volunteer members of the Bar Committee agreed to accept responsibility for a complete week at a time, to look after the cash and to pay the week's bar takings into any Branch of the National Bank of Malta to the account of Overseas R.F.C. A special sheet of 'Responsibilities' and 'Bar Takings Statement' forms were devised for the Duty Bar Member, copies of which follow. It was agreed that this system was not foolproof, especially during busy periods, but if stocktakings were carried out thoroughly it was easier for checks to be made, and the systematic weekly entries and banking made life easier for the Treasurer.

In September, 1967, came the first major change in conditions required for the Overseas to continue to use the Marsa Lodge as a Club House and this completely cancelled Sigs/426 which had been in force since September, 1961. Our annual request for permission to continue using Marsa Lodge, dated 22nd September, 1967, was sent as usual to the Secretary Army Rugby Football (Malta). Our letter was passed on to HQ 'Q' Branch and on the 3rd November, 1967, we received the following reply from Mr. J.H.H. Parker of this branch.

"Authority is hereby given for you to hold the Club Room at Marsa Lodge as an Encroachment. This will mean that in accordance with current Ministry of Defence instructions, you will have to pay a 'peppercorn' rent and take out an Insurance Policy to cover loss or damage to the building and third party indemnity."

On the 11th January, 1968, the D.L.A. informed us that we must insure the building for £5,000. On the 28th January, 1968, Mr. Parker (Col. retired) informed Overseas that the Malta Government wished to use the large (2nd) room for coaching athletics between the 1st June and the 31st August, 1968, as a Pilot scheme for the Council of Europe. If we objected we could only have the encroachment for the 'Bar Room'. The Maltese Government would also take out an Insurance.

Naturally, we agreed to the conditions required for us to hold the Club Rooms as an encroachment, taking out the necessary insurance. The Bar Manager, Mr. B. Jackson, received the encroachment (Licence) in March, 1968. Initially, we agreed in Committee to continue to share the playing season bar profits with the three Services, but this decision was rescinded at an Extra-ordinary Meeting, attended by the three Inter Service Representatives; on the 23rd May, 1968. It was then agreed to cease payment of 50% of the playing season bar profit to the Services. Accordingly, at the A.G.M. on the 12th September, 1968, Rule 9 was amended to leave out reference to the Services and also to the Extra-ordinary Meeting which had previously been held in April for submission of the playing season bar account to members and Joint Service Rugby Representatives.

Under the terms of the encroachment we could not let the Forces Driving Club of Malta (or similar clubs) use the Club

House for a function organized by them. They had to apply direct to the D.L.A. Previously we had allowed the Driving Club to use the Club House on certain occasions.

During the summer months of 1961 (April to October) the Club House was kept open on Thursday evenings. Functions were arranged fortnightly although it is not recorded how successful they were. From 1962 to 1964 inclusive the Club House was closed during the summer months for varying periods and even when open there was a loss on the Bar. In 1965 a summer Committee was formed with Mr. P. Ratcliffe (Ratty), Chairman, Mr. B. Bush, Bar Manager, and Mr. B. Jackson, Treasurer. The Club House was kept open throughout the summer months and it was an unqualified success. There was a profit on the Bar of £31. Ben Bush was a born organizer. During the summers of 1966 and 1967 the Club was kept open and facilities were given to the Cricket Section.

In April, 1970, we were informed by the Lands Agent that a Service or Service sponsored Civilian must be responsible as a member of the Committee in order to sign the lease. During this same period we had the opportunity of signing a Licence, drafted by the Lands Agent, which would have given us Security of Tenure for the premises even though the lands were handed back to the Maltese Government. Arrangements were made for Overseas Hon. Secretary, Mr. T.N. Ricketts, and Treasurer, Mr. G. Sharkey, to meet the Lands Agent in order to sign suitable documents to gain complete control of the Club Rooms, although there is no record of this taking place. The next record was dated the 15th October, 1970, when Mr. Sharkey was asked by Overseas Committee to look into the matter as regards Security of Tenure. However, Security of Tenure or otherwise, the matter was settled in no uncertain terms when the British Forces temporarily withdrew from Malta in January, 1972. Marsa Lodge as a Club House was lost to Overseas.

PLAYING SEASON 1960/61

In the words of Francis Chapelle, Team Captain, Overseas had quite a good playing record and exceeded expectations during the 1960/61 season. Viv Morris, Hon. Secretary and Team Secretary, said that it had been a successful season on and off the field.

With three exceptions, games were played at the Marsa on the newly renovated grounds. Two games were at Ta' Qali and one away game at Hal Far. This season proved exceptionally hot, and lack of rain curtailed the number of games drastically. The first game was not until the 10th December, and the last was on the 11th March.

The problem of getting Service teams to play on a Sunday, although always with us, seemed more acute in this season. Whilst it was suggested by Viv Morris, as the previous Fixture Secretary, at the A.G.M., that in view of the highly organized state of Service rugby and the difficulty of playing Associate or Full Service Members on a Saturday, it would be better to organize as many games on a Sunday as possible, this proved difficult. Frank Kitson, Fixture Secretary, was unable to persuade Service teams to play on a Sunday, although he had some hope against visiting ships. In fact, there were only two or three Sunday games throughout this season, and they were against H.M.S. Girdleness and R.N. School (Tal Handaq). I think this particular season stresses the difficulties Overseas faces in putting out a strong rugby XV without cooperation between Overseas and the Service teams. Having said this, I must stress that this co-operation, almost without exception, existed.

It is of interest that Overseas played 2 games against Tal Handaq, losing the first 3-5 and winning the second 9-3. These games were played in good spirit in spite of the fact that the lads were tickled pink to suggest that they would get their own back for all detentions suffered. The 'Old Crocks' liked to get an outing in these games and this year was no exception. In the first game Bill Polkinghorne and Viv Morris trotted out onto the field and had to be almost carried off.

During this season the Overseas applied to the Secretary Army R.U. (Malta) to take part in the Inter Service 7's Tournament. On this occasion it was refused.

PLAYING RECORD FOR 1960/61
P 15 - W 7 - L 8     Point for 103     Against 143

SOCIAL EVENTS

Although end of season accounts speak of expenses for two dances during the 1960/61 season, the minutes record plans for only one, that of the 28th January, 1961. This is particularly interesting because, although organized by the Overseas Committee, including army representatives, on the dance tickets the following was printed, 'The Army Rugby Club requests the pleasure' etc. One must remember, that during this season only, some functions were combined Overseas/Nomads efforts. In fact, in an open letter to Club Members.

38

dated the 6th March, 1961, Overseas Secretary, Mr. C.V. Morris, said that social events arranged during the season included an Overseas dance and a Combined Overseas, Forts and Nomads R.F.C.'s dance. I assume that the combined dance mentioned was that held on the 28th January, which was an unqualified success.

Mr. J. George, Hon. Social Secretary, resigned on the 29th March, 1961, prior to leaving Malta. He was succeeded by Mr. J.C. Griffiths who made strenuous efforts to put Overseas on a good social footing during the summer months. The Club House was kept open on Thursday evenings throughout the close season with fortnightly functions arranged. John Griffiths himself left Malta in July, 1961.

OFFICIALS LEAVING MALTA

In July, 1961, two members who had been part of the Social life of Overseas for three years, Bill and May Polkinghorne, left Malta. Both gave unstintingly in time and effort. Bill had been Hon. Treasurer for 3 years 1958-61, Club House/Bar Manager 1958/59, and in spite of having previously hung up his boots once or twice, he was the regular full back for Overseas in 1958/59. Bill had previously been a playing member of Overseas between 1950-53. May had been on the Social Committee in 1958/59 and again in 1960/61, and was the last Lady Committee Member to be elected at the A.G.M.

John George left Malta in August, 1961, after being Social Secretary in 1958/59 and again in 1960/61. In 1958/59 he organized events with very little financial backing and on this score he must have found it easier in 1960/61. John was an invaluable member of any Committee and his support and advice was welcomed by three Hon. Secretaries. He organized much of the printing required by Overseas between 1958-61.

One of the main reports at this meeting was that of the Rules Sub-Committee. The Sub-Committee of Messrs. C.V. Morris, V. Renyard and J. Kirkpatrick had been formed on the 29th March, 1961, to discuss new and modified rules for the Club. The amended rules were put before the members at the A.G.M. and adopted in entirely without addition or deletion. This was the first revision of the rules since their formation in 1958, and the amendments were made as a result of 3 years' experience in running the Club. Under the revised rules, the Officers of the Club were increased in number and included Vice-Presidents for the first time. The number of Vice-Presidents required was not stated. Unfortunately, there is no record of this working Committee's reasoning, but at least in the case of Mr. T.E. Arrigo, he was appointed Vice-President 'in view of his past allegiance to the Rugby Union Code and more particularly for the excellent support and encouragement which he gave the team last season'. In general, since 1961, Vice-Presidency has been given for past service to the Club, but it has been an active position, and Vice-Presidents are 'working' Members of the Club.

In October, 1961, Captain John Day left Malta, and so Overseas lost a very active Committee Member. John Day during the previous season(s) had been Secretary of the Army R.U. (Malta), Team Captain of Nomads R.F.C., Nomads/Army Representative on the Overseas Bar Committee, and occasional player for Overseas 1959/60 when not committed to play for the Nomads. (Captained Overseas on the 26th December, 1960, against H.M.S. Ark Royal). Acting under Lt. Col. T.G. Chambers, he was the person most active in discovering Marsa Lodge at the start of the 1960/61 season and receiving permission from the Army authorities for Overseas/Nomads to use it as a Club House.

RULES AS REVISED BY A SUB-COMMITTEE AND ADOPTED AT THE A.G.M., 12th OCTOBER, 1961
  1. 1 That the name of the Club be:- "THE OVERSEAS RUGBY UNION FOOTBALL CLUB, MALTA, G.C."
  2. 2 That the object of the Club is to help foster the true "Rugger" spirit on the Island by providing facilities for:
    1. (a) ALL Service and Civilian rugger players who are unable to play for any other rugger team; i.e. Members of Units unable to field a side.
    2. (b) ALL Service and Civilian rugger players, who although committed to play for a Unit side during the week, wish to play Club rugger over the weekend.
    3. (c) Non-playing rugger enthusiasts who may support the Club and join its social life.
  3. 3 That the Club colours by Navy Blue and White hoops.
  4. 4 That the Officers of the Club shall consist of the President, Vice-Presidents, Hon. Secretary, Hon. Treasurer, Hon. Fixture Secretary, Hon. Team Secretary, Team Captains, Bar Manager, Social Secretary. These Officers to hold office for one year and be elected by Members at an Annual General Meeting.
  5. 5 That the management of the Club shall be entrusted to a General Committee consisting of such Officers as shall be elected at the Annual General Meeting. Liaison with the representatives of the Services shall be effected by means of Joint Services Rugby Representatives, who will sit on the Bar Management Committee.
  6. 6 That the General Committee shall have the powers to fill any vacancies which may arise in their number during the course of the year, have full power to co-opt as may be found expedient and delegate any of its duties to such other Committees as may be necessary.
  7. 7 A quorum for a General Committee shall be one third of the Committee.

FINAL RECORD FOR 1961/62

P 19 - W8 - L 10 - D1   Points for 143 Against 209

INSURANCE COVER FOR PLAYERS

On the 2nd November, 1961, it was proposed and passed in Committee that the Club would hold itself responsible for the insurance of all players playing for the Overseas R.U.F.C. A number of enquiries had already been made, with different Insurance Companies, by Members of the Committee dating back to the 28th December, 1960. On the 8th December, 1961, a Comprehensive Insurance cover for players (Personal accident) was taken out with insurers "Northern" through Lambert Brothers (Insurance) Ltd., Insurance Brokers, London. This covered Permanent Total Disablement - Scale compensation £1,000 per player and Temporary Total Disablement - £5 per week per player, payable up to 52 weeks in excess of the first 14 days' disablement.

Although this particular insurance cover was renewed up to the 8th December, 1968, it was obvious, even in 1964, that it was insufficient in its coverage. On the 22nd May, 1964, the Hon. Secretary was asked to investigate and obtain a more satisfactory Insurance Policy.

The main problem was peculiar to Overseas. For the purpose of insurance one must think of players as Servicemen, U.K. Based Civilians entitled to medical treatment (Service Hospital and Clinic) by virtue of their Service Employment in Malta, and non-entitled Civilians. The insurance with Lambert Brothers covered all players for permanent disablement and temporary disablement in excess of 14 days, but it did not cover injured players being examined and treated in hospital on the day of injury and having to report to the hospital or doctor for further treatment. Thus, an injured non-entitled Civilian, under the Insurance Policy in force at the time, would be out of pocket receiving medical treatment within 14 days of the injury, at the Maltese Hospital St. Lukes, or King George V Hospital (originally built as a British Merchant Seamen Hospital).

In consequence of above, and an injury to Mr. Paul Flack, early 1964, which pin-pointed the problem, the following rule was added to the Club Rules at the A.G.M. on the 15th October, 1964.

"That the Club's liability in respect of injuries sustained on the playing enclosure by playing members shall be limited to the terms of the Insurance Policy in force at the time of the injury."

On the 6th November, 1965, the Club submitted a proposal form for one unit of the Rugby Football Union Insurance for players, at a premium of 15/-, covering Death (£150 - £2,250) and Permanent Disablement (£375 - £1,500). This meant we had two insurances in force and although Lambert Brothers' Insurance covered temporary disablement, we had taken it out on the basis of an excess for the first 14 days. Thus, we still had no insurance to cover the payment of hospital and doctor's fees from the time of occurrence of injury.

The problem was highlighted once again on the 19th December, 1965, when the team Captain, Mr. J. Handford, suffered a fractured fibula. Jack, a non-entitled Civilian, was taken to St. Luke's Hospital for treatment and initially had to pay the hospital bill himself. Immediately, the President (1965),

Mr. J. Sharp, wrote to Surgeon Rear Admiral M.R. Adams, R.N. Hospital, Bighi, requesting that injured players might be taken preferably to R.N.H. Bighi, or alternately King George V Hospital, for examination and necessary treatment by R.N. Doctors. Mr. Sharp, in support of his request, explained that the Club did not seek free treatment, as the players were covered by insurance, but at that time Mr. Sharp did not appreciate the shortcomings of the insurance cover. In reply, Surgeon Rear Admiral Adams said there was no problem about the entitled members, but he regretted that regulations do not permit him to accept non-entitled persons in R.N.H. Bighi, except as emergencies, and the correct hospital for them was K.G.V. There they could be treated by naval Orthopedic or Surgical Specialists as the case required, and if they so wish. However, because of possible unacceptable delay in treatment at K.G.V, by Naval Specialists, he was prepared to agree that Serious Casualties could be seen at R.N.H. Bighi, as emergencies in the first instance, and if in-patient treatment was required for a non-entitled patient he would be transferred to K.G.V. But, if he was unfit to move, he would be retained at Bighi at a charge of £9.5s a day which the M.O.D. laid down for non-entitled patients.

On the 22nd September, 1966, it was resolved to investigate with the R.F.U. to obtain a more comprehensive Insurance Policy with particular reference to the payment of hospital and doctor's fees incurred by an injured player from the time of occurrence of injury. However, on the 1st December, 1966, after a thorough investigation (with Lambert Brothers and the R.F.U.) it was decided that insurance to cover those players who were not entitled to Service Medical facilities was not possible at a reasonable premium. Immediately, on the 7th December, 1966, the Club started a 'Sinking Fund' to help players who were injured whilst playing for the Club to meet possible expenses. £10 was transferred from the Club's account and the match fee was raised to 2/6d. 1/6d of which went into the fund. Payment from this fund, up to 50% of expenses incurred through injury, to a maximum of £7.10s was given to the player. All members were asked to contribute to this fund. On the 1st April, 1971, a sum of £25 was transferred from the Club main account into the Sinking Fund.

Following Jack Handford's injury, John Hitt (Hitty) organized a 'Whip Round' to cover Jack's medical expenses. Fortunately, Jack's employer agreed to pay his medical expenses and so the money collected was not immediately needed. In Hitty's own words, "All in all, this is quite the best misfire I've ever had. From a Civil Servant that ain't hay." Hitty's 'Whip Round' was then paid into the Sinking Fund for future use.

On the 14th October, 1971, Surg. Cdr. J. Alderson, R.N., was able to report in Committee that agreement had been reached with R.N. Hospital Mtarfa for treatment of Club Members, entitled and non-entitled, in respect of any injuries occurring to players.

The Insurance Policy with Lambert Brothers lapsed on the 8th December, 1969, and the Insurance Policy with the R.F.U. lapsed with the British Services withdrawal early 1972 and the consequent temporary disbanding of the Overseas Club.

45

When the Club Rules were reformed at the A.G.M. 1973, the new rule 10 stated:-

"The Club cannot accept liability for loss, accident or injury which may occur on the field of play or on the Club premises."

On the 11th November, 1974, following discussion in the General and Rugby Section Committees, it was decided to take advantage of the R.F.U. offer of player's insurance as covered in an information letter from the R.F.U. dated 5th July, 1974. The Overseas (Now the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club) Rugby Section took out 2 units of cover per team (2 teams) at a cost of £2.60 per unit, covering Death (£250 - £3,000) and Permanent Disablement (£1,000 - £2,000). Compensation figures quoted are for one Unit of Benefit. The weakness still remained concerning doctor's fees for personnel not entitled to Service medical facilities, but it was felt at this time that individual insurance was the immediate problem of each individual. Unfortunately, when we tried to renew the R.F.U. insurance for the 1975/76 season the insurers, Sun Alliance, and London Insurance Ltd., decided that complications arise under terms of policy if cover is afforded to Clubs permanently based in an overseas country, and our application was not accepted. Players were advised to take out their own insurance.

OVERSEAS CLUB TIES

On the 19th October, 1961, following a proposal in Committee, the Hon. Secretary, Mr. C.V. Morris, agreed to investigate designs for a Club Tie. Sketches of a proposed design were sent to A.G. Almond, 46, Sidney Street, Cambridge. On the 24th January, 1962, after the inevitable correspondence, counter sketches, samples of materials and patterns of actual fabric showing design, a firm order, as approved by the members, was placed with A.G. Almond. The ties were of terylene in Navy Blue with the design of the Club Motif in white woven in. The cost to the Club was 16/6d each and after making allowance for payment of customs duty and post, they were sold to members at £1 each.

This was the first Club tie and they were well received by members. The ties arrived in Malta during April, 1962, and by June 8th, out of a total of 152 ties, 75 were sold.

In 1973 when Overseas became a Sports Club it became necessary to change the letters within the Motif from O.R.F.C. to O.R.S.C. The first order with the changed letters was placed with Maddocks & Dicks in February, 1974, and to keep cost to members down, initially at £11.20, the ties were printed although still with full motif. An order was placed with the same firm in May, 1975, with the material of a lighter blue, but the next order in September of the same year saw the return to dark blue.

In 1974 a special tie was made for Overseas by Badgecraft of Croydon and this was presented at the Annual Dinner Dance to Mr. J. Sharp, a Life Member, for his untiring work for the Club. The tie had a single hand-worked Motif in silver wire on a royal blue background. The Motif was similar to that on the ordinary Club tie. In February, 1975, it was decided in

Committee to reserve the same design for Life Members and in March, 1975, two such ties were presented to Mr. T.N. Ricketts and Mr. N.C. Morgan.

SOCIAL EVENTS 1961/62

Throughout the season various first class functions were arranged by Edgar Battye, Social Secretary, David Isted, Bar Manager, Vivian Morris, Secretary, and the Social Committee. The season opened with a Club Dance on the 4th November, 1961, and ended with an Open Air Supper Dance at the United Services Sports Club, Marsa (now called the Malta Sports Club) on the 7th July, 1962. For good measure a Supper Dance, with dancing to the R.M.A. Dance Band (Kirkop Brothers), was held at the Club House on the 24th March. The Annual Dinner was held at the U.S.S.C. on 5th April. Dancing to records took place after the meal. Other functions included Car Treasure Hunts, a Hot Pot Supper and a Roulette Night. The Social life was helped by the fact that every last Thursday in the month, as agreed at the A.G.M., was a Ladies night. Added to this, functions were arranged at the Club House by the Hawks (RAF), Overseas/Falcon (Fleet Air Arm Hal Far) and the Army R.U. (Malta). The Army entertained an Italian Army Rugby Team by holding a dance at the Club on the 1st March, 1962. The facilities of the Club House were certainly used.

On the 29th March, 1962, it was decided to keep the Club House open on Friday evenings during April and May. The position was to be reviewed at the end of May although no decision was recorded as to whether the Club House remained open for the remainder of the Close season.

In June, 1962, the General Manager of the Villa Rosa Beach Club, St. George's Bay, St. Julians, offered Block Membership to members of Overseas R.U.F.C. on the basis of half the normal single subscription rate. A number of members took up the offer.

During September, 1962, a Touring cricket team called "The Romany Players" requested facilities for a Dance on Saturday, 8th September. Arrangements were duly made.

REVISION OF RULES

Rule 11 was revised at the A.G.M. to make membership of the Club the same for Playing and Social Members at 10/- per season.

Altered Rule Read:-

  • 11 Membership
    • (a) Playing Members Annual Subscription 10/-
    • (b) Social Members Annual Subscription 10/-
    • (c) Student Members Annual Subscription 2/6

a. b. c. have full privileges.

PLAYING SEASON

The playing results for 1962/63 gave the Club its best season for several years, although according to the Team Captain, Mr. Louis Thacker, they gave little indication of the team's potential. The season was started with a new set of jerseys. The team played with great confidence until beset with injuries to key players over the Christmas period, winning 5 of the first 6 matches. At this stage the points tally was 107 for and 33 against. The Captain was one of the injured players and Paul Flack, Vice Captain, took over the Captaincy. Lou Thacker was the driving force behind the early successes. In his end of season report, Lou

Thacker spoke highly of several players. Terry Ashton who was an inspiration to the side at centre. Frank Kitson, who at first reluctantly agreed to play as hooker, was virtually never out-hooked. Jack Handford, the most consistent forward. Francis Chapelle in his 4th consecutive season with Overseas had a very good season at Full Back. His kicking, both place and touch, was invaluable.

Overseas Club was invited to participate in the Inter Service 7’s held at the Marsa on Saturday, 16th February, 1963. We entered one team. Unfortunately, no record has been kept of the results. Four pitches were used, Navy 1 & 2 and Army 1 & 2. According to a signal from the Army R.U. Secretary, Captain C.S. Ward, dated 7th November, 1962. ‘The Army grounds are the top two grounds at Marsa (USSC end) No. 1 being nearest the Road, No. 2 next to the golf course.’

During the Christmas holidays two games took place between a team from Tal Handaq School and a team made up from school- boys on leave with parents in Malta. The games were organised by Mr. Jack Sharp, and in this instance, with the able assistance of Viv Morris and Capt. Sam Ward. They were held at the Marsa on the 27th December, 1962 and the 4th January, 1963 the first of what was to become traditional ‘Exiles vs Tal Handaq’ Christmas holiday games. They became a Club commitment and for six years they were organised by Jack Sharp. It was decided that the Exiles should consist of schoolboys up to 19 years of age. Normally, the Exiles just held the edge over Tal Handaq, but during the 1966/67 games the school team, trained by Mr. John Bowen and Captained by Brian Jackson, gained 2 decisive victories. At this time an attempt was made to raise the age limit of the Exiles to 21, but it was decided, that as the school team would not be as strong the following season, to retain the age at 19.

FINAL RECORD FOR 1962/63

P 21 - W 10 - L 11    Points for 211 Against 198

SOCIAL EVENTS

It would appear, compared with the previous season, the Social life of 1962/63 was quiet. Nevertheless, the three dances held at the Club House, according to the Social Secretary, Mr. Edgar Battye, were a success, as also was the Army/Overseas Hot Pot Supper held at the Club on the 31st January, 1963. The fact that the second of these dances at the Club House, on the 19th January, 1963, caused complaints of overcrowding and a ‘Noisy Element’, led to the number allowed to future dances at the Club to be set at 180. Unfortunately, the end of season Dinner to have been held at the United Services Sports Club (now Malta Sports Club), Marsa, had to be cancelled due to lack of support.

During the close season, up to the 11th July, 1963, the Club remained open on Friday evenings, and closed completely between the 11th July and the 18th September.

                                    PLAYING SEASON

1963/64 was a season of mixed fortunes. Overseas
started on a bright note defeating D.E.R.R. Wanderers by
14 points to 3, but this proved to be the only Saturday
win of the season. Starting in January, five Sunday games
were arranged which made it possible to play Overseas players
otherwise committed on a Saturday (Service Teams) with the
result that a more balanced team could be fielded. This
produced a much higher standard of rugby. Three of the Sunday
games ended in wins.

The highlight of the season was without doubt the tour of
the Combined Services side (Army and R.A.F.) from Tripoli,
N. Africa. This tour was arranged by the Combined Services
(Malta) although Overseas was represented on the Working Sub-
Committee, which made arrangements for accommodation, transport
and entertainment for the touring side, by Mr. C.V. Morris (Hon.
Secretary) and Mr. E. Battye (Hon. Social Secretary). Four
games were arranged for the tourists, namely against the R.N.,
the Army, the R.A.F., and the Overseas Club, all played at
the Stadium, Marsa. For the game against the Overseas on the
14th December, 1963, we were honoured by the attendance of His

Excellency the Governor, Sir Maurice Dorman, accompanied by the British Ambassador to Italy. The Governor was presented to both teams. Although the Overseas came out losers, the teams were closely matched, and the game proved to be one of the best of the season for Overseas.

Overseas entered one team in the Inter Service Unit 7's at the Marsa on the 15th February, 1964. The team, namely, Handford, Randall, O'Brien, Mac, Spiers, Henry and Brown, was knocked out by Luqa, 5 points to 3 in the first round.

The Team Captain, Jack Handford, spoke highly of a number of schoolboys (Tal Handaq) who played for Overseas during the season, namely, Geoff Randall, wing, Ian O'Brien, centre; Brian Jackson (only 15 years of age) scrum half; and Tex Brown, forward, who won the 'Sam Ward Cup' for the most improved player of the season. This was the first year that the Sam Ward Cup was presented. Other players mentioned were Paul Flack, stand-off half, in his fifth and final year as an Overseas player, who proved to be one of the mainstays of the side, Charles Burton, wing forward, R. Sussex and Army, Peter Henshall, prop, a good all round player with vast experience, Harry Barstow, R. Sussex and Army, centre, Keith Donavon, D.E.R.R. Wanderers, scrum half, Derek Henry, prop, and John Why (Vice-Captain), lock. In summing up, Jack Handford said that as regards match results it could not be said that 1963/64 season was a good one for Overseas, but from the point of view of promoting rugby on the Island the Club played a large part. And this is one of the main objects of the Overseas Club.

SOCIAL EVENTS

In the months before Christmas most of the efforts of the Social Committee went into making a social success of the Malta tour by the Combined Services, Tripoli. The overall planning was done by the Working Sub-Committee but the special task for Overseas was to hold a Social Evening for the Other Ranks at our Club House, Marsa Lodge, on the 12th December, 1963. This was a success, helped by the fact that 6 crates of free beer were consumed during the evening. During the same evening an Official Cocktail Party was held at the Officers Mess Castille (Army HQ, Auberge de Castille, Valletta). Overseas was represented at this function by Jack Sharp (President), Vivian Morris, (Hon. Secretary), Jack Handford (Team Captain) and Frank Kitson (Committee Member).

From the beginning of the season Mr. J. Osman took over from Mr. E. Battye as Social Secretary, Praise for the success of Social activities must go to both for work done whilst they were in office.

A Tramps Ball held at the Club House on the 6th March, 1964 provided a first class evening. The band of the Royal Sussex Regiment attended.

The Annual Dinner Dance was held at the United Services Sports Club, Marsa, on the 15th May, 1964. Financially, the Club lost £34 on the evening but, bearing in mind that a subsidy of 2/6d was paid on 125 tickets and 14 tickets at 17/6d each were donated to Club Guests, the loss was not out of proportion to the enjoyment and goodwill created on behalf of the Club.

The Club House was closed for the summer months from 30th April to the 3rd September, 1964.

PLAYING SEASON

The 1964/65 season started off with two trial matches, the normal Overseas start of the season Trial Match and a Demonstration/Teaching Match under the new rules coming into force that season. This season the Overseas Trial Match was held at Ta' Qali, versus R.A.F. Luqa, on the 31st October, 1964. The Demonstration Match was organized by the Army (Malta) R.F.U. and all arrangements were made by their Hon. Secretary, Major J.W.S. Dominy. Overseas were invited to attend. The Team Captains of all invited Clubs forwarded the names of 5 players and from these names two XVs were selected and two Captains nominated. Overseas was represented by Messrs. J. Handford, J. Why, P. Henshall, D. Henry and I. O'Brien. The Malta Rugby Referees Panel appointed four referees to take this match and thereby gave the referees an opportunity to try their hand under the new laws. The Demonstration Match was held at the Marsa on the 7th November, 1964.

From the 1st October, 1964, each Thursday evening during the playing season, training facilities were made available at Tal Handaq School gymnasium when John Bowen, the school senior

53

P.E. Instructor, kindly ran training sessions. If overseas players were not fit it was not John's fault. His circuits were killers (I speak from experience), you had to be fit to get round once. Overseas Club has been indebted to the school Authorities for allowing us these facilities each rugby season since 1964. John personally ran these training sessions for three years. Trevor Ricketts, who succeeded John as Senior P.E. Instructor at Tal Handaq in September, 1967, has continued the Thursday evening training sessions to this date (1976/77). The Club is indeed indebted to John and Trevor.

During this season, up to the 9th January, 1965, Mr. P. Garnons-Williams, Fixture Secretary, gave an excellent press coverage in the local papers, 'Times of Malta' and 'Malta News', on each game in which Overseas participated. Unfortunately his reports faded out after the 9th January. These reports, together with the Team Captain's end of season list of games and results, have been used to record the season's results, also the main scorers. In his report on the opening match against the Duke of Edinburgh Royal Regiment Wanderers, Mr Garnons-Williams said that, unlike previous seasons, the majority of our players were fit. In his end of season report the Team Captain said 'for the first time ever the Overseas were amongst the fittest on the field. The team owes a great deal to John Bowen for giving up his time to achieve this.'

On the 31st January, 1965 Overseas entered two Invitation Teams in the Navy 7's Tournament. In the final of the Cup, Overseas 'A' lost to Falcon 'B' by 8 points to 3, and in the final of the Plate, Overseas 'B' lost to St. Angelo by 24 points to nil. We also entered two teams in the Inter Service 7's on the 27th February, 1965, with not quite as impressive results.

Throughout the season Overseas had a fairly strong and consistent XV. After a slow start the forwards improved, with Jack Hands (Team Captain) and Peter Hanshall most often mentioned in dispatches, whilst the back division was strong and potentially always dangerous. The backs mentioned in the Team Captain's report on the 14th January, 1965, were Brian Jackson (Senior), full back, David Agar, wing, John Evans and Ken Lawrence (Centre or stand off) and Keith Donavon, scrum half. Also mentioned were the good reserves available over the Christmas holidays with the arrival of Roger Wilson, Jim O'Doine and Patrick Hamilton-Hill, not forgetting Brian Jackson (Junior) (no relation of Brian Jackson senior) who was a very good stand-in as scrum half. The Captain expressed the opinion that the Club was in for a record season and today (14th January) one record had been broken when Brian Jackson (senior) had scored 108 points. The Team Captain's end of season report confirmed that Overseas played much improved rugby winning 17 out of their 26 games, which beat their previous best season of 10 wins in 1962/63, and scored 467 points with 167 against.

Fortunately, although no final complete results of player's averages is available, Brian Jackson has been able to confirm that he scored the record number of 187 points in the season (1964/65), including 13 tries. 13 tries from the full back position is pretty good. Brian also confirmed that David Agar scored 12 tries during the same season although there is no record of David's final points tally.

Ralph DeJear was awarded the Sam Ward Cup as the most improved player of the season. Ralph McGillivray, Overseas Team Captain of 1961/62, was selected to referee the Inter Service match on the 13th February, 1965, between the Army (Malta) and the Navy (Malta).

At the start of the season concern was shown by Overseas General Committee in the shortage of players. This problem has always been with us, increasingly so each year as the number of Service personnel stationed on the Island has decreased. The Overseas Secretary, Vivian Morris, wrote to a number of local firms, including Swan & Hunters, Shell Malta, Cable & Wireless, R.F.A’s, and also to the Personnel Officer of the Malta Drydocks, trying to interest members of their staff rugbywise. The Secretary also wrote to the Rector of St. Edward’s College trying to interest the Maltese Students in the game, with no success. Fortunately, as has already been shown by the number of reserves arriving during season 1964/65, the team was considerably strengthened.
