SOCIAL EVENTS

The innovation of Film Evenings for members and ladies proved a success. Through the kind services of Mr. J. Sharp, Overseas President, in providing films, equipment and projectionist, four Film Evenings were held at the Club House between November and March. All were well attended and overall were financially successful. Buffet arrangements were made by Mr. Ben Bush.

A successful Christmas Draw made a handsome profit of £29. Once again Ben Bush provided the buffet. A Stag Hot Pot Supper was held at the Club House on the 14th February, 1965. This was judged to be an excellent evening.

Games Nights were held at the WO's & Sgts Mess, Mtarfa, on the 16th January and on the 10th April, 1965, also at the Ordnance Social Club, Ospizio, on the 20th March, 1965. The second games night at Mtarfa was in the nature of a reciprocation by the Overseas RFC who were unable to act as hosts at Marsa Lodge. No reason was given.

The Playing season social activities ended with the Annual Dinner Dance at the United Services Sports Club, Marsa on Friday, 2nd April, 1965. Joe Camilleri's band attended. Once again a high number of Official Guests were invited,

fourteen in all, and resulted in a loss of £12 against the loss of £34 the previous season.

The Social Secretary, Mr. D. Henry left Malta during April, 1965, and he was succeeded by Ben Bush who was co-opted onto the General Committee for the summer months.

Initially, it was proposed to close the Club House during the close season as from the end of April, 1965. However, because of the keenness of members to keep the Club open, the General Committee authorised and set up a Sub-Committee to be responsible to the Main Committee for all activities which took place during the summer. This Sub-Committee has already been mentioned under the heading "Club House - Marsa Lodge". All functions arranged during the summer were well attended including the normal Thursday ev-ings. The purchases of a large refrigerator from M.P.B.W., Imriehel, for £20, at the beginning of the summer undoubtedly contributed to the success of the venture.

OVERSEAS CRICKET SECTION

During the summer months of 1965 an Overseas Cricket Team was formed. A previous attempt had been made in 1964 but the idea had been dropped through lack of support and lack of cricket gear. Initially, the cricket team was formed as an activity to keep members of the 'Rugger Club' in touch throughout the summer months. Indeed, the 'games of cricket at the Marsa' helped to make the summer social life at the Club House during this period such a success. A meeting of all Overseas members interested in cricket took place at Marsa Lodge on the 6th May, 1965, when a Captain and two Vice-Captains were elected and a Selection Committee formed. For this first season games were played outside the league programme.

The pioneers mainly responsible for the formation of the Cricket Team Section were, amongst others, John Osman in 1964, and Peter Ratcliffe (affectionately known as 'Ratty'), Brian Jackson (Jacko), Ralph Daley, David Agar, Peter Cantello, Jack Hambham, John Evans, Jack Roberts, Vic Jones, Peter Garnons-Williams, and big Ben Bush, in 1965. Not forgetting the General Committee behind them.

Following is a copy of Ben's Letter:-

30th April, 1965.

Dear Members,

On Thursday, May 6th, 1965, there will be a meeting at Marsa Lodge of all members interested in the formation of an Overseas Cricket Team. This will not be a separate club but an activity to keep members of the Rugger Club in touch throughout the summer months.

Business to be discussed includes the election of a captain, vice-captain and selection committee, availability of players, grounds and fixtures, etc.

I should be grateful if you would complete and return the attached form at your earliest convenience, to give some idea of the numbers likely to attend.

I should like to take this opportunity to introduce myself as the new Social Secretary. I am taking over from Derek Henry, who is leaving the island, and I will endeavour to uphold the standards set by him.

(BEN BUSH)
CRICKET & SOCIAL SECRETARY, ORUFC

The meeting of the 6th May was presided over by Mr. P. Ratcliffe. 13 Members were present.

The following were elected:-

  • Team Captain: Mr. P. Cantello
  • Vice Captains: Mr. B. Jackson, Mr. D. Agar

Selection Committee: The President, Captain, two Vice Captains and the Secretary

At an Overseas General Committee Meeting on the 16th March, 1966, an 'Official' Cricket Section was formed and it was agreed that all new members of the Club would pay a composite subscription to cover the Rugby and Cricket Sections. The Cricket Section to be administered by a Sub-Committee composed of a Chairman and two other officers to be elected by the Cricket Section. Peter Ratcliffe was elected the first Chairman. In his account of the 1966 summer season, Ratty said that the main item was the entry of the cricket team into the Combined Services League, which Overseas won. Between 1965 and 1970 the Cricket Section was 'sponsored' by the summer bar takings although all expenditure was sanctioned by the main Committee. In March, 1970, Mr. J. Christie, Cricket Section Chairman, requested a grant of £30 per annum as a subsidy from the main Club to the Cricket Section. The main Committee agreed that the Cricket Section should be considered as a Sub-Section and that any reasonable expenditure necessitated by this Section would be viewed with consideration by the General Committee, also that for the year 1970 the Cricket Section be allowed to purchase equipment to the value of £30. From this point (1970 season) the Cricket Section, whilst accepting a subsidy from the main Club at the start of each season to cover immediate expenses, always attempted to be self-supporting by covering this subsidy from match subscriptions and other methods of fund raising.

The Cricket Section, as a Section of Overseas, was temporarily disbanded between the 30th December, 1971, and the 21st September, 1972, due to the British Services withdrawal. In the summer of 1973, Overseas Cricket Team was back in action once again and in this season became Malta League Champions. Also in 1973 season a kind donor presented the Cricket Section with £50 and enabled them to more than return the £30 subsidy for that year. From January, 1972, the Marsa Club came under the management of the Maltese and its name was changed from the United Services Sports Club to the Malta Sports Club. Cricket, with its centre at the Marsa, came under the control of the Malta Sports Club Cricket Section Committee. Although it is for the Cricket Section to tell of their fortunes on the field, it must be stated, that like the Rugby Section, the Cricket Section has made a great contribution to sport in Malta, and helped to make 'Overseas' a respected name.

At a meeting held on the 4th October, 1965, it had been noted that under the rules of the Club, the Vice-Presidents, as nominees and not elected members, were not entitled to attend meetings of the General Committee. This point was raised at the A.G.M. and Messrs. N. Johnson; G.G. Jackson; J.P. Ratcliffe; L. Duncan and J.D. Green were duly elected, all to remain as Vice-Presidents until such time as they retire from Office or left Malta.

The Rules of the Club were amended to include the following as Rule 7:-

'That there be a Selection Committee of three the composition of which shall be decided at the Annual General Meeting and shall include the Captain, Vice-Captain and one other.'

This meant that the Vice-Captain be elected at the A.G.M. The composition of the Selection Committee for 1965/66 was Messrs. J. Handford (Captain); P. Henshall (Vice-Captain); and P. Ratcliffe.

From 1965 to 1971, inclusive, details of Overseas R.U.F.C. were inserted in the Sport Section of The Malta Year Book. These details usually included the President's and Secretary's names and addresses, the fact we were affiliated to the R.F.U. and the previous season's playing record.

PLAYING SEASON

1965/66 was another exceptionally good season from the playing point of view. Overseas set off with a new set of jerseys and play to match. The 5 pitches at the Marsa were all available, i.e. Playable, from the 1st November, and the Joint Services (Malta) Rugby Committee agreed that they be allocated by the Fleet Recreation Officer. The first match for Overseas was on the 10th November versus H.M.S. Rhyl.

Once again the Team Captain’s end of season report has been lost. After spending a number of hours in the Royal Malta Library, Valletta, looking for information and results in copies of the Malta News and Times of Malta, I compiled an incomplete list of fixtures and results. Fortunately, Jack Handford had kept his old fixture card, complete with results, and this he has recently handed to me. Jack has also produced an interesting list of player’s individual appearances over four years. This list I will reproduce at the end of the 1965/ 66 'Playing Season' report.

As in the previous season, according to the press coverage in the Malta News by their Rugby Correspondent ‘Ronnie Sacco’, the outstanding player for Overseas was Brian Jackson (senior). I have no complete analysis of player’s averages, but I have been informed by a very reliable source, Jacko himself, that the total number of points scored by Jacko during 1965/66 was 143. As mentioned previously in an item about insurance, the Team Captain, Jack Handford, broke his leg in December, 1965, and whilst Jack was out of action the Team was Captained most capably by Peter Henshall.

An interesting table in the Malta News (9th December, 1965) gave a round up of Joint Services Inter Unit Rugby, ‘All played on a friendly basis’. The table includes all teams based in Malta during the early part of season 1965/66, indeed, only the Sussex Regt. was not a permanent part of Malta Rugby at that time. For the purpose of comparison 'Overseas', the only Civilian Rugby Club in Malta, was included as a Service Unit. It is a pity that a similar table was not included at the end of the season. We would have topped the table.

P W D L F AGST.
Luq 4 4 0 0 50 12
Overseas 3 3 0 0 79 8
Hawks 3 1 1 1 26 5
Forts 3 1 0 2 15 27
Sussex 3 1 0 2 17 23
Nomads 3 0 0 3 4 94

Highlights of the season, After 6 years Overseas managed to beat Forts (Fort St. Angelo), 6 points to nil, in the traditional Boxing Day match at the Marsa. For the first time Overseas were winners of the ‘Plate’ in the Inter Service 7’s (sometimes termed the Inter Unit 7’s) on the 19th February, 1966. Overseas 'B' to be exact. Overseas also received an invitation to enter the Navy 7’s although no record remains as to whether we entered same.

Two Touring sides visited Malta in the second half of the season. Overseas played a British Army Team from Benghazi, N. Africa, on the 30th January, 1966, losing 5 - 8. Benghazi Bedouins kept an unbeaten record during their tour.

Last game of the season, on the 12th March, 1966 Overseas played a touring side (RAF) from Cyprus, losing 6 - 9.

One of the mainstays of the Overseas pack, Peter Cantello, left Malta in March, 1966. During his 2 years' service in Malta, Peter had played for the Royal Navy, captaining a winning side in 1964/65, also for Overseas and St. Angelo. Previously he had played for the R.N. (U.K.) and Hampshire County.

Adrian Wirth, one of the few Maltese players to have played for Overseas up to 1973, won the annual award of the Sam Ward Cup for the most improved player of season 1965/66. It was an exceedingly well earned award, both for the improvement in play and very courageous defence. He had absolutely no fear.

SOCIAL EVENTS

The main recorded Social Events of the playing season were the monthly Film Evenings at Marsa Lodge. These functions proved popular and financially successful, once again thanks to Jack Sharp.

A Christmas Party for the children of Overseas Club Members was held on the 30th December, 1965, at Marsa Lodge. This was organised by Janet Daley, wife of the Social Secretary, and a Ladies Committee formed for the purpose. The Overseas Committee were of the opinion that the venture was an unqualified success. The Annual Dinner Dance was held at the United Services Sports Club, Marsa, on Friday, 25th March, 1966. V. Valente and his band attended. John Hitt (Hitty) was Master of Ceremonies. This was voted another memorable evening. There was a loss of £33. 22 guests were invited.

The Club House remained open during the close season under a Summer Committee.

As shown above, Members who volunteered to do Bar Duties were named 'Bar Helpers', instead of, as previously Bar Committee Members. However, as described on Page 30 under 'Club House - Marsa Lodge', their duties were quite onerous without Committee work.

Up to the A.G.M. (1966/67) the financial year ended on the 30th September. At the A.G.M. it was proposed and carried, that because of the difficulty in organising the A.G.M. early enough in October, the financial year should end on the 31st March.

During this period the Club Accounts were audited by Turquand, Youngs and Co., Accountants of 10, South Street, Valletta. Four members who were on the staff of Turquand, Youngs and Co., and to whom the Club was most grateful, were Messrs. N. Johnson; J.L. Duncan; J.D. Green and P. Bennie. The first three named were Vice-Presidents of the Club between 1963 and 1969. Mr. Bennie was Hon. Treasurer of the Club 1965/67 although Mr. Green took over as acting Hon. Treasurer during the 1966/67 season. Mr. Green was elected Hon. Life Member of the Club at the A.G.M. of 1969/70. I believe there are other members of the staff of the same firm of Auditors who did sterling work for Overseas but unfortunately I do not know their names.

At the end of the 1965/66 season three very staunch supporters of the Club resigned from Office.

Jack Sharp had been President for four years and had decided not to stand for re election as he considered it time to make way for some other person. Jack, at this point of time

Club History

(1966/67), besides being Vice-President, 1961/62, President, 1962-66, and serving on the Bar Committee, 1963-65, had helped the Club in many ways behind the scenes. One of the more obvious ways in which he helped the Club was to provide all the necessities to hold Film Evenings. It is very difficult to talk of Jack in the past tense, as he is still, at the time of writing this history (1975/76), one of the mainstays of the Club. However, we will keep to the 1966 A.G.M. for the present.

Vivian Morris, after 6½ years as Hon. Secretary, felt the time had come to hand over to a successor. Vivian joined the Overseas in 1959 and in the following seven years, besides the Office of Hon. Secretary, held the Offices of Hon. Fixture Secretary, 1959/60 and 1965/66; Hon. Team Secretary, 1960-62; Caretaker Bar Manager during the close season 1962; and served on the Club House/Bar Committee, 1959/60; 1961/62 and 1964/65. He rendered the Club invaluable service. Vivian was succeeded by Mr. E.W. Platt, who, unfortunately, was due to leave before the next A.G.M. For this reason an Assistant Hon. Secretary was elected at the A.G.M. 1966.

Ralph McGillivray had been with the Club for 5 years and his record was also quite impressive. Ralph an Overseas player for 3 years became Team Captain for the 1964/62 season. He served on the Social Committee, 1962/63; the Bar Committee, 1963/64; and Bar Manager, 1964-66. Ralph was also a first class referee.

Playing Season

The Team Captain, Brian Jackson, in his end of season report, said that 1966/67 was another successful season - most games which we lost were against combinations. The highlights of the season were the two games against H.M.S. Hermes, the Inter Unit 7's Championship, and the end of season tour by the Penguins. The only players that Brian mentioned were David Agar and Philip Parker for the number of points they scored, and Jack Handford for leading the team when he (Brian) was injured. Mention should also be made of Ted Platt, who, at the age of 43, played in practically every game during the two seasons 1964-66. Ted also Captained the side on the odd occasion. Two pupils of the SCS Tal Handaq, Brian Jackson and Ken Lawrence, are also worthy of mention. Brian played for Overseas for 4 seasons (1963-67) at scrum half, he also Captained the School XV for 2 seasons. Brian is no relation of Brian Jackson, Team Captain. Ken Lawrence played for Overseas for 3 seasons (1964-67) at centre and stand off. Ken was Vice-Captain of the School XV and Student Representative on Overseas General Committee. Both were selected for the full Malta XV for the match against the Penguins. The Cup for the Most Improved Player of the Year was won by John Hitt.

Overseas entered two teams in the Inter Unit Seven-a-side Rugby Championship played at the Marsa on Saturday, 25th February, 1967. Overseas 'A' lost to RAF Hawks 'A' in the final, 14 points to 5. Interesting details of the 7's issued by the Secetary of the Combined Services Malta Sports Board were as follows:

Penguins Tour Summary

62

  • a) Number of teams participated - 18
  • b) Total number of games played - 24
  • c) Duration of tournament (playing time) - 4 hours
  • d) Points scored in Cup Competition - 245 Pts
  • e) Points scored in Place Competition - 108 Pts
  • f) Total points scored during Tournament - 353 Pts
  • g) Total number of Referees who officiated - 7

The Penguins, as guests of the Overseas Club, toured Malta from the 5th to the 15th May, 1967, and proved to be very popular socially besides producing excellent rugby. I think that even Ben Bush would have learned some new songs. The Penguins played five matches in eleven days, won four, lost one and scored 119 points to 31. The R.A.F. were the only side to beat the Penguins. The last game, against a Malta XV produced the best rugby of the tour, with speedy passing and some excellent backing-up.

Results (Home team's score first)

  • Combined Services 0 - 14
  • Selected Overseas XV 12 - 38
  • Overseas 8 - 24
  • R.A.F. 11 - 13
  • Malta 0 - 34

The main burden of arranging the Penguin's tour was borne by Ted Platt, Overseas Hon. Secretary, Ted in turn stressed that without the considerable help of the Army, in the person of Major J. Bird, and the Air Force, represented by Fl. Lt. C. O'Regan, the visit would not have been the success it was.

Penguin players come from a fairly wide area of the southern half of England. On the occasion of their trip to Malta the party consisted of 17 players and officials led by their Fixture and Team Secretary, Tony Mason. A humorous situation developed during this season at the Marsa. At the beginning of the season the Overseas Hon. Secretary wrote to the St. John Ambulance Association asking for a qualified member to attend our games every Saturday afternoon. The St. John Ambulance member or members duly attended complete with all the necessary first aid equipment. What the member could not understand was, why, with all their training and experience, they were no match for the magic ...

The sponge. They ran onto the field as soon as they saw a body lying on the ground writhing in agony, only to find, that by the time they reached the spot, the body was back in the scrum. I say humorous, there is always a touch of humour about the magic sponge. This is not forgetting the gratitude the Club felt for the St. John Ambulance Association and the members, male and female, who so kindly turned out giving up their own time.

Once again, during the 1966/67 season, the Club tried to interest Maltese youth in the game of Rugby. A letter was written to the Hon. Secretary, Malta Secondary Schools Association asking him to circulate to all schools within his jurisdiction informing them that the Overseas Rugby Club would like to encourage the Maltese to play and asking anyone interested to get in touch with the Overseas Hon. Secretary. Unfortunately, there was no response.

SOCIAL EVENTS 1966/67

David Agar, Hon. Social Secretary, very quietly and very efficiently organised a highly successful social programme during the 1966/67 season. David left Malta at short notice during the summer of 1967 leaving no record of events. I do not think that the Club President, Mr. Peter Ratcliffe, will mind me quoting from his address.

"Our Social life, 1966/67, was left in the very capable hands of David Agar. Everyone will agree I know that David did a splendid job in organising our Film evenings - for which of course, we are permanently grateful to Jack Sharp, as well as for his continued interest and support. David also organised an excellent Cocktail Party at the Naval Base Officer's Club on the 30th January, 1967, when we acted as hosts to the other clubs, another cockers for the Penguins, for which Mr. and Mrs. Bill Woodley kindly lent us their splendid residence in Dockyard Terrace, several Hot-pots, including one when the Penguins were here, and finally the Annual Dinner Dance which went with a zip and at which I set a personal record in remaining almost sober for a change and not losing my specs. a splendid job by David."

The Annual Dinner Dance was held at the United Services Sports Club on Saturday, 29th April, 1967. Once again Hitty was Master of Ceremonies.

Brian Jackson took on the double role of Club Captain and Bar Manager and did the two jobs with a maximum of efficiency and a minimum of flap. One must also mention George Jackson, another character of this era. It was a little difficult to carry on a conversation with George as he had a strange dialect from north of the border and was slightly deaf. Nevertheless, nothing was too much trouble for George and Dorothy Jackson to do for the Club. Their son, Brian, as a pupil at SCS Tal Handaq, has already been mentioned under Playing Season. Finally, David Agar and Bill Woodley, by their efforts on the Social side, helped to make the Penguins Tour a success. The Club House remained open during the close season 1967.

The President, Mr. J.P. Ratcliffe, pointed out that although the rules stated that the A.G.M. be held in October, the present A.G.M. was being held earlier, as was intended by the previous amendment, concerning the ending of the financial year, carried at the A.G.M. 1966. The President asked members to accept this and that a resolution to alter the rules would be proposed at this A.G.M. Having the A.G.M. in September, instead of October, allowed the Team Captain, elected at the A.G.M., to start training earlier.

The following resolution to amend Rule 9 was proposed and passed:

 'Annual General Meeting to be held in September, and an Extra-ordinary Meeting to be held in April for submission of the playing season bar account to members and Joint Service Rugby Representatives. The financial year to end on the 31st March.'

HONORARY LIFE MEMBERS

Honorary Life Members of the Overseas R.U.F.C., which is an honour bestowed on members by direct voting at an A.G.M. in recognition of outstanding service to the Club, was initiated at the A.G.M., 1967. The first Life Members, Mr. J.A. Sharp and Mr. C.V. Morris, were made at this A.G.M. and to the present date only seven members have received this honour. I do not propose to give the individual service which each member gave to merit Life Membership, I think the granting of such an honour speaks for itself.

Following is a list of Members granted Honorary Life Membership:

A.G.M. NAME
1967 Mr. J.A. Sharp
Mr. C.V. Morris
1969 Mr. N.C. Morgan
Mr. J.D. Green
1970 Mr. J.P. Ratcliffe
1974 Mr. T.N. Ricketts
1976 Mr. D.J. Taylor

At this point I must remind readers that the first Honorary Life Memberships were granted whilst the Club was known as the Overseas R.U.F.C., hence the wording of the first paragraph under the heading 'Honorary Life Membership'. At the A.G.M. of 1973, when the Club became known as the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, the honours already granted were automatically transferred under the new name. Under both names special Membership Cards were printed.

PLAYING SEASON

The 1967/68 playing season proved to be one of the most outstanding in the Club's history. The 'Overseas' Tour to Messina was undoubtedly the highlight, followed closely by the Inter Service 7 a-side Competition, and the end of season tours to Malta by the R.A.F. Cyprus; Nomads (Tripoli); John Evans XV; and the return visit of Messina University. Overseas played 30 games, a record in one season, and scored 434 points to 193. The Team Captain, Brian Jackson, mentioned no particular player's prowess on the field, but he left a very comprehensive analysis of fixtures, player's appearances, and individual scores. He mentioned Jack Handford and David Brooks leading the forwards, and the general fitness of Overseas players, thanks to the excellent work of Trevor Ricketts on Thursday nights (Training sessions). A very thorough record of the Tour made by Overseas remains. 'Jacko' sums it up by saying, it was a very successful season.

On the 24th November, 1967, as Secretary, I wrote to the Sports Editor of the Sunday Telegraph, London, asking if it was possible for the results of our games to be printed in the Rugby Union results column of the Sunday Telegraph. On different occasions Overseas Committee members had been asked for this service by members returning to U.K. Our first reply from the Sports Editor said that this was not feasible as they could not give results which were received 2 days old, never mind a week. We then received agreement, that if we could get the

Tour to Messina

The Tour to Messina was arranged as a result of an article in 'Rugby World' describing the 'Penguins' tour to Malta in May the previous year. On reading this article the Secretary of Messina University Rugby Club, or to be correct, Centro Universitario Sportivo, Messina, Sicily, wrote to Overseas suggesting we visit Messina, and that they pay a return visit at a later date. The Centro Universitario Sportivo, known as CUS, had initially thought we were a Maltese Club. The Tour was agreed to, and on the 7th December, 1967, a Sub-Committee was formed to make arrangements.

Tour Sub-Committee

  • Chairman J.P. Ratcliffe
  • Secretary N.C. Morgan
  • Team Captain and B.S. Jackson
  • Team Secretary
  • Committee Member T.N. Ricketts

The Tour to Messina took place between the 1st and 5th January, 1968. For the crossing from Malta to Syracuse on board the Citta di Alessandria we had booked an 18 berth dormitory, just about the size of an average cabin, plus a 3 or 4 berth cabin. We had a bus waiting on the quayside to transport us the 93 miles to Messina where we were met at the Central Station by the CUS Secretary, Pino di Lorenzo. The hospitality of the Sicilians was tremendous. As guests in Student House, or Casa dello Studente, each member of our party had an individual bed sitter. Being the Christmas holiday period, all the students and staff were away on holiday, and so we were fed, at CUS expense, at a nearby cafe. At most meals we were joined by the CUS Secretary, or the CUS President, Piero Jacai. For one meal we were joined by the whole Sicilian team. On this occasion, helped by a liberal amount of wine, we finished the meal by singing rugby songs, English and Italian. Neither team understood the other team's songs, but if Italian rugby songs are like English rugby songs, and the 'entente cordiale' was such that it seemed certain they were, then I don't know why we were not thrown out of the cafe. However, everyone, including staff and passers-by enjoyed themselves.

In the evening of the first day we were entertained by Members of the University Rugby Club at their Club House, where we were presented with a Sicilian Carroza and plied with Asti Spumante and cake. The following morning we were given a pleasant reception at the main Messina University by the Rector, Il Magnifico Rettore, Professor Salvatore Pugliatti. All Overseas Members were given a commemorative medallion. The 4th January, being a free day, we went by bus with most of our hosts to Taormina.

The CUS rugby pitch, if one can describe it as such, was within the walls of the old 'Cittadella', which is situated near the harbour. The 'pitch' is best described in the Team Captain's words.

'One of the most memorable moments of the tour was undoubtedly our first glimpse of the 'pitch', as it came into view between the cranes and piles of rusting scrap metal which littered the Messina dockside. No-one could believe it! It was hope- fully stated that that must be their practice ground, until the coach pulled up outside dressing rooms which made the Marsa seem palatial and far- distant. We have been warned that the pitch was not in very good condition owing to the heavy rain, but the mud bath we had expected turned out to be a stretch of gravel half covered by large areas of standing water. Grey skies and persistent rain did not help to improve the picture. In fairness it should be stated, however, that Messina does have an adequate stadium, which unfortunately, and to our hosts' dismay, was unplayable because of the bad weather.'

We were beaten, just, in both games played. We had the obvious handicaps, such as the inability of some of the regular Overseas 1st team players to tour, the pitch, and perhaps, above all, the difference in interpretation of the rules by the Sicilians and ourselves. On the other hand we were up against a good team, continental style, with their forwards as ready to run with the ball as their threequarters. Throughout the first game it rained incessantly with an icy wind blowing straight down from the mountains. For the second game the weather was a little kinder, but still wet and windy with water lying over large areas of the gravel pitch. All Overseas team played well, with P. Parker; P. Miller; J. Handford; T. Ricketts and C. Rice being mentioned in the Captain's dispatches. Peter Parker received well earned praise in the local Messina press.

During both games, the Sicilian players arrived on and left the pitch with such startling rapidity that it seemed scarcely possible that they had only two substitutes. It is customary in Italy to allow two substitutes. On one occasion, during the first game whilst a line out was taking place, there were 19 Sicilians on the field, including the Referee and Trainer. Overseas players were tickled pink, they could scarcely believe it. Two games full of excitement.

Wednesday, 3rd January, 1968

CUS, Messina 13 (2 goals, 1 penalty)
Overseas R.U.F.C. 6 (tries: P. Parker, T. Nicholson)

Friday, 5th January, 1968

CUS, Messina 9 (1 try, 2 penalties)
Overseas R.U.F.C. 8 (tries: R. Squires, I. Dewar,
1 conversion by B. Jackson)

In the first game Brian Jackson badly grazed his rear quarters by sliding on the treacherous surface, very painful and very embarrassing. In spite of being in considerable pain Brian played in the second game, much to the relief of the team and selectors. Even with Brian we had only 17 players. The second game was marred by unfortunate injuries to Reg Squires, broken collar bone, and Mike Perkins, broken ankle. Though uncomfortable, they both made the journey back

with the party in the bus.

All members of the touring party thoroughly enjoyed the tour, the games, the hospitality, and the people. For the 3 days it was constantly raining or drizzling and we all returned to Malta with huge black umbrellas bought in Messina – a future symbol of our Tour status. Our President, Peter Ratcliffe, was henceforth known as 'Il Magnifico Presidente', and our battle cry for future games during that season at the Marsa was 'Forza' and 'Avanti'. Only Peter Ratcliffe and John Why could speak any Italian and we were constantly relying on their good offices. The total cost of the Tour to each member of the touring party was only £10.3s7d.

On the 24th February, 1968, Overseas entered two teams in the Inter Service 7 a-side competition. Overseas 'A' won the Cup and Overseas 'B' was runner-up in the Plate.

The first touring team of the season was the R.A.F. from Cyprus. In a game at the Marsa on the 25th February, 1968 we were beaten by 3 points to 23.

On the 5th April, 1968, an article in the Times of Malta stated that Malta's small rugby community was very fortunate to be able to close their 1967/68 season with the visit of 3 touring sides from 3 different countries.

The game against the Tripoli Nomads were played on No. 3 pitch, Marsa and those against the CUS and John Evans XV were played on the Stadium pitch, Marsa. Playing so late in the season presented difficulties with dry and hard grounds. Thanks must go to Mr. Hanlon, Sports Field, M.P.B.W., for caring for and constant watering of the pitches. The referees were provided by the Referees Panel, Malta, Secretary, Staff Sgt. W.J. Thomas.

The Nomads, R.F.C. from Tripoli, Libya (13 in party) stopped at St. Julians Hotel, Paceville, at their own expense. Overseas provided transport. The Tour was arranged for the Nomads, initially, by Secretary, Mr. D. Webb, and later arrangements by Secretary, Mr. R. Harrison. Unfortunately, 5 of their players were unable to make the tour due to Visa problems at the Tripoli end, and they were further handicapped by injury problems on the tour. F.O. L.C.V. Hill, Secretary R.A.F. (Malta) R.U., helped the tourists by providing players to complete their team. In spite of the high scores against them, in the words of the local correspondent in the Times of Malta, the Nomads provided fine sport and Bill Dunlop's Trojan efforts in their back row was the highlight of their play.

The Nomads were followed by the CUS, Messina, on the return visit (19 in party). CUS stopped at Mount St. Joseph House, Targa Gap, Mosta, with expenses paid by Overseas. Overseas provided transport. Like all rugby teams, CUS enjoyed life, and I think Father Dammairn, Principal of Mount St. Joseph House, was very understanding. The Sicilians played good rugby and this time, in two very exciting open games, the honours were even. Overseas tried, as far as possible, to play the same team as that which visited Messina. Looking back, Overseas/CUS tours and games proved a very interesting part of Overseas history.

Finally, we had the tour of John Evans' party from South

Wales. John, an Ex Overseas player, brought an exceptionally talented party of players, including Derek Morgan (England and Barbarians). This was a memorable tour. They were billeted at 234 Signal Squadron Mess, Lintorn Barracks, Floriana, by kind permission of Major Brian Woods, at a very moderate cost to the tourists. Arrangements for accommodation and transport were made by Capt. Mike Adams, Secretary, Army (Malta) R.U. In two extremely hard fought games the visitors remained undefeated. Both games were dominated by the outstanding play and leadership of Derek Morgan, who at times seemed to dictate events almost at will. The outstanding player for Overseas was 'Taffy' Grey, forward, who scored two tries. It was a fitting finale to an enjoyable season.

Arrangements were made by Mr. R. Squires, with the kind permission of Surgeon Captain McLintock, R.N., Royal Naval Hospital, Bighi, for members of the touring teams in Malta over the Easter period to be treated as out-patients and hospitalized in the R.N. Hospital. This service was free under a 'Grace and Favour' scheme.

And so ended perhaps the most memorable playing season of all. Amongst the memories of the normal Saturday and Sunday games, one thinks of two very pretty girls who took the oranges on at half time, Judith Cross and Maureen Jones, they too were part of this season. Also Arthur Cross who took his duties as Trainer on the afternoon of a game very seriously. The Cup for the 'Most Improved Player' was not presented for the 1967/68 season.

SOCIAL EVENTS 1967/68

The Social life of the Club during the 1967/68 season was very full and very successful. With three sides to entertain over the Easter period, a Sub-Committee was formed in January, 1968, to organize fund raising and entertainment. Initially, the Sub-Committee members were Messrs P. Parker(Chairman), B.S. Jackson; T.N. Ricketts; C. Rice and C. Brown. Unfortunately, Peter Parker was away from Malta for 7 weeks at the vital time and Colin Brown took over as Hon. Social Secretary and Chairman of the Sub-Committee.

Various functions were organized to raise cash. Members who made the trip to Messina were asked to pay £4. each into the Tour Fund. All members of the Club were asked to donate to the Tour Fund and their donations were added to a Subscription List. The General Committee agreed that the Overseas Club should pay up to £100 towards tour expenses, and that any excess in fund raising to be kept in reserve for future tours.

The hard work by Colin Brown and his Sub-Committee, Social and General Committees, and the response to all appeals and functions organized by the Committees was tremendous and helped to assure the success of the Tours to Malta. Quoting from the President, Mr. J.P. Ratcliffe, 'Of course, tours of this kind cannot exist without organization, and here I would like to put on record my very sincere thanks to those members of the Committee who gave up so much of their time to help. Our Secretary, Norman Morgan, who organized both our trips to Sicily and the return visits. The Special Social Committee of Colin Brown, Trevor Ricketts, Charlie Rice, and Bar Manager,

Brian Jackson, did a remarkable job of fund raising between Christmas and Easter. Without all this work and goodwill, the tours would not just have been flops - they would have been impossible.

A very unexpected but welcome guest arrived at the Cocktail Party held at Brian Jackson's house. The irrepressible John Evans, and I believe Jacko, together with other members of both 'teams', met Len Hutton and his wife somewhere 'about town'. They were on holiday in Malta. Such an important sportsman had to be invited.

Overseas members of the 1967/68 season will long remember it for the rugby provided, Tours, and the first class Social life. For myself, I regret to say, I left Malta on the 8th July, 1968.

In accordance with the fact that Overseas no longer made payments from the Bar profits to the three Services, Rule 9 was amended as follows, leaving out any reference to the Services and stating only the month in which the A.G.M. is to be held and the date of the financial year ending.

'Rule 9. The Annual General Meeting to be held in September and the financial year to end on the 31st August.'

The playing season of 1968/69 was a success. The Team Captain, Roy Ravenscroft, left Malta before the end of the season and the report was given by the Vice-Captain, Jack Handford. This makes interesting reading and I quote,

"The number of points scored '477' is a Club record, but balanced against this the number of points scored against '242' is also a record." (This does not include the game against the Army (Cyprus) on the 19th January, 1969, which Overseas won 11 points to 6.)

"The R.A.F. side, known as the Hawks, were once again our bogey team and they beat us on 3 occasions. Other defeats were recorded against John Evans XV and R.A.F. College Cranwell (two touring sides). H.M.S. Fearless, Army Malta and the two regiments, although we beat the latter in return matches later in the season. Most notable of our wins were those mentioned.

against the two regiments and R.A.F. Malta.

The 7-a-sides were a disgrace. Probably fielding the strongest seven in the competition on paper, both our sides were defeated in the first round. In the Plate the 'A' team could only attain runners up, while the 'B' team once again went out in the first round.

With regard to the players, probably our biggest headache was in replacing 'the Boot' Jackson who, through a knee injury, only made 9 appearances. However, we were fortunate in having a long haired, bearded, at that time, University lecturer who showed us that he could kick. He is, of course, Charlie Rice and he finished up the season with 121 points. Peter Miller was leading try scorer once again.

The pre season training at the Marsa and at Tal Handaq started off on the 17th September, 1968. The main feature of the season was the number of sides touring Malta, including our friends Tripoli (Libya) Nomads and John Evans XV. Investigations made into the possibility of Overseas touring Naples, Sicily or N. Africa came to nought. Unfortunately, we had to turn down an offer from Rugby Reggio to take part in a tournament because the dates were unsuitable for Overseas.

Their Manager was, of course, John Evans, ex Overseas player, with Assistant Manager, P.R.V. Sinden, ex Durham Medicals. The team was Captained by W.G.D. Morgan. (Malta) and Overseas XV'S, also to take part in the aforementioned Sevens.

SOCIAL EVENTS 1968/69

With three Touring sides visiting Malta during the season there must have been a fair amount of social activity arranged. This is borne by the fact that Mr. P. Ratcliffe, President, when thanking Colin Brown, Social Secretary, and the Social Committee, for their efforts, remarked that it had been an excellent year. However, except for a Hot Pot Supper and a farewell Cocktail Party at Brian Jackson's residence, both organised for John Evans touring party, very little is recorded.

Once again, the film evenings were the mainstay, with all films and equipment provided by Jack Sharp. All Thursday Club Evenings were well attended.

The Annual Dinner Dance was held on the 29th March, 1969, at the United Services Sports Club, Marsa. This proved to be a most successful occasion. A loss of £4, claimed at the time to be the smallest loss on any Club Dinner Dance ever recorded, was a good effort as a total of £22 was spent on tickets for Official guests.

The Club House remained open during the close season.

W.O. W. ThomasArmy

Social Committee

Messrs. C. Charlton (Secretary); M. Farnan; J. Why; R. Walker; H. Fudge; D. Davies and B. Lloyd.

Club Bar Helpers

Messrs. R. Daley (Manager); B. Jackson; R. Walker; R. Nicol; M. Farnan; P. Henshall and D. Davies

The President, Mr. J.P. Ratcliffe, in his address thanked the three Services, placing on record the fact that without them we would have no Club House, no pitch, no referees, no opposition, no Rugby, and therefore no Overseas. In other words we would cease to exist. Over the years, since the inception of the Club, this Statement has remained mostly true, and the fact that in this situation we have remained a completely 'Civilian' Club, and I believe, the centre of Rugby in Malta, is unique. Ratty could have said that we have relied on Service personnel joining the Club as 'Civilians' for a fair percentage of our players, in varying degrees, over the years. It must be said that we have not always relied on the Services for a Club House, we have provided the occasional 'Civilian' referees, and the only non Service opposition has been the odd touring team.

The President also commented on the fact that although we had heard nothing official, it was rumoured that part or the whole of the Marsa grounds may be returned to the Malta Government. This included our Club House at the Marsa. Apparently these rumours came from various press reports. This fortunately did not happen until after the withdrawal of the

British Services in 1972.

Peter Ratcliffe resigned from office on the 27th April, 1970, after 4 years as a very popular and hard working President, and finally left Malta in July, 1970. Ratty had been a member of 'Seas since 1961. Besides his term as President, he had been Vice-President for 2 years, 1964-66, on the Selection Committee, 1965-69, and also served on the Social Committee, 1962/63. I will always remember Ratty as 'Il Magnifico Presidente' on Overseas' Tour to Messina, Sicily, in January, 1968.

One must also mention Brian Jackson who left Malta in July, 1970, after being a playing member of 'Seas since 1964. Jacko was Team Captain/Team Secretary for 2 years, 1966-68, Club House/Bar Manager for 3 years, 1966-69, and for good measure served as an ordinary member of the Bar Committee, 1965/66, and the Social Committee for 3 years, 1966-69. I have already written about his prowess on the field - his record of points scored in one season for Overseas (187) has never been beaten.

Ratty and Jacko were two 'Characters', the kind of people a Club revolves round and finds hard to replace.

PLAYING SEASON

The playing season started on the 18th October with a game against the old enemy, the Nomads, a team formed from Army small units. Up to February, Overseas had very poor results, winning 4 games out of 16, and beating only 2 sides, Nomads (3 times) and the 1 Lancs Regt. From February to April it was a different story, we won 7 games out of 9, including victories over the Army (Malta), John Evans XV and HMS Hermes.

The outstanding features of this season was the efforts made by Mr. A. Bragger, Overseas Tours Secretary, and the Committee under President Peter Ratcliffe and Hon. Secretary, Trevor Ricketts, to take Overseas on tour and to attract tourists to Malta. Unfortunately, with little success. Mr. Bragger wrote to Clubs at Reggio and Tripoli, also Universities at Messina, Catania and Palermo, asking for home and away fixtures. Attempts were made to attract Petersham Rugby Club, Australia, via a contact in U.K., Clifton RUFC, England, and a French team from near Paris, to tour Malta.

Petersham Rugby Club was on a World Tour but it turned out that Malta was not one of their ports of call. The French team, under Philippe Dorsemain, wished to visit Malta for one week between the 20th March and the 4th April, 1970, and it would appear that difficulty in arranging accommodation in Malta, leaving little time to arrange the tour, was the main reason why it was called off. Philippe had been an Overseas player for at least 2 years, approximately 1965-67. Clifton RUFC showed interest in visiting Malta and it would appear that lack of communication resulted in disappointment. We actually received an invitation from Catania for Overseas to go on tour at Easter only to have to call it off through lack of support from Overseas players.

In spite of all the hard work, the only team to visit Malta, as a result of arrangements made by Overseas Committee, was John...

Evans XV from S. Wales on their third tour. During their short tour, 25th to 31st March, 1970, they played against Overseas and also against the Combined Services. Once again they were accommodated in Lintorn Barracks, by kind permission of the Army (Malta) authorities. There is no record of the names of players and officials included in the party, although one must assume that they were not quite as strong as in their previous two tours as Overseas beat them 18 - 15. The Tour was a great success.

The other touring teams, Army (Cyprus) who remained unbeaten during their short tour, R.A.F. (Cyprus), and the R.A.F. Training College, Cranwell, (Sleaford, Lincs.) were arranged by the Services.

Touring Teams
Army (Cyprus) 21st to 28th November, 1969
R.A.F. Cranwell 29th December 1969, to 2nd January, 1970
R.A.F. (Cyprus) Approximately, 21st February, 1970
John Evans XV 26th to 31st March, 1970

Overseas entered the Inter Service 7's on the 14th March, 1970. No record remains of the results.

Several players who had been Overseas stalwarts for a number of years left Malta at the end of the season. These included John Why; Peter Henshall; Eddie McClure and Adrian Wirth. The Cup for the 'Most Improved Player' of the year was won by Mr. M. Farman.

SOCIAL EVENTS 1969/70

Mr. T.N. Ricketts, Hon. Secretary, reporting in the absence of Mr. C. Charlton (returned to U.K. in July, 1970) said that the Social Life of the Club was not as successful as previous year, the exception being the Annual Dinner Dance, which he described as the 'best we have ever had'.

The only other function reported was a Hot Pot organised at the Club House for John Evans party in March.

The Annual Dinner Dance was held at the Marsa (USSC) on the 17th April, 1970. This was a very enjoyable night, just over 100 attending. The arrangements were made by Mr. Charlton.

The Club House was closed during the month of August.

Playing Season

The President, Jim Christie, and the Team Captain, Mike Pearey, both stated that 1970/71 was a most successful season, and that we were, throughout the whole season, the best team on the Island. This was in spite of the fact that we were desperately short of players, we were plagued by injuries, and we lost three of our key players in January. In February we were down to 16 playing members. Jim Christie summed it up when he stated, "The Rugby team under Mike Pearey had a successful season, and his experience, tactics, and sense of discipline, were reflected on the field of play." Unfortunately, for Overseas, Mike Pearey left Malta at the end of the 1970/71 playing season. Mike represented the Royal Navy on the R.F.U. Committee and before leaving Malta he had been appointed to sit on the RFU Sub-Committee on laws.

Training started on the 1st October, 1970, at Tal Handak under the direction of Trevor Ricketts, and the first game of the season was on the 24th October against HMS Ark Royal. At the start of the season 22 players were in regular training. Wednesday and Saturday were ball training sessions, with Thursday evening being fitness training. As far as I know, this is the only season in the Club's history that such strict training has been carried out. I was told that on one occasion Charlie Rice was dropped for not attending training, this says a lot for Captain and players and it reflected on the Club's

record for the season, losing only once to a resident team,
the R.A.F. and we in turn defeated them twice.

The Team Captain in his end of season report mentioned
only one player. He described Derek Kiddle, from a Captain's
point of view, as the ideal player, never missing a training
session or a game, always on good time, and always going hard.
The President, when particularly referring to people leaving,
mentioned B. Jackson, a grand stalwart of all sports and of
the Overseas Club, Peter Miller, whose forceful runs down the
touchline thrilled all, and Derek Kiddle, who tackled all he did
with the utmost vigour, whether on the field or in the Club. John
Symes won the Cup for the 'Most Improved Player' of the year.

For the fourth successive year John Evans brought a touring
party to Malta from South Wales, on this occasion from the 8th
to 14th April, 1971. This time, due to the rundown of the
Services, the Army (Malta) authorities did not give permission
for them to be accommodated in the Services Transit Accommodation
Lintorn Barracks, Floriana. The party of 20 booked themselves
into flats. John Evans XV played against Overseas on Saturday,
10th April, and against the Combined Services on Monday, 12th
April. No record remains of the names of players and officials
in the party, or of the results and scores. Only because the
teams which Overseas lost to during the season were named, do
I know that Overseas were victors in the Overseas/John Evans
XV game. In spite of this, John Evans spoke of it as being an
excellent tour. This was the last tour that John Evans' party
made to Malta. During their four tours they made a great
contribution to rugby on the Island, they played magnificent
entertaining rugby, and Overseas has much to thank them for,
particularly John Evans.

The Army (Cyprus) under Major P. Winchcombe, R.E.M.E.,
toured Malta in December, 1970 playing against Overseas on
5th December. The RAF (Cyprus) toured Malta in January, 1971,
playing against Overseas on the 30th January. Overseas lost
to the Army 17 points to 0, and the R.A.F. 30 points to 0.

The Tours Secretary, Eddie McClure, also carried out
correspondence with Clifton RUFC, and the Secretary or Manager
of the Paris Team, Didier Borsenaz, brother of Phillipe,
former Overseas Player. Both these teams expressed a wish
to tour Malta at Easter, 1972, and it was proposed by Overseas
Committee to hold a Rugby Festival over the period covered
by their intended visits. John Evans also expressed a wish to
take part in the Festival. It was further proposed that a
Committee, consisting of two Overseas Members, T.N. Ricketts,
and W. Lewis, and three other Members, one from each of the
Services, be formed to prepare the Festival. Major R. Hurley,
Chairman Army RU(Malta), agreed that this was an excellent
proposal and stated that he would suggest at the following
Committee Meeting of the Inter Service Rugby Union (Malta)
that it be accepted. This was not to be. With the with-
drawal of the British Forces in January, 1972, and the consequent
temporary disbandment of Overseas RUFC, no rugby was played on
the Island during the second half of season 1971/72.

On the 20th March, 1971, an Overseas Team, under the
Captaincy of Ralph D'Oley, convincingly won the Inter Service 7's
Competition. The following results show just how good and
fit Overseas players were:-

SOCIAL EVENTS 1970/71

Once again the films provided by Jack Sharp proved to be the mainstay of the Club's Social life during the season. Film evening took place at the Club House once or twice a month. Two Cheese and Wine Parties were held. The first on Wednesday, 18th November, 1970, held mainly for the RAF and HMS Ark Royal. The attendance was very poor, only 10 full members being present. The second on Thursday, 8th April, 1971, held for John Evans Touring Party, was a success. A Hot Pot was provided for the Army (Cyprus) Touring side.

In November, 1970, the Inter Service R.U., Malta, asked the Overseas Committee to make a grant to the Inter Services (Malta) to help cover the cost of entertainment of visiting teams etc.. Their point of view was that Overseas Rugby Club had the benefits of a Service maintained ground and Club House, also that with the rundown of the Services there was very little money available for allocation to rugby from Service non-public funds in Malta. The Army, for example, had only £200 to cover all sports for a full year. At a meeting held in January, 1971, Overseas Committee agreed that, of the expenses incurred by the Malta XV's which could not be met by any other means, one third would be paid by the Overseas Club, the Club's contribution for entertainment of any one team team not to exceed four pounds.

The Annual Dinner Dance was held at the United Services Sports Club on the 23rd April, 1971. In spite of the fact that the total Membership was stated in Committee on the 18th February, 1971, as being as low as 44, the dance was attended by 147 paying guests, and proclaimed to be a tremendous success. The dance was organised by Mr. R. Walker and Committee, and for the second year in succession, Trevor Ricketts acted as Master of Ceremonies.

PLAYING SEASON

In spite of the political clouds on the horizon, the 1971/72 season started off normally. Training started on the 30th September with circuit training in the gymnasium at Tel Handaq School under the supervision of Trev Ricketts.

From the start there was a shortage of playing members, and although the Team Captain, Dave Taylor, believed that we had a reasonably competent side, there was, on the occasion, difficulty in raising a side. Lack of interest in training did not help. The two combined led to a number of defeats in the short lived season. It was not until the 18th December that the Captain said in Committee that "Last Saturday's win" had shown a strong change in fortunes. This must have referred to a game in which Overseas beat RAF 1st side 78 points to nil. Dave Taylor scored 4 tries. In all 14 tries were scored, 11 of which were converted by Charlie Rice. Unfortunately, there is not a complete list of games played and results. I believe approximately 6 games were played before the withdrawal.

The points value of a try was increased this season from 3 to 4. No rugby took place in Malta during the second half of the season. This put paid to the plans ahead for the Rugby Festival which was to have taken place during Easter period 1972.

WITHDRAWAL OF BRITISH FORCES IN JANUARY, 1972, AND CONSEQUENT TEMPORARY DISBANDMENT OF OVERSEAS R.U.F.C.

The possibility that Overseas might have to fold up due to the political situation was first discussed by members at the Annual General Meeting, 1971. The President, Jim Christie, asked members to forward to the Committee, any ideas they might have for dealing with the Club's finances if this should occur. At this same meeting, the Committee was empowered, in the event of no such ideas being forthcoming from members, by the November Committee Meeting, to put forward suggestions themselves.

On the 18th November, having received no written proposals from members, the Committee discussed several methods of dealing with the Club's finances, including the idea of sponsoring a Cup or Competition so that the name of the Club would live on. It was agreed, "That, in the event of the Club winding up, the Committee in office at that time should be given authority to use any surplus funds in the furtherance of the name of Overseas R.U.F.C., Malta, bearing in mind the possible continuance of the Club in some subsectional form".

The blow came on the 29th December, 1971, when a deadlock was reached in the financial negotiations between Britain and Malta, and Britain prepared to withdraw the British Forces from Malta. An Extra-ordinary Committee Meeting of the Overseas R.U.F.C. was held at the Club House, Marsa Lodge, on the 30th December. Present were: Messrs. M. Holt; J. Alderson; D. Taylor; A. Phillips; H. Handford; T. Ricketts; M. Lewis and H. Harris. At this point it was almost certain that the Club would have to be disbanded and plans were made accordingly. This was the last meeting of an Overseas Committee at Marsa Lodge. It was then decided to contact Cdr. Mike Pearey, R.N., Overseas Team Captain 1970/71, and now serving on the R.F.U. Sub-Committee on Laws, with the view to purchasing two trophies to be used for competition at U/15 U/19 Schoolboy International level. Mike Pearey was asked to contact the R.F.U. to ascertain the possibility of such a competition. Arrangements were made to withdraw money from the bank and given to Lt. A. Phillips, R.N. to hold for this purpose. Arrangements were made for the books to be audited and for Mr. F. Kitson to take care of the Secretary's books. It was decided to give a gratuity of £25 to Angelo, Bar Steward. Finally, a Full Meeting of the Club was arranged for the 6th January, 1972, the Secretary to inform as many people as possible in the circumstances. This was not to be.

Although the Malta Government, on the 1st January, extended its deadline for the withdrawal of British troops by a fortnight, the evacuation of families of British Services started on the 7th January. On the 15th January the Malta Government lifted its ultimatum for evacuation of British troops, but by this time the evacuation of families and U.K. Based Civilians was complete and only a nucleus of necessary Military remained.

As from the Overseas Meeting on the 30th December, the affairs of the Club were left in the very capable hands of 6 Officials, namely, the President, Jim Christie, The Secretary, Trevor Ricketts, Jack Sharp, Frank Kitson, Mike Pearey and Arthur Phillips. One must remember that at the time of the

87

withdrawal it was presumed that the disbandment of the Club was final. Remaining in Malta, Jim Christie, Arthur Phillips, and Jack Sharp, arranged settling of the Club's affairs, including the withdrawal of monies from the bank and sending of same to Mike Pearey for re-banking in U.K. Frank Kitson held the Secretary's books for future reference. Mike Pearey in the U.K. acted as contact between Overseas R.U.F.C. and R.F.U. Trevor Ricketts returned to U.K. and from his home continued to carry out the Secretary's duties and co-ordinated all arrangements by the different interested parties in Malta and the United Kingdom.

On behalf of the Overseas Club, Mike Pearey approached the R.F.U. to find out their reaction to Overseas offering two trophies as awards for the winning international sides in the Schoolboy’s Championships at under 19 and under 15 level. In fact, Mike forwarded Trevor’s letter to this effect to the R.F.U. In reply, on the 24th January, 1972, Mr. Prescott, R.F.U. Secretary, said that both he and the President of the Rugby Union, Dr. T.A. Kemp, felt that trophies were a problem in themselves, more so when schools sides from year to year, owing no allegiance to any particular school, would have custody. Also, equally, problems of transport and insurance could present difficulties. Mr. Prescott suggested that the Overseas funds might be passed into a Centenary Youth Trust which was then being created and perhaps preferably utilised in some tangible and visible way at Twickenham to commemorate Overseas Club. Before it was decided one way or another the political scene suggested that Overseas might be resurrected. Mr. Prescott received this news with great satisfaction, hoping that Overseas would be revived and continue to prosper and flourish. He also said how our original offer had been appreciated.

Arthur Phillips and Jim Christie closed the bank account, settled outstanding bills, and on the 17th March, Arthur Phillips sent the balance to Mike Pearey.

On the 26th March, after protracted negotiations in London, Rome and Malta, a 7 year Defence Agreement was signed in London between the British and Malta Governments. From the 14th April, British Service personnel gradually started returning to the Island. In a letter to Jim Christie on the 16th April, Trevor Ricketts said, "It would appear that Overseas will be reborn in the not-too-distant future."

On the 5th June, Mike Pearey wrote to Trevor informing him that he had invested the Overseas Rugby Funds in the National Savings Bank. £50 in an ordinary account and £223 in an investment account at 7.5%. In Mike’s words, the money was safe, could be withdrawn at one month’s notice and the National Savings Bank gave a reasonable dividend.

In July, 1972, Trevor duly returned to Malta and immediately started picking up the debris and rebuilding Overseas. Arthur Phillips had in the meantime returned to U.K., but most of the Committee elected at the previous A.G.M. had either remained in or returned to Malta. A Steering Committee was held at 13, Zachary Street, Valletta, on the 21st September, 1972. Present were: Messrs J. Christie; T. Ricketts; J. Sharp; R. Daley; M. Lewis; D. Taylor; F. Kitson; and J. Handford.

From this point I will leave the telling of the rebuilding of the Club to its proper place, i.e. the 1972/73 season. However, the sterling work done by the previously mentioned Officials must be mentioned. From the last meeting prior to the withdrawal these men had worked continuously looking after the Club affairs in Malta and U.K. The Committee elected at the 1971 A.G.M. more than kept faith with the members who elected them. If one person can be singled out, it is Trevor Ricketts who co-ordinated all efforts and without whose tenacity, singleness of purpose, and love of the Overseas Club, the Club might not have been rebuilt, at least for the start of the 1972/73 season.

SOCIAL EVENTS 1971/72

With the shortened season there is little to report in the social life of the Club. The one event reported, a disco evening, was not a success through lack of interest. The monthly film evenings took place. The one reported success was the Children's Christmas party.

1972/73

REFORMATION OF OVERSEAS R.U.F.C.

As mentioned previously, a Steering Meeting of members who had been elected at the A.G.M. 1971, was held at the Malta United Film Corporation Offices, Zachary Street, Valletta, on the 21st September, 1972. Present were: Messrs J. Christie; T. Ricketts; J. Sharp; R. Daley; M. Lewis; D. Taylor; F. Kitson and J. Handford. This was the initial meeting to determine the possibility of the rebirth of the Club. Mr. Christie was able to inform members of this Committee that he and Mr. Sharp had visited Dr. B. Camilleri, the Malta Government Minister in Charge of the Marsa Grounds, and permission had been given for Overseas to use a pitch at the Marsa, complete with 2 changing rooms and bar facilities after the game. From this it will be appreciated that the situation as regards Club House, grounds and changing rooms had changed completely. Prior to the withdrawal, the Marsa Sports Grounds area, including Marsa Lodge, came under the jurisdiction of the British Army Authorities.

Now, however, the whole area came under direct control of the Malta Sports Board, a department of the Malta Government. At this Steering Committee Meeting it was decided to invite the Service Representatives to a 'discussion' on Rugby on the Island, also to hold an Inaugural Meeting for all ex-members and potential new members.

The informal Meeting of Overseas Committee and Service Representatives took place at the N.U.T.C offices on the 5th October, 1972. The Inaugural Meeting took place at the Malta Sports Club, previously known as the United Services Sports Club, on the 19th October. At the Inaugural Meeting it was formally decided that the Club should be reformed under the same constitution as that in force prior to the enforced disbandment. It was also decided that all Officials elected at the 1971 A.G.M. should continue in Office until the next A.G.M.

The Rules of the Club, as at the time of the withdrawal, were adopted. Following the adoption of the Rules, Rule 13 was amended to raise the Membership Fees to £M1 for Playing Members and Social Members, and to 50cents for Student Members. Also, Rule 2 was amended to change the word 'Rugger' to 'Rugby'.

It must be pointed out at this stage that as from the 16th May, 1972, the currency in Malta went decimal. Cents and mils replaced the old shillings and pence.

PLAYING SEASON

The season started off quietly from the playing point of view, with problems of playing strength and servicing of the pitch. By January we had a good reserve strength and the playing standard had improved. Finally, at the end of the season, the Team Captain, Mr. N. Armstrong, was able to report that we had the best standard on the Island. In his own words, "all in all it had been a tremendous and extremely successful season."

The team strength was built round the Captain, playing at hooker, and Jim Glover, playing at stand-off. Jim Glover, ex Oxford University Team Captain, Cornwall county player and Barbarian, could dictate play and looked as good as his impressive record. Ably assisted by Charlie Rice, Brendan Cradden and Christopher Medlicott, Overseas played an open game.

The problems of servicing the pitch were gradually overcome. Prior to the withdrawal we had relied on the Services to look after the pitch, now we found that the problem was ours. As a Civilian Club, through the efforts of Jack Sharp and Bill Christie, the President of the Malta Sports Board, Dr. E. Camilleri, had given us permission to use the pitches at the Marsa, but we were expected to look after them ourselves. At the beginning of the season, the groundsman employed by the M.S.B., Mr. Selvul Busuttil, had employed outside labour to prepare the pitch. Overseas Committee appointed Mr. F. Kitson to act as liaison between the groundsman and the Club. Through the good offices of Lt. Cdr. J. Harrell and Lt. J. Lunn we were able to use the Navy marker and creosote.
Mr. D. Taylor took over the task of looking after the pitch.

The highlight of the season was the defeat of HMS ARK Royal. An Overseas '7' was beaten in the final of the Inter

91

Service Sevens Tournament on the 8th April, 1973.

During the season the old problem was discussed yet again, whether to play our games on Saturdays or Sundays. Whereas Saturday games were better from the spectator point of view, we could field a stronger team on a Sunday. It was decided to accept fixtures whenever available.

The Cup for the 'Most Improved Player of the Year' was awarded to Peter Jeornig.

PLAYING RECORD FOR 1972/73

P22 – W15 – D1 – L6    Points for 401    Against 170

CLUB HOUSE – 21, FLAGSTONE WHARF, MARSA

As has already been mentioned, Marsa Lodge, our old Club House, now came under direct control of the Malta Sports Board. Consequently, the Club rooms and Bar were lost to the Overseas R.U.F.C. Although both the Malta Sports Board and the Malta Sports Club were approached for temporary facilities, an immediate search was made for a permanent Club House.

Thanks to the Team Captain, Mr. N. Armstrong, we were not long without a home. Mr. Armstrong, the General Manager of Andrews Feeds Malta Limited, obtained permission from his Directors for Overseas to use premises belonging to the firm at 21, Flagstone Wharf, Marsa. The premises consisted of 2 adjoining rooms above a warehouse, the main drawback being that it was situated approximately three quarters of a mile from the playing field.

Thanks again to the directors of Andrews Feeds and to Mr. Armstrong, a bar was built in the inner room and a loan was forthcoming to buy a stock of beer. Tables and chairs were obtained from the Services. The grand opening was on Sunday, 17th December, 1972, after the game at the Marsa versus HMS Fife.

Mr. Armstrong, as Bar/Club House Manager, immediately registered the Club with the Malta Police and applied for a licence. This was no easy matter. First, a number of additions to the Club Rules were necessary, all appertaining to Membership. In the hopes of speeding up the issue of a licence, in spite of the fact that the existing Club Rules stated that Rules could only be amended at an A.G.M., the Committee adopted the additional rules on the 8th March, 1973. The additional rules, 16 to 18, were accepted by the Members at the A.G.M., 1973. Also, during the 1972/3 season, the Malta Police checked past and present Membership lists.

At the beginning of the 1973/74 season, members were asked by the Police Authorities to report to the Police Station in their area, and confirm that they were bonafide members of the Overseas R.U.F.C. This proved impracticable. The Police Officials at these Police Stations knew little or nothing about the situation, also the Police had difficulty in contacting members.

In February, 1974, members were asked to sign a form declaring that they were fully paid-up members and finally, in April, 1974 the Police issued the Club with a licence.

From the outset, the building and all items within were insured by Andrews Feeds. In April, 1974, an incident in which water was left running within the Club, and which seeped through into the warehouse below, involved insurance claims which Andrews Feeds dealt with. After this incident, Mr. D. Taylor, Overseas Treasurer, inquired into the necessity of Overseas taking out a separate insurance, only to be told that a blanket insurance was held by Andrews Feeds Malta Ltd.

When Overseas R.U.F.C. became Overseas Rugby and Sports Club in September, 1973, Mr. Armstrong believed we should look into the possibility of purchasing our own premises. Because of the political situation the Committee were against purchasing a property, and in November, 1973, Mr. Armstrong was asked to approach his Company with the view to a long-term rental, depending on Police permission. Fortunately, or unfortunately, the Directors of the Company were against this, but, they had no objection to some form of redecoration under Mr. Armstrong's control. However, before this, was carried out another problem arose. Mr. Armstrong reported that there was a possibility of the area in front of the Club House being turned into a dry-dock with consequential difficulties in approaching the Club House entrance. Once again Mr. Sharp came to the rescue. In an interview with Mr. I. Sant, Minister of Public Buildings & Works, Mr. Sharp was informed that the dry-docks were only in the planning stage and that it would be some time before the scheme affected us. With this assurance, the work went ahead. On the 22nd November, 1973, a Sub-Committee was formed, comprising of Mr. C. C. Fox (Chairman); Mr Armstrong and Mr R. Ward, to deal with redecoration. Mr. Ward, Hockey Section Captain, advised on possible designs. On the 22nd February 1974, with the expert advice of the firm's architect workmen from Andrews Feeds and the R.U.S.C. widened the opening between the two rooms by means of an archway. A number of Club members volunteered their assistance. The alteration and redecoration were completed by the 31st March, 1974.

During December, 1974, the Club House was again re-decorated, this time under a Sub-Committee comprising of Messrs. A. Armstrong, J. Masuero, H. Crossfield and B. Jones. The General Committee authorized that £50 be spent on soft furnishings and decoration. In January, 1975, curtains, tables and chairs were purchased, and at long last the Club House was complete. Again a number of members volunteered their assistance.

Niall Armstrong left Malta in October, 1975. It is thanks to Niall's unceasing effort that the Club, in the first place, received permission from the Directors of Andrews Feeds to use the premises, and later received permission to alter them structurally. It is also thanks to Niall and Jack Sharp for overcoming the problems of obtaining the Police Licence and carrying out alterations.

Finally, at the beginning of the 1975/76 season, the Bar/ Club House Manager, Mr. H. Crossfield, and the Social Secretary, Mr. J. Hughes with the help of other members, gave the Club House another face lift.
