SOCIAL EVENTS 1972/73

Except for the Annual Dinner Dance, held at the New Villa Rosa, St. George's Bay, on the 5th May, 1973, the only social events of the season were the film evenings at the Club House.

The film evenings starting on the 8th February proved a success and a good source of revenue at the bar. Once again all the equipment and films were provided by Jack Sharp.

The Annual Dinner Dance, although financially a failure, was an enjoyable event, in pleasant surroundings.

The Club House closed during the summer months.

PART III

1973/74

'OVERSEAS' BECOMES A RUGBY AND SPORTS CLUB

Annual General Meeting, 21, Flagstone Wharf, Marsa, 20th September, 1973.

At this meeting members were asked to vote on perhaps the most controversial issue in the history of the Club. A motion was put forward to change the rules of the Club, a motion which was to change the structure of the Club completely. It was, in effect, to change the name of the Club from Overseas Rugby Union Football Club to Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, for the affairs of the Club to be run by a General Committee, and for the Club to embrace not only rugby and cricket as sections of the Club, but any other sporting factions who applied to become part of the Club and could satisfy the General Committee as to their viability.

The resolution was put forward by Mr. T.N. Ricketts and seconded by Mr. C. Rice. In Mr. Ricketts' own words, "The amalgamation of the other sports clubs with the Club would not take away the name of Overseas R.U.F.C., but would try to bring under one roof all finances for the betterment of sport in Malta in general. Many people were paying out two or three lots of fees in order to belong to these clubs. The financial position of the Club would be improved. The bar would be open more therefore increasing the bar profits. Social functions would improve and the name of Overseas would be perpetuated by many Clubs. The identity of the Rugby section would not be lost as it would bring all sportsmen together."

The basic idea behind the proposal was good. On an Island as small as Malta, a number of men were playing 2 or 3 different sports over each weekend, particularly during the winter season, and also, as has been stated, paying subscriptions to each sport. The same men were mostly from the comparatively small band of U.K. Based Civilians and Service Units, and so they not only met on the field but at many social functions as well. Very naturally, a number of rugby 'Die-hards' who had put a great deal into the Club, some over a number of years, had no wish to see, nor could they see the need of, other sports being amalgamated in the Club. Also, one must not forget that the Club funds had been hard won by these same rugby players at functions and over the bar. There was a genuine fear that these funds could be used to subsidize other sports.

Mr. Ricketts answered all questions put to him, as regards the intentions behind the resolution, with sufficient clearness to ease most members' minds. Most points raised were covered in the rules as proposed in the resolution. He said that up to that time all Clubs (Soccer and Hockey) had been self supporting and therefore, after inclusion within our umbrella, all sections would again be expected to be self supporting. The initial Committee would consider each Section's financial needs at the start of each season. Any grant given to a section at the start of a season must be repaid. Mr. Ricketts also said that there was nothing in the rules against lady members, a ladies team could join under the same conditions.

95

At this point I would mention that Club membership has always been open to lady members, although, in general, they have not been encouraged. My wife, Amy, is very proud of having been the first Lady Member of the Club, at least to be issued with a Membership Card, in 1958. Also, as previously mentioned in this history, Mrs. M. Rushworth and Mrs. N. Polkinghorne were Committee Members in years 1958-60, and Mrs. Rushworth was elected Hon. Social Secretary at the A.G.M. 1959.

The proposed rules were based on the existing rules, plus the rules previously mentioned, as required by the Malta Police Licensing Authorities, appertaining to Membership. Amendments had been made to the resolution, prior to being put to the members, particularly as regards keeping the word 'Rugby' in the name of the Club, and the following motions were put to the Members.

MOTION 1: That the Club Rules be changed to the following:-
RULES OF THE OVERSEAS RUGBY AND SPORTS CLUB, MALTA, G.C.
  1. That the name of the Club be: THE OVERSEAS RUGBY AND SPORTS CLUB, MALTA, G.C.
  2. That the object of the Club is to foster a true sporting spirit on the Island of Malta by providing facilities for:
    1. All Service and Civilian players who are unable to play for any other team, i.e. Members of Units unable to field a side.
    2. All Service and Civilian players, who, although committed to play for a Unit side during the week, wish to play for the Club on any other occasion.
    3. Non-playing sports enthusiasts who may support the Club and join in the social life.
  3. That the Management of the Club shall be entrusted to a General Committee of such officers as shall be elected at the Annual General Meeting. Liaison with the Representatives of the Services shall be effected by means of the Joint Services Representatives in each sport.
  4. That the General Committee of the Club shall consist of:
    President
    Vice-Presidents
    Hon. General Secretary
    Hon. General Treasurer
    Bar Manager
    Social Secretary
    Secretary for each Section
    Chairman for each Section.
    The Officers to hold office for one year and to be elected by members at an Annual General Meeting.
  5. That the General Committee shall have powers to fill any vacancies which may arise in their number during the course of the year, have full power to co-opt as may be found expedient, and delegate any of its duties to such other Committees as may be necessary.
  6. Each Section shall be governed by its own Committee which shall consist of: Chairman; Hon. Secretary; Hon. Treasurer; Captain, and Vice-Captain. The Officers to hold office for one year and be elected by the members at the Annual General Meeting. Each Section Committee shall be fully accountable to the General

Committee for its management and its Chairman and Hon. Secretary shall be Officers of the General Committee.

7 A quorum for the General Committee shall consist of one third of the Committee.

8 The Annual General Meeting to be held in September and the financial year to end on the 31st August.

9 Members to be given 14 days notice of a General Meeting. Items for inclusion on the Agenda to reach the Hon. General Secretary not later than seven days prior to the meeting. Extra-Ordinary General Meetings may be called by ten or more members or by a majority vote of the General Committee.

10 The Club cannot accept liability for any loss, accident or injury which may occur on the field of play or on the Club premises.

11 That the sanction of two thirds of the number of members present and voting at the Annual General Meeting or Extra-Ordinary General Meeting is required for the passing of any resolutions to alter the rules.

Any other resolutions shall be passed by simple majority.

12 Membership Fees:

  • a) Playing Member - Annual Subscription £M1.
  • b) Social Member - £M1.
  • c) Student Member - 50 cents

a, b, c. have full privileges.

13 That these rules be placed on the Club Notice Board, and a copy be forwarded to each member.

14 That in the event of the Club winding-up, the Committee in office at that time should be given authority to use any surplus funds in the furtherance of the name of Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, Malta, G.C.

15 New members must be proposed and seconded by existing members and elected by the General Committee.

16 Membership will cease if

  • a) A member gives notice in writing to the Committee to cancel his membership
  • b) A member fails to pay his annual subscription by 31st December and the Committee removes his name from the list of members.
  • c) A member is guilty of misconduct and in the opinion of the Committee his membership should be cancelled.

17 Members may admit guests to the Club premises. The names and addresses of those guests must be recorded in the visitors book and members are responsible for the conduct of their guests.

18 No entrance fee is payable for admission to Club Premises either for members or their guests.

19 The Club premises may be open to members and their guests on any evening from 4.30p.m. to 1.00a.m. providing a Committee Member be present.

20 No beer, wine or spirits will be sold to any member or guests under 16 years of age.

97
MOTION II:
Should Motion I be defeated, then rules 15 to 20 in the said Motion be accepted as additional rules for the Overseas Rugby Union Football Club.
The result of the voting was not unanimous, 18 to 5 in favour of Motion I. However, suffice it to say, from this point in its history, the Club became a 'Sports Club', with all the expected teething troubles. Initially, Rugby and Cricket were the only Sections, and one must keep in mind that the Annual General Meeting, 1973, started off purely as that of the Overseas R.U.F.C. This meant, that at this A.G.M., not only must a Rugby Section Committee be elected for the year, but also a General Committee for the year. In succeeding years there would be separate Annual General Meetings for the General Committee and for each of the Sections. Vice-Presidents would be elected at the General Committee A.G.M., and as confirmed by Mr. Ricketts prior to the vote being taken, they would be working members of the Club and not a source of income. It was to be considered an honour.
The following Officials were elected:

Applications for New Sections

At the first General Meeting held on the 18th October, 1973, the U.K. Civilian Soccer Club and the Overseas Hockey Team applied to become, and were accepted, as Sections of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club. Although the 'Overseas' Hockey Team was so called prior to amalgamation with Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, they were two entirely separate Units. The President, Mr. C. Fox, confirmed that each Section should hold its own monthly meetings and report back to the General Committee at each meeting.

Membership Secretary

Also at this first General Committee Meeting, in view of the enlarged membership, it was decided that there was need of a Membership Secretary. Mr. W.C. Morgan was duly elected. The task had previously and normally been undertaken by the Hon. Secretary. This was a position that would have to be legalised at the next A.G.M., and so initially the Membership Secretary was 'co-opted' to help the General Secretary.

Hon. Social Secretary, Rugby Section

On the 12th November, 1973, the Rugby Section decided in committee that a Social Secretary was required, even though a General Social Secretary had been elected at the A.G.M. to serve all Sections. Mr. P. Joerning was elected as Hon. Social Secretary of the Rugby Section.

Rugby Section 1973/74

Against all pessimistic views, Rugby on the Island proved to be in a very healthy state, and Overseas had an excellent season. This was at a time when the resident teams had declined in number to 5, i.e. Overseas, R.A.F.; 40 Cd: Gp RM; 234 Signal Sqdn and Kirklee Battery. Each of the 5 fielded an A and B team also 203 Sqdn (RAF) on one occasion fielded a B team. Overseas must thank the Team Captain, Niall Armstrong, who gave a great deal of his time to Rugby in Malta, not only for Overseas, both organising and playing. Also, during this season, we had a very keen and talented junior side. Other factors contributing to a good rugby season were the number of visiting naval ships, who could usually field an A and/or a B side, and the touring sides organised by the Services. The season started with 1st and B team practice games on the 20th and 21st October, 1973.

Whilst on the subject, the following list will show how the number of resident teams in Malta, who had provided regular opposition to Overseas XV's, had declined year by year due to Service station closures. The list gives the season when Overseas last played a particular team although one must bear in mind that my fixture lists are incomplete, especially prior to 1954.

1949-50 Med. Fleet (Possibly further fixtures between 1950 and 1954)

1954-55 E.R.A.'s Club
1955-56 H.M.S. Ranpura (Depot Ship)
1956-57 R.A.F. Ta' Qali
1958-59 H.M.S. Forth (Depot Ship)
1961-62 R.A.F. Siggiewi
1963-64 H.M.S. Ausonia (Depot Ship)
1964-65 Fort R.F.C. (Naval Shore Establishments - Formed 1956)

1964-65 H.M.S. Falcon (R.N. Air Station, Hal Far)
1966-67 Fort St. Angelo (Naval)
1970-71 Nomads (Signets) (Small Units Army Team - Formed 1957)

1973-74 Hawks R.F.C. (R.A.F.)
1974-75 234 Signal Squadron (Army)

H.M. Ships Ranpura, Forth and Ausonia, all Depot Ships, possibly relieving each other, but this proves that the last of the big Depot Ships, at least providing Rugby opposition, departed Malta in 1964. Fort St. Angelo appeared on the scene in 1964-65 and was initially known as 'Fort St. Angelo (Bastions - Forts 2nd Team)' or 'Bastions'. Forts R.F.C. disappeared as a Club after the 1964/65 season, after which the Navy Shore Establishments continued to put out a team up to the end of 1966/67 as Fort St. Angelo. I believe Hawks R.F.C. was first formed as an R.A.F. small units team. It ceased to exist in name after 1973/74, although it probably carried on as R.A.F. 'B' Team. 234 Signal Squadron ceased as a team after 1974/75, although the unit provided players for an Imtarfa XV in 1975/76. I have not included the main Army opposition as this depended on the regiment serving in Malta at any particular time and this opposition is still provided by 41 Royal Marine Commando (1977/78).

Once again the National Sports Board, Malta, gave Overseas Rugby Section permission to use pitches, known of old as numbers 2 and 6, at the Marsa Playing fields. These rugby pitches were for the use of Overseas Rugby Team and their opponents. For use of these pitches we must thank Mr. C. Cauchi, who gave us permission on behalf of the National Sports Board, and also our Section Chairman, Mr. J. Sharp, who negotiated on the Club's behalf. We had to look after and mark the pitches ourselves, with the use of equipment loaned by the Services, and this was ably done by Dave Taylor, Dave Snaith, and Jim Masuwale. Number 2 pitch proved a little dangerous at times when the local Archery Club were practising. This problem was solved when they kindly agreed to change the direction of flight of arrows!

At the start of the season Col. W.E.B. Dansie agreed to be the rugby Press Relations Officer. Both Col. Dansie and Mr. Sharp gave the local papers details of games and results.

At the Annual General Meeting, Mr. D. McKenzie, the Student Representative, had informed the Committee that 20 players were keen to play for the B side. They were mostly pupils from Tal Handaq School. During the Season this B side became known as the 'Colts' or 'Junior Side'. Their ages varied from 14 to 19, with the odd stalwart to add strength, and one must appreciate that the only opponents available at this time were adult teams. They were organized and trained by Marcus Halliday, Dave Taylor, and Jim Masuwale, and very ably led by their Team Captain, Don.

100
McKenzie, and Vice-Captain, Clay Owens. Don's leadership on and off the field was excellent for such a young person.
A number of the Juniors played for the Senior side including D. McKenzie, C. Owens, C. Laurie and J. Callens. On the 12th November, 1973, a B Team Selection Committee was formed comprising D. McKenzie, D. Taylor, J. Masuwale and T. Agius Farrante.
Fixtures were arranged on a monthly basis by the Joint Services Rugby Committee (JSRC). Previously teams had arranged their own fixtures, but with the small number of resident teams on the Island, the JSRC assured an even distribution of games. The duties of the JSRC also included discipline, tours, selection of Malta XVs and entertaining of touring sides. The JSRC had been in existence in Malta for a number of years in one form or another, and one of its main functions had been to control the use of the Service Pitches. The JSRC withheld permission to play on Service Pitches, now only at Safi and Hal Far, and no games were arranged to take place at the Marsa, now under control of the Maltese National Sports Board, until the winter seasonal rain started assuring continuing growth of grass. Overseas was represented on the JSRC by the 1st Team Captain Mr. N. Armstrong, and by the Junior Team Representative, Mr. M. Halliday.
During the season two problems arose concerning the Junior team, both of which were resolved to the benefit of Club and players. For the first time the Club had a large number of junior members, 25 in number, one or two as young as 14, and obviously, where functions were concerned, this age group could not mix with adult members. Most of the Juniors were also members of a club called the Junior International Sports Club (JISC), and there was talk of the JISC forming its own rugby team the following year. With the obvious talent amongst junior members, it was in the interest of Overseas to keep them with the Club. From decisions made in Committee, separate functions were arranged for the Juniors, including film evenings, and they were further represented on the Rugby Section Committee, by Mr. J. Masuwale, Junior Team Representative, and Mr. C. Owens, 'B' Team Vice-Captain.
During the season, as Secretary of the Rugby Section, I corresponded with Mr. L. Elliott, Secretary of Scarborough R.U.F.C. Colts, making arrangements for the Scarborough Colts to visit Malta during the following New Year. It was hoped to arrange games for them against our Colts and the Exiles. Unfortunately, Scarborough Colts had to start rebuilding their side at the start of the 1974/75 season.
The annual fixtures, Tal Handaq School versus the Exiles, took place over the Christmas Holidays. Although it was planned in Committee otherwise, the games were organized by the youths themselves and were extremely successful. Both games were won by the Exiles, the first by 27 points to 19, and the second by 11 points to 10.
Four touring sides were arranged by the Services; three were Welsh, namely, Ynysdu R.F.C., Hirwaun R.F.C. and Cardiff H.S.O.B., and the English team Canterbury R.F.C. The four parties were accommodated at Salina Bay Hotel at their own expense. Arrangements were made for each of the visiting teams to be hosted by a different home team. Unfortunately, the team which Overseas were asked to host and play against, Hirwaun R.F.C., cancelled their tour. This meant that Overseas. 
    had no fixture against any of the touring sides. Overseas
    was represented in the Malt XVs to play the tourists by
    Messrs. J. Glover; 3. Gradden; N. Armstrong; D. Tay10r;
    P. Joenring; C. Redlicott; C. Rice; K. Mathers; J. Mesuwale;
    M. Pearce; and C. Owens.

CRICKET SECTION 1974

The Cricket Section of Overseas was formed in 1965 and details of its inception have already been given. In September, 1973, the Cricket Section had just finished a very successful season. Mr. T.N. Ricketts, Section Chairman, reported that Overseas had, once again, been the side on the Island and won the Malta League Championship. Peter Wright had been a regular source of runs, ably backed by Ralph Daley (Captain) and Trevor Ricketts. Peter Wright and Ralph Daley had finished the season with batting averages of over 40. On the bowling side Rob Ward, Mike Caseley and Dave Taylor had the best analysis.

RECORD FOR 1973
P15 - W12 - L3 Points 48

The Cricket Section held its Annual General Meeting on the 7th March, 1974, and the following Officials were elected:-

CRICKET SECTION
  • Chairman: Mr. A. Latham
  • Hon. Secretary: Mr. W. Newton
  • Hon. Treasurer: Mr. L. Finnis
  • Team Captain: Mr. T.N. Ricketts
  • Team Vice-Captain: Mr. R. Ward
  • Selection Committee: Messrs. T.N. Ricketts; R. Ward and P. Wright.

Elected on formation of 'B' XI

  • B Team Captain: Mr. P. Merchant
  • Vice-Captain: Mr. G. Porter

For Overseas the 1974 season, under the Captaincy of Trevor Ricketts, was again successful. Overseas won the 6 a-side Competition, the single wicket competition with Jim Glover being the victor, and finished runner-up in the league. Also, after two months of inactivity from mid July to mid September, we were losing semi-finalists in the Governor's Cup Knockout.

The formation of a 2nd XI marked a welcome expansion of the Section's activities. Under the Captaincy of Pete Merchant and Vice-Captaincy of Gerry Porter, the side made a commendable first season's effort.

2nd XI record for 1974 - P5 - W3 - L3

The 6 a-side competition was organized as a curtain-raiser to the season, taking place on the 11th and 12th March, with 16 teams taking part. Overseas entered 4 teams and all acquitted themselves admirably. The 'A' side won the competition with the 'B' side being losing semi-finalists.

  • 'A' Team: T. Ricketts (Captain); P. Wright; M. Shaw; D. Taylor; J. Glover and R. Ward
  • 'B' Team: W. Newton (Captain); A. Latham; M. Caseley; D. Walker; M. Pennter and L. Finnis

Six teams participated in the league, namely, Overseas, Malta Sports Club, R.A.F. 'A' and 'B', R.N. and Army, with each team playing the other 5 twice. All games in the league were played between the 16th May and the 17th July. Overseas finished the league 2nd to R.A.F. 'B', losing 3 out of the 10 games, 2 of the 3 being by the smallest of margins (2 runs and 5 runs). Overseas also played 3 friendly matches against the R.A.F.

R.N., H.M.S. Fearless and the Marsa Sports Club, winning the first two and losing to the M.S.C.

1st XI League Record for 1974 P10 - W7 - L3

The single wicket competition took place on the 14th July. Each league side was restricted to 3 competitors, with Overseas being represented by J. Glover, T. Ricketts and A.N. Other.

Touring sides to come to Malta during the 1974 season were as follows:

Blighters

The Lancashire and Cheshire Cricket Lovers Society, 21st to 25th September. They were brought to Malta by Rick Bradshaw, ex Overseas Player.

Mendip Acorns

28th September to 3rd October. Stars in the party were Don Shepherd, England and Glamorgan, Barry Meyer, Gloucester, and Jim Presdee, Glamorgan.

Bertie Joel's XI

6th to 16th October. The team was brought out by the man himself, Bertie Joel, M.C.C. Member, and the party included Bill Frindall, B.B.C. Commentator.

The touring sides' visits were organized by Mike Newton as Secretary of Malta Cricket League. Overseas had no fixtures with the tourists although we were represented in the Malta Select XIs by T. Ricketts (Captain), R. Wright and I. Shaw.

All Overseas Cricket Section 1st team matches, and the majority of the 2nd team matches, were played at the Marsa, the cricket centre of Malta. Whilst competitive games and touring sides are organized by the Malta Cricket League Committee, all teams playing at the Marsa and using the facilities of the Club do so by kind permission of the Malta Sports Club. The Malta Sports Club itself plays as a Club on Sundays from June to the end of the season. These matches, played at the Marsa, are friendlies and are organized by the M.S.C. Cricket Committee under a different match manager each week. At the beginning of the 1974 season the M.S.C. Cricket Section ordered a new hard wearing cricket mat, at a cost of £210, which arrived during the season. The Navy provided a mat for the start of the season. The six teams participating in the league were required to pay a league entrance fee of £M14 and a ground fee of £M1.05 per match.

At the start of the 1974 season Overseas General Committee gave a grant of £M44 to Overseas Cricket Section to cover the cost of new equipment. The equipment position was aggravated by a burglary at the M.S.C. sports stores at the Marsa. At the end of the season, by players paying match fee of 25p per game, the section was able to repay £M37.

In his end of season report, Mr. A. Latham, Chairman of the Cricket Section, commented on the wealth of talent in Overseas underwritten by Mr. J. Glover's performance in the single wicket competition, when he emerged as this season's champion. R. Wright who played in all 13 matches with a batting average of 56. Mr. Latham mentioned to Mr. J. Sharp for his support and Mr. T. Ricketts, Captain, for his drive and enthusiasm in forming a 2nd XI, for organization of teams and practices, and for the services rendered to the Cricket Section and Club in general.

I wish to thank Mr. M. Newton, Mr. T. Ricketts and Mr. A. Latham for making available details of the Cricket Section for inclusion in this history.

SOCCER SECTION 1973/74

Soccer became a section of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club on the 18th October, 1973. Mr. T. Ricketts, the Soccer Club's Chairman from 1968 spoke in support of their application.

Officials of the Soccer Section for 1973/74:

Chairman
Mr. T.N. Ricketts

Hon. Secretary
Mr. P. Wright

Hon. Treasurer
Mr. W. Panter

Hon. Social Secretary
Mr. J. Bonner

Team Captain
Mr. D. Locke

Team Vice-Captain
Mr. P. Dobson

For the history of the Soccer Section, and for details of the 1973/74 season, I am indebted to Mr. T. Ricketts. Also to Mr. D.W. Pennick, Joint Services Public Relations Officer, Malta, for allowing me to look through back copies of the Dolphin & Eagle.

At the time of applying for membership of Overseas, the Soccer Section was already a thriving Club, in fact, they started the 1973/74 season with the nucleus of the very successful side of 1972/73. The Club was formed in 1968, although a 'Team' had been entered in the league prior to this. At the time of amalgamation the Section had teams playing in the Joint Services Football Association Major and Minor Leagues. When first entered in the Major League, the side had a combination of Civilian and Army (Service) elements and they played under the name of Corinthians. After a year the Civilian element became predominant and took over. The side entered in the Minor League was purely Civilian and played under the name of U.K. Civilians. The Soccer Section's home ground, prior to the withdrawal, had been at the Marsa, the pitch in front of Marsa Lodge now used by Maltese Industrial Firm's Teams. After the withdrawal Corradino became the home ground, by kind permission of the Navy Authorities. The Soccer Section play in red jerseys.

On becoming a Section of Overseas the intention was, if possible, to play under the name of 'Overseas', although naturally, season plans were too far advanced at the time of amalgamation, to make any changes for 1973/74. For the 1974/75 season, the team, when playing in the Minor League, changed the name from U.K. Civilians to Overseas. Unfortunately, when playing in the Major League, because of the original entry terms, part Civilian and part Service, and Overseas Rugby and Sports Club being purely a Civilian Club, the name had to stay as Corinthians.

Football leagues and cups, as organized by the Joint Services Football Association (Malta), and in which the Overseas Soccer Section had an interest in the 1973/74 season (and still do), were as follows:

  • Major League
  • Minor League. For the 1973/74 season the Minor League was split into two with promotion and relegation at the end of the season, four up and four down. The two teams at the top of each division to play each other to decide overall winners of the Minor Unit League. Overseas, playing as U.K. Civilians, were placed in Division II, even though they had won the Minor League the year before.

Minor Units Knock-Out Cup

Overseas Representative on the Joint Services Football Association for 1973/74 was Mr. T. Ricketts.

The 1973/74 season started off with a Major League game on the 15th September - Overseas, as Corinthians, played the R.A.F. at Corradino.

1973/74 proved to be the most successful season in the Soccer Section's history. It finished the season 2nd to 41 Commando in the Major League, Champion of Division II in the Minor League, and winner of the Joint Services Knock-Out Cup. Only 8 games were lost out of a total of 37.

The highlights of the season were two superb games in the Major League against 41 Cdo. Both times the Commandos managed to overcome the Corinthians by the odd goal, firstly 3 - 2 and then 4 - 3. Corinthians finished the league with 14 points from 10 games.

In the Minor League U.K. Civilians swept all before them and a succession of superb wins left us at the top of the table with 28 points from 16 games, 6 points in front of our nearest rivals '2 Troop'. Prior to the two games lost in this league during 1973/74, the U.K. Civilians had not lost for 4 years. U.K. Civilians completed a double in the Minor League when they won the Knock-Out Cup, beating St. Angelo in the final by 5 goals to 1.

Throughout the 1973/74 season Overseas was basically dependent on 16 players for both leagues, and this fact alone makes their achievements even more remarkable.

During the month of January, 1974, we were down to 12 players. Of the 21 players who appeared for Overseas during the season, 10 played 30 or more games out of the maximum of 37. In his end of season report, the Soccer Section Secretary, whilst commenting on, and because of, the tremendous team spirit, said it would be wrong to single out individual players. He did mention, however, that in keeping with the spirit of the side, Mike Newton played 15 times and was substitute for 10, Malcolm Panter played 10 times and was substitute for 18, also that two of the side scored over 100 goals between them out of 136 scored by the team.

Dennis Locke had been Team Captain for the last two seasons 1972-74, and in this task he had been ably assisted by Vice-Captain Phil Dobson, known to one and all as 'Dobbie'. Jeff Bonner did an excellent job in organizing numerous social functions.

HOCKEY SECTION 1973/74

As previously stated, the Overseas Hockey Team became a Section of Overseas Rugby and Sports Club on the 18th October, 1973. The Hockey representative, Mr. D. Taylor, spoke in support of the application for membership.

Officials of the Hockey Section for 1973/74

  • Chairman: Mr. D. Taylor
  • Hon. Secretary: Mr. D. Ditcham
  • Team Captain: Mr. R. Ward

For details of the history of the Hockey Section, and results for 1973/74, I am indebted to Mr. D. Taylor and Mr. D. Ditcham. I also found useful information in the Dolphin & Eagle.

Mr. Ditcham informed me that when he first arrived in Malta in September, 1971, there were several teachers at Tal Handaq, including Mr. Taylor and Mr. Ward, who had previously entered the Inter Service 6 a-side Hockey Tournament each year. Mr Ditcham joined their ranks. As the majority of the players were already members of what was then the Overseas R.U.F.C., it was a natural development to call the team 'Overseas'.

Following the British Forces withdrawal and subsequent return, the Navy P.T. Department in Malta organized the Joint Services Hockey League. Teams were entered by St. Angelo, 41 Cdo, R.A.F. Luqa, 234 Signal Squadron and R.N. Hospital Mtarfa. Overseas entered the League at the start of the 1973/74 season. League fixtures for 1973/74 ran from October to February and from the 8 games played Overseas derived 4 points - a long way behind the Champions, 41 Cdo, who remained unbeaten.

During this season Overseas also played a number of friendlies against H.M.S. Hermes, H.M.S. Lynx, H.M.S. Hampshire and the local team 'Young Stars'. In this inaugural season Overseas Hockey Team played a total of 14 matches, scoring 17 goals and conceding 34. Overseas lost 3 - 2 to H.M.S. Hermes on Easter Monday.

With permission from the Navy, Overseas home ground was at Corradino. Overseas colours, white shirts and black shorts.

Although the hard core of Overseas players came from S.C.S., Tal Handaq, anyone was eligible to become a member of the Club and so play for the team. For the 1973/74 season the team was invariably made up from R. Ward (Captain), D. Ditcham, D. Taylor, H. Ritchie, Mave Turner, P. Joernning, P. Marchant, M. Lewis, J. Whitehead, F. Frendo, T. Ricketts, P. Wright, J. Bonner, and J. Glover. The only lady in the side, Mave Turner, was an exceptionally good player.

It is worth pointing out that of the names mentioned, at least four, namely, J. Glover, T. Ricketts, D. Taylor and P. Joernning, played, or had played for the 1st teams of each of the four sections, Rugby, Cricket, Soccer and Hockey. P. Wright played for the 1st teams of the Soccer, Cricket and Hockey Sections. Even from the few names mentioned, one can see the sound argument of those advocating joining the four sections under one roof.

In the Joint Services 6 a-side Competition held on Sunday, 3rd March, 1974, a total of 15 teams competed, and these were split into 3 leagues. Overseas 'A' qualified for the Knock-Out final rounds by leading their league. They were eliminated 1 - 0 by H.M.S. St. Angelo, the eventual winners, in the quarter final.

SOCIAL EVENTS 1973/74

The amalgamation of the four Sections injected new life into the social activities of the Club. Not only were functions organized by the Hon. General Social Secretary, Mr. P. Joerning, but also additional functions were organized by each of the Section Hon. Social Secretaries.

The Film Evenings at the Club House continued as the main social events and were well supported. From February these evenings were arranged on the 2nd and 4th Thursdays of each month. Once again we must thank Jack Sharp for the supply of films and for arranging for Mr. Maurice Baldacchino to operate the equipment. Also, once it became accepted that there was a clash of interests between the Colts and some of the Senior Members, separate films and functions were arranged for the Junior Section.

An attempt was made to enter an Overseas team in the Bowling League. A dozen members turned out for a trial get together at the Malta Bowling Club on the 9th March. Further practices were arranged with the view of finding out if there was enough interest. A good time was had by all, but the idea came to nought.

As has already been mentioned in the Rugby Section report of 1973/74, we had been asked by the J.S.R.C. to host the touring team, Hirwaun R.F.C. Unfortunately, the Club made extensive preparations for their visit, including a disco at Marsa Lodge on the 24th March, before learning of the cancellation of this tour. This left a void when no social functions were held.

The Annual Dinner Dance was held at the Preluna Hotel Skyroom on the 30th March, 1974, and this event proved a tremendous success, with 120 paying guests attending. As Mr. Joerning said in his end of season report, it was an ideal occasion to honour the 14 members, of all sections, who were leaving the Island. Besides the official guests, Mr. & Mrs. Colin Cauchie, the ladies of the 5 Colts who had played for the 1st team attended. The young ladies were the personal guests of Mr. J. Sharp, Chairman of the Rugby Section. Commenting in Committee, Mr. Sharp said that this dance was the best he had attended in his 15 years association with the Club. All credit was due to Peter Joerning for the organization and success of the dance.

Dinner Dances were also organized by the Football Section at the Crystal Hotel, Bugibba, on the 19th January, and by the Cricket Section at the Marsa Sports Club, on the 27th April. Both dances were a great success and most enjoyable.

A special farewell dinner was held at the Lancer Hotel, Salina, in honour of Charlie and Jacky Rice when they left Malta in June. Charlie had been a popular member of the Club for 7 years and could only be described as a great character. Besides being a star on the Rugby and Football field, Charlie had the odd game of Cricket & Hockey for Overseas.

For the final event of the season Peter Joerning organized a barbecue during the summer at Armier. Peter deserves a great deal of credit for the tireless effort, always with a touch of quiet humour, he put into arranging social activities during the season. In his end of season report the President said 'His [Peter's] organization this year was most efficient as evidenced by the very successful dinner dance the Club held at the Preluna Hotel'.

1974/75

GENERAL COMMITTEE

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 21, Flagstone Wharf,
Marsa, 19th September, 1974.

The following Officials were elected:

  • President: Col. W.E.B. Dansie
  • Vice-Presidents:
    • Mr. J. Sharp
    • Sub. Lt.L.R. Lloyd
    • Mr. T.N. Ricketts
    • Mr. J. Handford
    • Mr. C. Fox
    • Mr. F. Kitson
    • Mr. N. Armstrong
    • Mr. D. Taylor
    • Mr. N.C. Morgan
    • Mr. D. Alexander
    • Mr. J. Masuwale
  • Hon. General Secretary: Mr. T.N. Ricketts
  • Hon. General Treasurer: Mr. D. Taylor
  • Hon. General Social Secretary: Mr. P. Joerning
  • Membership Secretary: Mr. N.C. Morgan
  • Club House/Bar Manager: Mr. N. Armstrong
  • Bar Committee:
    • Messrs N. Armstrong (Manager)
    • B. Jones
    • M. Crossfield
    • D. Alexander
    • J. Masuwale

This was the first A.G.M. to be held as the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club and Officials elected at this meeting were concerned only with the general running of the Club. Committee and Section reports were submitted.

In his address the retiring President, Mr. C. Fox, said that this year had seen a dramatic change in the formation of the Overseas Club, from being mainly a Rugby Club to that of a Rugby and Sports Club. Mr. Fox also said that this step had, during the course of the year, proved to be a means of enhancing the name of Overseas, and for the first time for many a year, we can boast membership of almost a century. In fact, the membership at the end of the 1973/74 season stood at 68 players, of all sections, and 28 social.

As expected, such a change in the formation of the Club had its teething troubles and, where possible, consequent changes in the Rules to help to correct them.

The Rules were changed as follows:

Rule 6 amended to read

Each Section shall be governed by its own Committee which shall consist of: Chairman, Hon. Secretary, Hon. Treasurer, Captain, and Vice-Captain. The Officers to hold office for one year and be elected by Members at the Annual General Meeting of each Section. Each Section Committee shall be fully accountable to the General Committee for its management and finance and its Chairman and Hon. Secretary shall be Officers of the General Committee.

Rule 12 amended to read

Membership Fees:

  • a) Playing Member Annual Subscription £1
  • b) Social Member £1
  • c) Student Member 50cents
  • d) Temporary Membership 10cents/match
  • a) and b) only have full voting rights

Addition to Rule 2

2(d) Student Members who are still in full time education who wish to become Playing Members of the Club.

One of the initial problems facing the Club, in giving notice of the first Annual General Meetings of the General Committee and of the different sections, was that the majority of Members were interested in the General Committee A.G.M. and also one or more section A.G.M.s. This particularly concerned Members of the Rugby Section, the largest faction of the Club. The different notices would be addressed in many cases to the same individual Members. This could mean as many as four notices going out, and also there was the difficulty in trying to fit the meetings of the Rugby, Soccer and Hockey Sections in before the main A.G.M. This is accentuated by the fact that a big percentage of Members, including Committee Members, are Schoolmasters and are away from the Island during the summer months, returning early September.

The Club rules as formulated at the 1973 A.G.M. did not specifically state that each Section must hold its own A.G.M., hence the already mentioned change to Rule 6. No separate notice for the Rugby Section A.G.M. of 1974 was sent out, but advantage was taken of the word 'Rugby' in the name of the Club, i.e. anyone interested in Rugby would attend the main Club A.G.M., after having been informed of such. In fact, all Members attending the main A.G.M. in 1974, and who were interested in Rugby, were asked to attend the Rugby Section A.G.M. immediately following. For the following year (1975) this was resolved by the General Secretary sending out one notice to all Members giving dates of the different Annual General Meetings. The same information was broadcast over the B.F.B.S. and the local radio, also inserted in the local press and the Dolphin & Eagle.

'OVERSEAS' FUNDS, UNITED KINGDOM AND MALTA

During this season it was increasingly felt by Overseas Members, in view of the belief that Overseas might cease to exist once the British presence in Malta ended in March, 1979, that the Club funds, now in the U.K. in Cdr. M. Pearey's name, should be utilised for the benefit of the Club at the present time. Consequently, following decisions made in Committee, the Hon. General Treasurer Mr. D. Taylor, wrote to Cdr. Pearey asking him to make arrangements to transfer the Club monies, then in his name, to a bank assessible to and under control of the Hon. General Treasurer. Accordingly, Cdr. Pearey made arrangements and following resolutions passed in the General Committee on the 24th March, 1975, an account was opened with Lloyds Bank, Cox's and King's Branch, Pall Mall, London, in the name of Overseas Rugby and Sports Club (Malta) with a starting balance of £231.37. The account was immediately made use of to purchase training films from the R.F.U. Twickenham (£36.30) and for Cricket balls (£34.20).

As previously stated in this history under year 1959, Overseas first opened an account in Malta with Barclays Bank on the 23rd March, 1959. This account was closed and transferred to the National Bank of Malta in approximately 1964 until it was transferred back to Barclays Bank International in December, 1972. The account was held with Barclays Bank International, Sliema, until this bank ceased to operate as such in Malta on the 30th September, 1975. On the 1st October, 1975, the banking business of Barclays Bank International in Malta and Gozo, and the account of Overseas, was transferred to Mid-Med Bank Limited.

A Company registered in Malta. The Barclays Bank (Transfer of Business) Act 1975 was specially enacted by the Maltese Parliament for the purpose of facilitating the transfer of the business to Mid-Med Bank Limited and to ensure the smooth continuance of that business. The new bank had a share capital subscribed as 60% Malta Government and 40% by Barclays Bank International Limited.

ELECTION OF LIFE MEMBER - TREVOR RICKETTS

At the Annual General Meeting on the 19th September, 1974 Trevor Ricketts was honoured by being elected an Hon. Life Member of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club. It was an honour well deserved. Mr. C. Fox, the retiring President, said of Trevor 'Your Committee feel that there is a Member of the Club without whose unremitting hard work, helpful guidance and efficient organization we would not be held in such high regard in the sporting world of the Island. No Club can be successful without a dedicated Hon. Secretary and we have such a Secretary who has given up a tremendous amount of his time during the past 6 years in the running of our Club'.

Besides his contribution to sport in general in Malta, Trevor had served Overseas continuously, in one office or another, since arriving in Malta in September, 1967, and played for, or had played for, the 1st teams of all four Sections of the Club. He will always be remembered for his sterling work in reforming Overseas after the temporary withdrawal of the British Forces from Malta early 1972, and for his being the prime mover in Overseas becoming a Sports Club in September, 1973. Trevor also played a great part in training youth and teaching rugby to the pupils at the Maltese Colleges.

Trevor served the Club in the following capacities, up to 1976:-

Chairman Soccer Section since its inception in 1968 8 years
Hon. Secretary, Overseas R.U.F.C. 1969-73 4 years
Hon. General Secretary, Overseas Rugby & Sports Club 1973-76 3 years
Hon. Secretary, Overseas Cricket Section 1972-74 3 years
Served on the Social Committee 1968/69 1971-73 3 years
Captain of Cricket Team 1973-75 3 years
Fitness training of Rugby Section Members Thursdays during Rugby season 1967-74 7 years
RUGBY SECTION 1974/75
Annual General Meeting, Club House, 21, Flagstone Wharf,
Marsa, 19th September, 1974.

The following Officials were elected:

Chairman

Mr. J. Sharp

Hon. Secretary

Mr. N.C. Morgan

Hon. Treasurer

Mr. D. Taylor

Hon. Social Secretary

Office remained to be filled. Mr. P. Joerning accepted office on the 8th October, 1974.

Tours Secretary

Mr. J. Glover

Team Captain

Mr. N. Armstrong

Vice-Captain

Mr. P. Joerning

'B' Team Captain

Mr. T. Agius-Ferrante

Selection Committee

Messrs. N. Armstrong; P. Joerning and J. Hodgeon

Student Member

Office remained to be filled

Junior Member

Mr. J. Masuwale

Representative

Mr. D. Snaith

Ground Manager

Mr. D. Snaith

First Aid Man/Trainer

Mr. J. Hodgeon

Mr. N. Armstrong, Team Captain, described 1974/75 as a very successful season, as a Club we had a high percentage of players selected for the Malta XVs against touring sides. Again we ran two teams with most of the 1st and 'B' Team games taking place on Sundays and Saturdays respectively. Field training for the season, on the traditional Thursday evenings, started on the 24th September continuing until the evenings darkened earlier. Fitness training then took over, under the instruction of John Hodgeon, in Tal Handaq Gymnasium. The first games were at Marsa on the 12th October, 'B' Team vs H.M.S. Ark Royal Colts, and on the 13th October, 1st team vs H.M.S. Hampshire. Both comfortable wins for Overseas. Throughout the season 1st team opposition proved difficult to obtain, the already difficult situation of shortage of local teams being worsened by the fact that 41 Commando Unit was temporarily serving in Cyprus. Of the 15 games played by the 1st team only 4 were against local opposition, and this included playing R.A.F. 'A' 3 times. The other local opposition, being: (79 Kitklee) Battery. 'B' Team opposition was easier to find, 7 out of 16 games being against local opposition. For the first time, at least since Overseas started entering the competition in 1961/62, and excepting for 1971/72 during the withdrawal, the Inter Service 7's were not held. This was mainly because the army rugby was disorganized due to 41 Cdo serving in Cyprus.

The 'B' team, ably lead by Tim Agius-Ferrante, again gave a good account of itself, but how the make up of the team had changed! During the previous season (1973/74) the Club had 25 Student Members, mostly from S.C.S. Tal Handaq, who, strengthened by a number of older and more experienced players, had formed the 'B' team. In 1974/75 only one Student Member remained, most of the other had returned to the U.K., and the 'B' team took on a different complex. The main strength came from the staff of Tal Handaq and local U.K. Servicemen, but to the great pleasure of the Overseas Committee, a number of Maltese, one or two quite experienced, showed an interest in playing and learning the game. A great deal of credit for this must go to the 'B' team Captain, Tim Agius-Ferrante, himself an ex Head Boy of Tal Handaq, to Marcel Cassar and David Schembri, also to the comradeship which was built.

up in the previous season.

Overseas Representatives on the Joint Services Rugby Committee for 1974/75 were the Team Captain, Niall Armstrong, and the Junior Member Representative, Jim Masuvalo.

Once again, Jack Sharp, Rugby Section Chairman, worked hard behind the scenes arranging with the Secretary of the National Sports Board, Mr Colin Cauchi, for Overseas to use the rugby pitches at the Marsa. Two pitches remained. We were guaranteed use of the main pitch (Ex Navy no 1), running parallel to and about 100 yards from the Stadium, for the season, and use of the smaller pitch, below the main pitch and parallel to the golf course, for the start of the season. The smaller pitch had been used mainly for the 'B' team games. Unfortunately, early March, 1975, we lost the 'B' team pitch completely and the main pitch was re-sited by moving it approximately 15 yards nearer to the Stadium. This situation arose when part of the rugby playing area was taken to enlarge the golf course. To mark the new boundary for the golf course a fence was erected across the 'B' team pitch, continuing along the length of and a number of yards inside the main pitch, right up to the existing fence which guarded the ditch running through the Marsa. Work on the new boundary fence was already in progress when Dave Snaith, Overseas Grounds Manager, went to mark the pitches on Friday, 7th March, and by this time it was across the 'B' team pitch and into the dead ball line of the main pitch. Jack Sharp immediately contacted the National Sports Board and managed to delay work on the fence until the following week, thereby allowing the 1st team game arranged for Sunday, 9th March, to be played, and also for the main pitch to be re-sited before completion of the fence.

A great deal of hard work was put in, and time given, by Dave Snaith and also the Team Captain, Niall Armstrong, in looking after the grounds, especially when the one ground was lost to us and the main pitch, now the only remaining pitch at the Marsa, was re-sited. Both were very active in attempts to have the pitch re-seeded, without success. Fortunately, the pitch was watered by the National Sports Board throughout the summer of 1975 and so the pitch was kept in good condition without seeding.

Rugby in Malta during the second half of the 1974/75 season was enriched by three touring sides from the U.K. and one from Sicily, namely, Bedford Athletic, Pembroke, Moseley, and the Messina Rugby Clan, and the season ended with a feast of good rugby. Arrangements for the visits of the teams from the U.K. were mostly made by the Joint Services Rugby Committee. However, the ground work for Moseley's visit was done by one of our Vice-Presidents, Mr. D. Alexander, himself a Member of the Moseley Club. Moseley, a superbly drilled and strong side were easily the best of the visiting teams and remained unbeaten during their tour. When Moseley beat a Malta XV by 26 points to 6 on the 2nd April, the score represented the difference between the two teams. The team from Sicily, the Messina Rugby Clan, toured Malta mainly because of their own insistence in making the trip to play Overseas. Initially, Overseas approached Messina University (CUS) for Overseas to make a tour to Sicily with the possibility of CUS making a return visit. Unfortunately, CUS replied saying it was impractical this season and at the same time they informed Messina Rugby Clan of our interest. When Messina Rugby Clan approached Overseas asking if they could tour Malta at Easter, 1975, they refused to be put off when informed

that we already had a full programme with other touring sides at that time. In answer to a last minute telegram from Overseas Team Captain they sent their own telegram which said 'Possibility Tournament with visitors and yourselves or armed forces? Visit already programmed will arrive 28th (March) evening'. Arrive they did. Overseas put out a 13-a-side to play them and although Seas beat them 34 points to 12, they played entertaining rugby and enjoyed their visit. They lacked the experience of the Overseas XV. Provisional arrangements were made for Overseas to visit Sicily January, 1976. The referees were organized by Mr. D. Snaith, and included in the panel of referees was Mr. D. Davis who accompanied the Bedford Athletic party.

In the 1974/75 season Tal Handaq did not have the playing strength to provide opposition for the Exiles during the Christmas holidays. Two games were arranged, Exiles versus an Overseas 'B' Team, for Saturday, 28th December, and Wednesday, 1st January. The first ended in a 10 - 10 draw and the second with an easy win for the Exiles 26 - 0. Major Ian Robinson, OIC 234 Signal Squadron, his son an Exile, together with Dave Taylor for Overseas, organized the series.

At the Annual Dinner Dance on the 19th April, 1975, the 'Most Improved Player' cup was presented to David Schembri, and the 'Young Player of the Year' Cup to Tini Agius-Ferrante. It was great satisfaction to the Club that the awards were won by Maltese players. It was also a pleasure that David, a regular 1st team player, was selected to play on occasions for the Malta XV.

The Marsa was proving to be a popular area for the Maltese people on a Sunday afternoon. The main attraction was of course the horse racing, but many made use of the playing area where the rugger pitches are situated, some I am pleased to say even stopping to watch what is a 'foreign' game to them. The National Sports Board started to control the use of the area. At the beginning of November, 1974, Overseas Members were issued with permit cards by the N.S.B. allowing them to use the 'Marsa Sports Club Rugger Pitches' and so the Marsa Car parking area by Marsa Lodge. The permits were signed by Mr. C. Cauchi, for the N.S.B., and Mr. T.N. Ricketts, Overseas General Secretary. For the 1974/75 season no serious effort was made to control cars entering the Marsa playing area from the Marsa end and these permits were never asked for on entry.

At the end of January, 1975, one of our most popular
and 'colourful' characters, namely, Usain Nasuwale, known
to all as Jim, left Malta. Jim, a Fijian, always with a
great sense of humour and with an interest in all sports,
gave a great deal of his time in representing and coaching
the Junior Members in rugby. At the end of the season we lost
many Rugby Section Members, including Peter Joenring, Vice-
Captain and Social Secretary, Dave Snaith, Grounds Manager
and referee, and Jim Glover, Tours Secretary and all rounds
sportsman. All men hard to replace, both as Officials and
and players, and for his ability on the field perhaps none
more than Jim Glover. Approximately 15 Section Members left
Malta at the end of the season or during the close season,
too many to mention all by name, but all a loss to the Club.

SOCCER SECTION 1974/75

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 21, Flagstone Wharf, Marsa, 5th September, 1974.

The following Officials were elected:--

rman              Mr. T.N. Ricketts
 Secretary        Mr. P. Wright
. Hon. Secretary  Mr. W. Newton
 Treasurer        Mr. G. Porter
 Social Secretary Mr. J. Bonner
 Captain          Mr. J. Glover
-Captain          Mr. P. Wright
ction Committee   Chairman, Captain and Vice-Captain

For the Soccer Section the season was one of mixed fortunes. In the Major League we were unable to maintain our high standard and managed only 7 points from 8 games. This can be attributed in part to the fact that the league programme was affected by the withdrawal of 41 Commando Group. The Team Captain, Jim Glover, reported in December, 1974, that games were only every two weeks (due to the withdrawal of 41 Cdo), the league was in a shambles (at the time of the report), and this was showing in our play. In spite of this, under his Captaincy, they played entertaining football and the team spirit remained high.

In the Minor League it was a different story. Against strong opposition, especially from Engineering Wing and 203 Squadron, we remained unbeaten winning 15 out of 16 games, finishing the season as champions of Division I. The only point dropped was in a 4 - 4 draw with Ops. Wing.

The Minor Units Cup Competition was run more on a League basis than a Knock-out. After a good win over 840 Signals Unit in the semi-final, 5 goals to 3, we were crushed by Engineering Wing in the final, 5 goals to nil.

The main goal-scorers were again Pete Wright, who finished the season with a tally of 37, and Jeff Bonner with a creditable 18. 19 players appeared for the team during the season, 9 of these playing more than 15 of the 21 games. Pete Wright and Mike Novak were the two ever-presents in the side.

During the close season of 1975 the Section lost at least 4 good players in Jim Glover (Team Captain), Peter Wright (Vice-Captain), Mike Novak and Malcolm Panter, the first 3 being regular 1st team players. Pete Wright had been Secretary for two years, 1973-75, and Malcolm Panter had been Treasurer for at least the year 1973/74.

My thanks to Trevor Ricketts, Soccer Section Chairman, for details of the Soccer Section results for 1974/75. In his end of season report Trevor said the following:

"The Team spirit of the side was again very high and thanks for this are due to Jim Glover who skippered so well. Also in his absence I would like to thank Pete Wright who has organized the Club (Soccer Section) as Secretary so well for the last two seasons. We hope his successor will be able to maintain his high standard. A vote of thanks must also go to our Treasurer, Gerry Porter. It is always satisfying to be able to report to the

Main Committee that not only has the Soccer Section been self supporting but has in actual fact made a profit this year. Finally, I would like to thank Jeff Bonner for his work in organizing all the Social Functions.

HOCKEY SECTION 1974/75

Chairman
Mr. D. Taylor
Hon. Secretary
Mr. D. Ditcham
Captain
Mr. D. Ditcham

The forced withdrawal of 41 Commando from sporting activities in Malta at the start of the season affected the Hockey Section considerably, perhaps even more than the other Sections. Even without this problem it was difficult to build up a complete fixture list. The Joint Services Hockey League was a scrappy affair. Initially the commando withdrawal left only 5 teams to contest the title, although from the final league table published in the Dolphin & Eagle it would appear that the Commandos did complete the fixture list with a weakened team. For Overseas the league programme proved hard going with many players committed in other sports. In summing up Overseas play and difficulties in the League, Dave Taylor, Section Chairman, said, to quote "As usual the Overseas fielded a changed XI for each fixture, those who turned out were those who happened to be available at short notice. On occasions some good Hockey was played, but generally we lacked the smooth teamwork of the Services' sides. Nevertheless, we enjoyed our games. In the final league table we were placed 4/6, having won 1, lost 3 and taken 1 W.O."

In the Joint Services 6 a-side Competition held on Sunday, 9th March, 1975, Overseas gave a creditable performance. We were beaten 1 goal to nil in the quarter finals by 234 Signal Squadron, the eventual winners. Dave Ditcham, Hockey Section Secretary, describes our performance in this competition as our best during the 2 seasons 1973/74 and 1974/75. Fourteen teams entered and these were split into two leagues of seven teams, the top three teams in each league going into a Knock-out competition. It was a long competition, and those who played in the final played a total of 2 hours 8 minutes actual play. The Cup was presented by Rear-Admiral David Loram.

As with all Sections of Overseas, the Hockey Section had to take stock of players who had returned to U.K. during or since the previous season. For the 1974/75 season we had lost our Captain, Rob Ward, and Mike Lewis, but gained other players in Dave Walker, Dave Longlands and Martin Crosfield. Barrie Jones and Mike Newton also put in appearances.

At the beginning of the season Overseas applied to join the Malta Hockey League. This was turned down because of the rule which said that no side in this league could field more than two non-Maltese. According to Dave Ditcham this rule was introduced to prevent local sides getting hold of all the best Services players and to prevent the R.N., R.A.F. and the Army entering teams.

During this period a ladies' team called 'Overseas' played in the Ladies League, and although they were not connected with the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, I think readers will be interested in learning something about them. The ladies did consider applying to become a section of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club in September, 1973, but decided against it at the time. The Ladies Overseas began as an effort by Maureen Kearns (now Mrs. Whittle) and Marylin Fletcher (now Mrs. Wanley-Harris), to organize a Ladies League to give the Tal Handaq Schoolgirls' team some competitive sport. A Ladies

League operated in both 1973/74 and 1974/75 season. Overseas ladies team won in the former and the Wrens in the latter with Overseas runners-up. Other teams were entered by Mtarfa wives, Hospital, and Tal Handaq entered two teams Tal Handaq 'A' and 'B'. Half of the Overseas team was from Luqa. Notable players included Pat Greenwood, Hilary Miller, Norma Lovett and Janet Campbell (all Luqa), Marjorie Riddsale (DOE) and Bridget Lowery. Mrs Ditcham was the organizer. It was all almost loose arrangement started by adverts in Dolphin & Eagle and on B.F.B.S. - but most successful.

Once again I must thank Dave Ditcham and Dave Taylor for details of the Hockey Section, also Dave Ditcham for details of the Ladies Overseas. My thanks also to the Dolphin & Eagle for details of the Joint Services 6 a-side competition and for final results of the league table.

CRICKET SECTION 1975

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 21, Flagstone Wharf,
Marsa, Monday, 3rd March.

The following Officials were elected:-
Chairman Mr. A. Latham
Hon. Secretary Mr. M. Newton
Hon. Treasurer Mr. L. Finnis
Social Representative Mr. G. Porter
Team Captain Mr. T.N. Ricketts
Vice-Captain Mr. M. Newton
Selection Committee Messrs T. Ricketts, M. Newton and P. Wright

Overseas were fortunate to retain most players from the
successful season of 1974, and again to be Captained by Trevor
Ricketts. We did not reach the height of the previous seasons
but nevertheless acquitted ourselves well, being runners-up
in both the league and in the 6 a-side competition.

Net practice took place at the Malta Sports Club on
Tuesday evenings at 1600 commencing on the 1st April, and the
season started with the Malta Cricket League 6 a-side competition
on the 26th/27th April. For the 6 a-side Overseas entered
four teams out of a total of sixteen taking part. The eight
first round games were played on Saturday, 26th, and the
second round, semi-finals and final on Sunday, 27th.

The Malta Cricket League started on the 3rd May and ended
on the 10th August, although the last game for Overseas was on
the 19th July, all games taking place at the Marsa. Seven teams
took part, all playing each other twice. During the games each
side was restricted to 36 overs batting and no bowler could bowl
more than eight overs. Perhaps the best game for Overseas was
against the previously unbeaten Puffins on the 15th July. Set
a target of 162 runs Overseas knocked them off for a loss of 4
wickets. The two Overseas batsmen in form were Pete Wright, 87
not out, and Jim Glover, 43.

Overseas League Record for 1975 P12 - W8 - L4 Pts 33

The Malta Sports Club arranged friendly matches on Sundays
at the Marsa from June onwards.

A wealth of cricket was provided by three good touring sides
from U.K. The Mendip Acorns visited Malta in May and again in
October, the second visit captained by D.J. Shepherd of Glamorgan.
In September we welcomed the 'Blighters', the touring team of

members of the Lancashire and Cheshire Cricket Lovers Society, and finally in October, Bill Frindall, the B.B.C. Radio Cricket Commentator, who toured Malta in 1974 as a player in Bertie Joel's XI, brought out his own party. Overseas played matches against the Mendip Acorns and the Blighters, losing both matches.

A new competition called the 'Government Tourist Board Trophy' was started in 1975 but through forces of circumstances the final, between 41 Cdo and the M.S.C., had to be left for early 1976 Season. The Government Tourist Board Trophy had taken the place of the traditional Governor's Cup Knock-out.

Cricket Section expenses for 1975 were high. To offset this the Club advanced £M40 for local expenses, also £34 Stg. to buy kit in the U.K. All but a marginal amount was repaid. In order to boost Section income the Treasurer, Lew Finnis, organized a weekly raffle so successfully that he raised approximately £M25 over the season. In anticipation of this financial need the match fee had been raised at the start of the season to 30 cents per game and this had raised £M47.40 This effort speaks highly for all members of the Committee and players.

In common with other sections the Cricket Section lost a number of players leaving Malta during the season, these included Pete Wright, the most consistent and highest scoring batsman, also Jim Glover, Malcolm Panter and Dave Snaith. All were hard to replace.

Social Events 1974/75

The social life of the Club continued to thrive with a variety of events arranged by the different sections. The General Social Secretary, Mr. P. Joerning, arranged all the main and Rugby Section functions, including the Annual Dinner Dance, quietly and efficiently with the added advantage of being an active member of all four sections, which enabled him to work easily with the Section Social Secretaries.

The film shows continued to play a major part in the order of events, taking place at the Club House on the 2nd and 4th Thursdays of each month. Films and equipment provided by Jack Sharp. Also, thanks to Jack, General and Rugby Section Committee Meetings held at Zachary Street were remarkably short of hot air with the knowledge of a film show afterwards. Our thanks also to Niall Armstrong for looking after us when Rugby Section Committee Meetings were held in his office.

A Children's Christmas party was held in the Club House on Saturday, 14th December, 1975.

A number of very successful dinner dances were held throughout the year, the main one being, of course, the Club Annual Dinner Dance held this year at the Malta Sports Club on the 19th April, 1975. After initial enquiries by Peter Joerning appertaining to venue and prices a Sub-Committee was formed to work out details of the Annual Dinner Dance. The Sub-committee consisted of Messrs W. Dansie (President), T.N. Ricketts (Hon. General Secretary), P. Joerning, and D. Taylor. Peter had written to 14 possible venues before submitting details to the General Committee. The dance was a great success with over 150 members and guests attending. Trev Ricketts carried out the duties of Master of Ceremonies. In accordance with the decision taken by the General Committee, because of the large number of members leaving before the end of the season, the only 'going away' presentation given on this occasion was a tankard to Peter Joerning for his work as Social Secretary of the Club. Overseas General Secretary, Trevor Ricketts, as a member of the Malta Sports Club, took advantage of the M.S.C. Rule which said that the fee of £15 for hire of the hall would be waived if it was booked by a member of that club.

The other Dinner Dances included those organized by the Cricket Section on the 12th October, 1974, and the 24th May, 1975, both held at the Malta Sports Club, and by the Soccer Section at the Crystal Hotel, St. Paul's Bay, Bugibba, on the 9th May, 1975. The General Social Secretary also organized a pleasant Dinner Dance for the General Committee at the Armada Restaurant, Mosta, on the 25th January, 1975.

On Sunday, 2nd March, 1975, Overseas played the touring team, Bedford Athletic R.F.C., and the same evening, acting as hosts, held a Disco-Dance in their honour at Marsa Lodge. The Disco hire was called ASCO. A most practical cold buffet was organized by John Hodgeon and Niall Armstrong.

The final function of the season arranged by the Club was a barbecue held at the Malta Health Farm, Tarxien on the 14th June. This was a final get together for those leaving Malta before the next season. On this occasion those leaving were presented with Club ties. Jack Sharp also provided a film for those leaving.

BARRIE JONES

Just prior to Christmas, 1975, a tragic motor accident resulted in the death of Mr. Barrie Jones, a very popular Social Member. This was felt deeply by the members closely associated with Barrie and in response to the Club's appeal to the members, also with the assistance of the three Services Junior Schools, the net sum of £100 Sterling was sent to Mrs. Jones, then in U.K. A Sub-Committee, under the Hon. General Secretary, was formed to deal with the collection.

OVERSEAS CLUB PLAQUE

In March, 1974, Mr. M. Van de Elijk, a rugby playing member of the Club, made 27 plaques of solid plaster, a number of which were backed with wood. The design consisted of a white Maltese Cross on a blue background. Above the cross were the letters O.S.R.F.C. At the end of the 1973/74 playing season a number of leaving members were presented with one of these plaque.

Whilst researching for this history, I was informed by both Mr. Ian Chapman (Hon. Secretary 1954-56) and Mr. Mike Phillips (Hon. Treasurer 1953-56) of the blazer badge which was produced for Overseas R.U.R.C. in 1954/55. Mr. Chapman forwarded his badge to me and in October, 1975, it was placed before the General Committee to discuss whether the basic design could be used for a Club badge or plaque. It was felt that a badge would be unmarketable, but a beautiful plaque, a replica of the original design, was made by a contact of Mr. P. Tyler. Two plaques were made for the Club at a price of £14 each, the first

one being paid for by Mr. Taylor himself and presented to the Club. The plaque itself was made of wood and the inserts of the 'design' and 'Overseas R.S.C.' were made of plaster. The intention was to present a plaque when it was deemed necessary to a visiting team and such a presentation was made to the Yugoslav touring team 'Energoinvest' on the 21st March, 1976. Also, in March, 1976, Mr. J. Sharp and Mr. J. Hughes produced sample pennants, the latter from 6 girls at S.C.S. Tal Handq. Authority was given by the General Committee for Section representatives to ask Mr. Hughes to commission pennants as need arose. In actual fact, with a replica of the sample pennant as produced by the schoolgirls being unavailable, a pennant was purchased from Sports Dealer, Emmanuel Said, Britannia Street, Valletta, embossed with the Club Badge as on the Car Sticker, and presented to Energoinvest, together with the aforementioned plaque, and a number of Club ties (3 were mentioned in minutes prior to the presentation, although I believe 6 were given).

OFFICIALS LEAVING MALTA - 1975/76

Officials leaving Malta during this season included our President, Mr. D.J. Taylor. Dave left Malta in July, 1976, after serving the Club for 6 years in many capacities. His departure was a big loss to the Club and appreciation of this fact was shown by his being elected an Hon. Life Member, details of which are given on a following page. Also included amongst those leaving, with full details under separate headings, were Mr. N. Armstrong and Mr. J. Handford.

Another hard worker for Overseas, and therefore whose departure in April, 1976, was a loss to the Club, was Mr. G. Porter. Gerry took an active part in the Soccer Section (Hon. Treasurer 1974- 76, Hon. Social Secretary 1975/76), the Cricket Section (Hon. Social Secretary 1974/75), and also the Hockey Section.

Finally amongst the leavers I must include myself. I left Malta in July, 1976. On previous occasions when I left Malta I knew I would be returning, but this time it was almost certainly final. With Overseas Club being so much part of my life since 1948, it was a sad occasion. My greatest hope was that Overseas would continue to exist as a Club, in one form or another, after the British presence was finally withdrawn in March, 1979.

NIALL ARMSTRONG

Niall left Malta in October, 1975, and his departure was a loss to rugby in general in Malta and to Overseas in particular. For 3 years he had given a great deal of his time and energy to rugby in Malta, both as a player and as an organizer. As Overseas XV Team Captain he represented Overseas on the Joint Services Rugby Committee and was therefore also our Fixture Secretary. He was an automatic choice as hooker, latterly as Team Captain, of the Malta XV. He was a great Team Captain and Club man, and very popular.

Overseas will always be grateful to Niall for coming to the rescue when we were without a Club House in 1972. As General Manager of Andrews Feeds Limited, Malta, he obtained permission from his Directors for Overseas to use their premises at 21, Flagstone Wharf, Marsa, and to fit out same as a Club House.

Offices in which Niall served Overseas:-

Vice-President 1974-76
Club Captain & Fixture Secretary 1972-75
Rugby Section
Bar Manager 1972-75
Selection Committee- Rugby Section 1972-75

JACK HANDFORD

In November, 1975, Mr. Jack Handford, a Vice-President and one of the Club's longest serving Members, left Malta. Jack left quietly and no official farewell was given. When the General Committee was informed Jack was already away. The omission was partly remedied by the President, Mr. D.J. Taylor, sending a letter from the Committee and a gift from the Club of an engraved paper knife. Jack's club record is quite impressive. He joined the Club in 1962 and when he left in 1975 he could claim the club record of being the longest continuously serving Committeeman, 1963 to 1975. He was a playing member of the Rugby Section for 10 years, from 1962 to 1972, during which time he played 185 games for the Club out of a possible total of 225. This is allowing for the fact that he broke his leg in December, 1965, and could play only 8 games out of 21 in that year, also for the fact that I cannot confirm the number of games he played in 1966/67 and 1971/72. List of games played is produced below. Jack was a hard uncompromising player. He was Team Captain for 3 years, 1963-1966, Vice-Captain for 3 years, 1966-1969, and finally taking over as Vice-Captain for a 4th year when Eddy McClure was injured in November/December of the 1969/70 season. He was a Vice-President for 7 years, 1969-1976. Jack took part as a player (vice-Captain) in the Rugby tour to Kessia in January, 1968, and was in Committee during the temporary disbandment and reformation of the Club in 1972.

Jack also played for the Cricket Section from its inception in 1965 to approximately 1972.

Election of Life Member - David Taylor

On the 3rd April, 1976, David Taylor was honoured by being elected an Hon. Life Member of Overseas Rugby and Sports Club. Speaking on behalf of the General Committee, Mr. J. Sharp, Chairman of the Rugby Section, said that David had served Overseas in many capacities since he joined the Club on his arrival in Malta in 1970, both as a player and in an Official capacity, not least in his final year as President.

David had played with credit for 6 years for the 1st teams of all four Sections, Rugby, Soccer, Hockey and Cricket, also playing a great part in training youth and teaching pupils at the Maltese Colleges the art of Rugby.

David served the Club in the following capacities between 1970 and 1976:-
  • President 1975/76
  • Vice-President 1973-75   2 years
