RUGBY SECTION 1975/76

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 21, Flagstone Wharf, Marsa, 11th September, 1975.

The following Officials were elected:-

Chairman Mr. J. Sharp
Hon. Secretary Mr. N.C. Morgan
Hon. Treasurer Mr. D.J. Taylor
Mr. J. Andrews took over duties of Hon. Treasurer in December, 1975)
Hon. Social Secretary Mr. J. Hughes
Team Captain & Fixture Secretary Mr. J. Hodgeon
Vice-Captain Office remained to be filled
'B' Team Captain Mr. M.N. Cassar
Selection Committee Mr. J. Hodgeon (Vice-Captain and one other remained to be elected)
Tours Secretary Mr. J. Hodgeon
First Aid Man/Trainer Mr. J. Hodgeon

From the outset John Hodgeon said he would be a non-playing Captain and this left the problem of Captaincy on the field, and also the vacant position of Vice-Captain, to be settled. Niall Armstrong willingly captained the team on the field until he left Malta in October. At this point Brian Charnley tentatively agreed to take over from Niall, and James Andrews agreed to be Vice-Captain. The position was further complicated when John Hodgeon left Malta on the 21st January, 1976, but then Brian Charnley agreed to take over the Captaincy on and off the field. Mr. J. Sharp was elected as the 3rd Member of the Selection Committee, with the other two Members being Mr. J. Hodgeon, later Mr. B. Charnley (Captain), and Mr. J. Andrews (Vice-Captain). It was decided that as the number of Student Members had fallen in the previous season there was no requirement for Student Member of Junior Member Representatives. In fact no Student Members joined the Club in 1975/76. Mr. Hodgeon, later Mr. Charnley, represented Overseas on the Joint Services Rugby Committee.

Through the good offices of Mr. Jack Sharp, Overseas was again given permission by the President of the National Sports Board, Dr. Benny Camilleri, to use the pitch at the Marsa. With the pitch having been watered throughout the summer by the National Sports Board it was in good condition at the start of the 1975/76 season, and no seeding had been required. Throughout the season the pitch was looked after by the Naval Sports Officer at St. Angelo, Lt. B. Traynor, also P.T.I. D. Cousins, with Mr. J. Andrews acting as link between the Sports Officer and the Rugby Section Committee. In January, 1976, following the departure of John Hodgeon, Lt. Traynor was asked to sit on the Rugby Section Committee as R.N. Representative.

The season started with 3 practice games. These were against H.M.S. Intrepid on the 13th September, and against 'G' Coy. 41 Cdo on the 28th September and the 5th October. The Team on the Island throughout 1975/76 was undoubtedly 41 Commando, they proved unbeatable. This made the standard of all other teams, including Overseas, poor in comparison, and made for some heavy defeats, especially at 'B' team level. At 1st team level there were only 4 regular local teams, namely, Overseas, 41 Cdo, R.A.F. Luqa and

128

Alma Battery, and at 'B' team level the only regular local teams were Overseas, 41 Cdo and R.A.F. Luqa. Other teams who managed to put out a team on the odd occasion at 'B' team level were 203 Sqdn (R.A.F.), Mtarfa, St. Edwards College and S.C.S. Tal Handaq. This meant that players, particularly in our 'B' team, who met 41 Cdo six times during the season, began to think, 'Oh, not again!'. However, notwithstanding this situation, the season was exceedingly enjoyable rugbywise. The first four games of the season for Overseas were against visiting naval ships, all wins, and the final game of the season for Overseas was against the touring team Energoinvest R.C. from Makarska, Yugoslavia. Good rugby was also provided by two touring sides from S. Wales Deri R.F.C. and Abercarn R.F.C., although Overseas did not have a fixture against them. The tours by the two S. Wales sides were organized by the J.S.R.C. Overseas was represented in the Malta XV against Deri by B. Charnley, D. Schembri, and W. Wood, and in the Malta XV against Abercarn by B. Charnley. Overseas entered two teams in the Inter Service 7's on the 28th March, 1976, with Overseas 'A' being beaten in the semi final by 41 Cdo, the eventual winners of the competition. At the outset of the season Mr. J. Hodgen, Tours Secretary, attempted to arrange a tour to Messina to play Messina Rugby Clan. This failed through lack of support.

The highlight of the 1975/76 season was the visit to Malta by Energoinvest Rugby Club from Makarska, near Split, Yugoslavia, between the 19th and 26th March, 1976. The initial approach to our Club for this tour, by Mr. Marko Protega, General Secretary of the Yugoslav Rugby Federation (Ragbi Savez Yugoslavia), was made at Federation level, after finding our Club address in the R.F.U. Twickenham handbook. From this point, all arrangements for the tour were made between Overseas General Secretary, Mr. T.N. Ricketts, and Mr. Marko Protega, acting as Tour Manager for Energoinvest R.C. The touring party of 25 travelled by Yugoslav Airlines (JAT) and stopped, at their own expense, at the Villa Rosa, St. George’s Bay. With kind permission of Capt. L. Pace, B.E.A. Manager at Sliema, they were met with due ceremony on the airport tarmac by our President, Mr. D.J. Taylor, accompanied by Mr. Ricketts and Mr. J. Sharp, Rugby Section Chairman. They were an extremely talented and sporting side and this resulted in two very good games, the first on Sunday, 21st March, versus Overseas, and the second on Wednesday, 24th March, versus a Malta Select XV, both on our regular pitch at the Marsa. We had hoped to play the two games on the Marsa Stadium pitch which at this time was mainly a soccer pitch. Permission was received from the National Sports Board, and by courtesy of the R.A.F., the Naval Sports Officer, Lt. B. Traynor, had actually had the rugby posts transported from Hal Far, but due to last minute disagreement by the Maltese soccer fraternity, we were not able to install them. Our own posts had proved too rotten to move.

The game against Overseas was very exciting and looked upon by Energoinvest as a 'Friendly International'(Prijateljska Medunardona). Overseas, well led by their Captain, Brain Charnley, played well and fully contributed to a fast and open game. Overseas were beaten by a fitter side and superior threequarter play.

Result: Overseas 20
Energoinvest 30

Overseas was represented in the Malta Select XV by Brian
Charnley and by David Schembri as reserve. Energoinvest fielded
an unchanged side. After the running game by Energoinvest
against Overseas, and knowing the strength of the Malta team,
mostly 41 Cdo, a large crowd turned up expecting a good game.
They were not disappointed, but with most threequarter movements
being stopped by the opposing cover, it became an uncompromising
trial of strength up forward, and so scrappy at times. In the
second half the strength of the Malta Select's forwards gradually
wore their opponents down.

Sat 17th Apr Malta XV vs Abercarn R.F.C. Safi

At the beginning of the season Overseas yet again attempted
to interest the Maltese Colleges in rugby. Mr. J. Sharp, Rugby
Section Chairman, first approached the National Sports Board
and then wrote direct to the Rectors of St. Edward's, De La Salle
and St. Aloysius College. Mr. Sharp pointed out that we would
like to see the game of rugby established in Malta before the
British presence was withdrawn in 1979. This produced immediate
response from St. Edward's College and by agreement between the
College, the N.S.B., and S.C.S. Tal Handaq, pupils from the
College trained with pupils from Tal Handaq during the latters
games periods on Friday afternoons at the Marsa. The pupils
were instructed by Trevor Ricketts and Dave Taylor, sports
masters at Tal Handaq, with Dave being in charge of coaching
the boys from the College. By the end of January some of the

130

Pupils from St. Edward's had improved sufficiently to play for Overseas 'B' team and indeed on the 14th February, the College fielded a team to play Tal Handaq. Also in February, St. Edward's put out a side against 'G' Company (41 Cdo) and, although losing 24 - 0, had played well. On the 14th March three pupils from St. Edward's played for Overseas 'B'. In February, De La Salle College also started training, too late to take part in games, but sufficiently improved to give hope that they could field a XV the following season. No interest was shown by St. Aloysius College.

In November, Brother Hilary was approached to find out if the Maltese viewers would be interested in rugby on his sports programme on Malta TV. In reply Brother Hilary offered to film a game for TV. The match chosen 'by Overseas, in conjunction with the J.S.R.C., was the Malta Select practice game on the 14th February, Probables versus Possibles. The film was shown on Malta TV on Friday, 15th March, 1976, with Marcel Cassar, 'B' Team Captain, commenting on the game in Maltese. Marcel also gave the viewers a brief history of Overseas Rugby Club. Whilst making the film care was taken to shoot one or two carefully planned highlights involving David (Schembri) and Marcel. With David and Marcel being local boys this involved the Maltese with Overseas and the game more and also gave a better impression of what rugby is all about.

In addition to the direct approaches made by Overseas, David Schembri and another local sportsman cum reporter, writing under the Nom de Plume 'Atticus', attempted to reach the Maltese public by writing separate articles in the Times of Malta. David, a lieutenant in the Malta Armed Forces, winner of the Overseas Club's 'Most Improved Player of the Year' Cup in 1974/75, wrote an article (16th October,1975) under the heading 'Rugby is a Fascinating Game', 'Atticus', himself an all-round sportsman, in his weekly article (sportspage) headed 'By the Way - Sport' wrote twice (February 4th and 11th) on rugby in general in Malta, going back over the years, and on Overseas Rugby Club in particular. Both writers informed the public that Overseas would be pleased to teach rugby to anyone interested.

In November, once again, members experienced difficulty in entering the Marsa whilst horse racing was in progress on a Sunday afternoon - police were stopping cars at the main gate. It was decided to have cards reprinted and issued to members, similar to those issued at the beginning of the 1974/75 season. This did not suffice, and those Overseas members who were not also members of the Malta Sports Club, i.e., unable to show a M.S.C. Car sticker, had to obtain a N.S.B. car sticker. Jack Sharp was able to get a limited amount of N.S.B. stickers from the N.S.B. Secretary.

During the season a problem arose over the makeup of Overseas 1st team, and which, because of the small number of teams on the Island, affected rugby in Malta in general. A special meeting of all rugby players was called on the 29th January, 1976. presided over by Mr. J. Sharp, Overseas Rugby Section Chairman. The crux of the matter was that Overseas, as a Civilian Club, was fortunate to be able to accept as members, and so select its teams from, all interested players, Civilian and from Service Units. This included 41 Cdo personnel, when they were not committed to their own unit team, most of whom were good enough to walk into

131

any team. Many 41 Cdo chose to play for Overseas when possible, often to the detriment of less able players who had no other team, and so at times Overseas looked very much like 41 Cdo itself. Overseas players, that is, players who owed allegiance only to Overseas, were adversely affected, also the opposition started remarking on similarity of teams. The meeting was handled with great tact and good sense by Jack Sharp and Overseas Team Captain, Brian Charnley, to the general satisfaction of all concerned. 41 Cdo were friends of all gathered and no one wished to offend. The rugby community in Malta is of necessity a very close unit, and as Brian Charnley said on addressing the meeting ‘Overseas' was unique, it was more than a Club, the team was made up of Civilians, 41 Cdo, Battery, Navy and R.A.F. From this point Overseas recreated its own identity and rugby was more enjoyable for all concerned. This was a chance for Brian, also James Andrews, Team Vice-Captain, to pep up Overseas players on lack of fitness, asking them to let the Captain know they wished for a game, promptness on the field etc. - The meeting was a good airing of views and a success. At the end of the season Jack Sharp stressed that in view of the difference of opinion encountered this season, we should have Service Representatives on the Rugby Section Committee next year. The same practice was adopted when we had our Club House at Nasra Lodge.

Consequent to the above, the second half of the season was more enjoyable and according to the Captain, our standard of play generally improved. He described the season as reasonably successful after a disappointing start. Brian did not comment on the play of any individual, but there is no doubt that Brian himself earned his place playing at scrum half for the Malta XV. Dick McArdle and Brian were our most consistent players. Credit is due to Marcel Cassar who captained the 'B' Team under great odds, always short of players. He gave a great deal of his time and energy looking for players during the week, and he was a tower of strength on the field. No player was considered to have earned the 'Most Improved Player of the Year' Cup. The 'Young Player of the Year' Cup was presented to Peter Traynor.

SOCCER SECTION 1975/76

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 11th September, 1975.

The following Officials were elected:-

  • Chairman: T.W. Ricketts
  • Hon. Secretary: J.J. Bonner
  • Hon. Treasurer: G. Porter
  • Hon. Social Secretary: G. Porter
  • Team Captain: J.J. Bonner
  • Vice-Captain: D. Smith
  • Selection Committee: Chairman, Captain and Vice-Captain

Throughout the 1975/76 season the Soccer Section had difficulty in raising a team of comparable standard with previous seasons. This was particularly so in the Minor League and there were fears that we might be relegated to Division II at the end of this season. Fortunately, these fears were not realised.

The main problem was trying to replace the experienced players who left Malta during the summer months and this proved almost impossible. This was aggravated by the occasional clash of Soccer Section and Rugby Section fixtures on Saturdays. The fact that one or two members who played both codes might chose to play rugby was a serious matter when the Soccer Section had so few players to chose from. This led to the Section Secretary, Mr. J. Bonner, approaching the General Committee for priority to be given to Soccer on Saturdays. After the start of the season, Jeff Bonner reported using schoolboys in the Major League, although the Minor League XI was made up of all Overseas players. In January, 1976, the League Management Committee queried the constitution of our membership with reference to one of our players, although this was cleared up to our satisfaction at a League Management Committee Meeting in the February. Our point that our constitution allowed a certain amount of freedom of choice of players was agreed to, provided we informed the Management Committee of any players we used.

In April, 1976, the Soccer Section lost another good player and hard working Committee man in Gerry Porter. Gerry had been Treasurer for 2 years, 1974-76, and in his final year also took on the task of Social Secretary.

The Hockey League 1975/76 was much better organized than in previous seasons. The Overseas Hockey team was also much stronger and consequently it was a successful and enjoyable season.

The League started on the 27th October and ended on the 12th April with 8 teams taking part, namely, Overseas, 234 Signal Squadron A & B, Royal Marines A & B, St. Angelo, R.N. Hospital and Luqa.

During the season the regular players were D. Walker, D. Taylor, P. Marchant, M. Crossfield, H. Ritchie, G. Devey, J. Whitehead, C. Fitches, G. Porter, Captain P. Stanley (O.C. Schools), Miss M. Turner, Miss M. Loughran, D. North, M. Hyland and L. Pape. The last three named were boys from the S.C.S. Tal Handaq. Unfortunately, from this small number of players, the following left Malta during or at the end of the season, L. Pape (February, 1976), M. Hyland (March, 1976), G. Porter (April, 1976), Captain P. Stanley (July, 1976), and D. Taylor (July, 1976)

CRICKET SECTION 1976

The Annual General Meeting was initially held at the Club House on the 19th February, 1976, but due to an error in procedure it was declared null and void. The meeting was reconvened on the 25th March, 1976.

The following Officials were elected:-

Chairman M. Caseley
Hon. Secretary G. Davey
Hon. Treasurer P. Marchant
Hon. Social Secretary J. Hughes
Team Captain M. Newton
Vice-Captain D. Walker
'B' Team Captain J. Robinson

The season opened on the 24th April with the 6 a-side Competition. Overseas entered 4 teams including a team of boys from Tal Handaq as Overseas 'C'. Our strongest team, Overseas '1', succeeded in reaching the semi final when we were beaten by 41 Cdo, the eventual winners.

The final of the Government Tourist Board Trophy for 1975, between the Malta Sports Club and 41 Commando, which had, through force of circumstances, to be left over until May, 1976, was won by the Malta Sports Club.

The Single Wicket and the Double Wicket Competitions were held on the 3/4 July and the 14/15 July respectively. The Double Wicket was won by Ray Berrington and his son. The B.F.B.S. Trophy was held on the 27th June.

Overseas 2nd XI, under the Captaincy of Jim Robinson, played 3 matches, winning against the Malta Sports Club and Tal Handaq, and losing to the Navy.

The Malta Cricket League started on the 8th May and ended on the 17th July. Fixtures and results were as follows:-

Overseas League Record for 1976

P12 - W6 - L6       Points 134

League won by M.S.C., Overseas 4th.

136

Throughout the summer Malta enjoyed good and exciting cricket from touring sides from U.K. In April we had the Speedbirds, a cricket organization of British Airways, and at the end of May we had a team from Panteg, Glamorganshire, who chose Malta for their centenary celebrations. Then, at the end of August, the Old Boys of the Royal Grammar School, Worcester, under the name of the Old Vigornians, visited us. The end of the season was more like a cricket festival. Starting late September we had the Blighters from Cheshire and Lancashire, followed in quick succession by the Mendip Acorns from the West Country, 2 - 10 October, Bill Frindall's XI, 10 - 17 October, and finally the Forty Club, 18 October. The touring sides played against individual Civilian and Services sides, Combined Civilian XIs, Combined Services XIs, and also against the full Malta XIs. Overseas played the Old Vigornians on September 2nd and Mendip Acorns on October 2nd. The Forty Club included Fred Trueman, and the Mendip Acorns included Don Shepherd, amongst their players.

The season produced a veritable feast of cricket at the Marsa from April to October in which Overseas members played a full part. For Overseas, in spite of some good wins in the league, our success was limited until late in the season when we reached the final of the 1976 Government Tourist Board Trophy for the first time. The final was held on the 23rd October and here we came off second best to the M.S.C. Overseas Team Captain, Mike Newton, in describing our improvement in play, said Overseas had found a real gem in Ken Dobell, his last few knocks being 117, 33, 73 not out, 65 not out, and 35 not out, plus Trevor batting like a man inspired and the steady batting of Gerry Davey, so our fortune with the bat had taken a turn very much for the better. We could look forward to next season with very much more confidence.

SOCIAL FUNCTIONS

Throughout the 1975/76 season we had a very full calendar of events. It was a very successful year. All Club and Rugby Section Social Functions were excellently organized by John Hughes, General and Rugby Section Social Secretary, backed by the hard work of Martin Crossfield, Bar Manager, and James Andrews, General Treasurer, who kept the bar stocked. James, successor to Niall Armstrong as General Manager of Andrews Feeds, was responsible to his firm for the continued use of their premises at Flagstone Wharf by the Club.

Again we must thank Jack Sharp for the film shows throughout the year, whether at the fortnightly club event on the first and third Thursday of each month, or on the many other occasions, including Committee evenings. They were very much appreciated by all who enjoyed Jack's hospitality.

One never likes to see members leaving Malta, but the official functions given to Club Officials prior to their departure were a great excuse for all members to get together. This season they were excellently organized by John Hughes and Trevor Ricketts, General Secretary, and were approached with a great sense of humour. The events were organized under the guise of a 'quiet drink' and the recipients were greatly surprised to be led into a 'noisy' social function arranged for their benefit. They were a success socially and enjoyed by members, especially by the person so honoured. The first occasion was on the 4th October, when a Farewell Cold Buffet and Dance was organized for Niall and Carol Armstrong at Tigne Beach Club, Tigne. At the end of the season, on the 3rd July, the President, Dave Taylor, and his wife Marjorie, were also given a Farewell Cold Buffet Dance at Tigne Beach Club, and finally, on the 8th July Amy and I were honoured by a Farewell Dinner at the Crystal Hotel, Bugibba. Other enjoyable and successful Farewell Parties were arranged privately, which all added to the social scene and comradery.

Great effort and no little expense was put into entertaining Energiovinvest, the visiting team from Yugoslavia. The Disco & Buffet organized for them at Marsa Lodge on the 24th March did not come up to expectations, mainly through lack of support, although the expense was considered acceptable in terms of the goodwill created between Overseas and Energiovinvest. The final cost to the Club of hosting the visitors was £65.81. There was a definite language barrier as only their Tour Manager, Marko Protega, spoke fairly good English, but they enjoyed themselves at all functions arranged for them. They were particularly interested in a rugby film showing games played by the British Lions on one of their tours. They took their rugby very seriously indeed and drank very little intoxicating liquor on this tour. They were also entertained by Jack Sharp at the M.U.F.C. Valletta. Whilst still on the subject of the tourists, I must add to what I have already written about the language difficulty. Whilst Marko was the only one who could converse fully in English, one or two of the others spoke some English, whilst none of the hosts could speak any of the three major languages used in Yugoslavia.

The Annual Dinner Dance, successfully organized by John Hughes was held at the Old Villa Rosa, St. George's Bay, St. Julians, on the 3rd April. We were a little cramped for space and numbers had to be kept down to 65 doubles. Actually, approximately 48 couples attended. The only official guest invited, although unable to attend, was the President of the National Sports Board, Dr. Benny Camilleri. Each Section of the Club also organized their own Section Dinner to which all members were welcome. Other functions held included a Stagnight (9th October), a Cheese & Wine Party (13th November), a Games Evening (27th November) and a Children’s Christmas Party (18th December).

After 4 years as Hon. Secretary, followed by 3 years as Hon. General Secretary, Trevor Ricketts was honoured by being elected the 12th President of the Club. It was an honour well deserved. The Office of Hon. General Secretary was taken over by Charlie Fitches.

Steering Committee for the Run Down of the Club

With the 7-year Defence Agreement between Malta and Britain due to end in March, 1979, and the consequent complete withdrawal of all British Forces and U.K. Based Civilians from Malta, there exists the very real possibility that on or before that date the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club will be forced to close down. Besides the obvious problem of lack of numbers, there is the question of whether the Maltese, members and non-members, have sufficient interest to keep the non-Maltese sports of rugby and cricket alive in Malta. As for soccer and hockey, especially with soccer being the Maltese national game, the question is whether there would be the continued need for 'Overseas' XI's. All sections of the Club have already felt the strain of decreasing numbers and lack of fixtures as the British Forces have gradually withdrawn, but the testing time will finally arrive when the last of the British Service Schools, Tal Handaq and Luqa, close in July, 1978. The biggest proportion of our present membership comes from the Service schools, particularly S.C.S. Tal Handaq, and to a lesser extent from the Services. With this in mind, in February, 1977, at the suggestion of the General Secretary, Mr C. Fitches, the Overseas General Committee formed a Steering Committee to consider the future activities of the Club, and ultimately to make recommendations with regard to the distribution and eventual disposal of the Club's funds.

The Steering Committee was formed from members of the General Committee and was made up as follows:

Messrs C. Fox (Chairman), J. Sharp, J. Andrews and B. Leonard

The Steering Committee met twice during the second half of the 1976/77 season, and having examined the full list of members, both playing and social, the Chairman, Mr. C. Fox,

139

was able to report to the A.G.M. on the 30th September, 1977, that subject to the continued availability of the Marsa Pitch, rugby will continue for another season (1977/78), we shall have a soccer and hockey team, and that we shall enjoy cricket at least until the end of July, 1978. At the same time the Steering Committee decided that there might just be a possibility of leaving a nucleus of an Overseas, in a much reduced form, here after 1979.

The Steering Committee's suggestion that interested members of the Services and the University might be co-opted on the General Committee to ensure that the game of rugby will continue after this season, was adopted by the General Committee.

Finances

At the end of 1976/77 the Hon. General Treasurer, Mr. J. Andrews, was able to report that available funds amounted to £M225.13, and that the U.K. balance stood at £123.37. This was attributed not only to the healthy profit from the Bar of £M175.61, a figure considerably higher than in recent years, but also to all social functions being financially successful. The financial position of the Club was described as being very sound, and in his end of year report the President was able to thank James Andrews for his meticulous book-keeping and his desire to sort out problems at any time.

In addition to the above, the sum of £M172 was still owing to the Club from the sale of T.Shirts. This was a project in which Jeff Bonner had 200 White T.Shirts printed with the name of Overseas Rugby & Sports Club, Malta, a Maltese Cross incorporating the initials ORSC, and a picture of the Maltese Islands. It was not only financially sound and the shirts popular, but it was a means of spreading the word about the Club in Malta, and in the U.K.

Membership

In 1976/77, a difficult year in which the withdrawal of the British Forces and U.K. Based Civilians was beginning to show in the Club's membership strength, the Membership Secretary, Mr. Alan Latham, was able to report a fully paid up membership of 77, including 5 students. A difficult job in difficult time, added to the fact that due to the relaxed nature of rugby in Malta, it was virtually impossible to insist all players were members. These figures compare with previous years as follows:- 

    1973/74    96 members including 25 students
    1974/75    87 members including 1 student
    1975/76    130 members including no students

Over the years the task of Membership Secretary had almost always been carried out by the Hon. Secretary, and it was not until 1973/74, when the membership increased on Overseas becoming a Sports Club, that it was accepted as necessary for one man to be in sole charge of membership. In 1975/76 the rules of the Club were amended to add the Membership Secretary to the list of full members of the General Committee.

RUGBY SECTION 1976/77

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 21, Flagstone Wharf,
Marsa, 30th September, 1976.

J. Andrews
J.A. Hughes

C.P.O. M. Kirk and P.O. W. Wood
F/O G. Laing

In spite of the problems by the gradual run-down of membership, Overseas continued to field two teams throughout the season, although at times with great difficulty, and with great pressure on the Rugby Section Committee. It was increasingly difficult to put out a full XV. The pressures came to a head at the back end of 1976 when, Mr. Jack Sharp, temporarily resigned. And although struggling to continue with our high standards, we maintained a full fixture list, albeit it was amongst the same few teams. Our problems increased late in the season when unfortunately the 'B' Team Captain, Mr. Marcel Cassar, cracked his ribs during a game.

The number of senior rugby XV's in Malta now stood at 4 i.e. Overseas, 41 Commando, the R.A.F. and the Army, with the occasional visiting H.M. ship. With so few resident teams it was a credit to the Joint Services Rugby Committee that they managed to keep a full fixture list. Our Representative on this Committee was Brian Charnley, Overseas Team Captain. At 'B' Team level, besides the 'B' teams of the participants at senior team level, we also had teams from St. Edward's College, De la Salle College, the University of Malta, and the S.C.S., Tal Handaq. The fact that these Colleges and the University were fielding XV's is the brighter side of the season, and of great pleasure to the Overseas Club. It was a reward in itself to the present and past Committees, both at General and Rugby Section level, who had worked so hard over a number of years to interest and encourage the game locally. Also, it was an added pleasure that the number of Maltese playing in Overseas XV's and joining the Club increased during the season.

Once again, at Both A and B team levels, the rugby standard of 41 Commando was too high for other teams on the island and Overseas suffered several defeats in fixtures with them. The season started off disastrously for Overseas on the 3rd October, 1976, with a 50-20 defeat by the Army, and ended on the 24th April, 1977, with a milder defeat, 13-10, by H.M. Yacht Britannia. The season was quite long for Malta. Our standard improved during the season with one or two new players, and the return of one or two old hands, including the President, Trevor Ricketts, and over the season we finished about even against the R.A.F. and the Army. The Young Player of the Year Cup was awarded to Alex Darmanin.

Thursday evening indoor training, organized by Brian Charnley,

Commenced on the 3rd December in the gymnasium of Tal Handaq School, by kind permission of the School Authorities. The Club rugby training films were now held by Marcel Cassar, who acted as Librarian. The films were now coming into their own as different bodies were interested in using them, including the R.A.F., and the new teams of the University and the Colleges.

Again, through the good offices of Jack Sharp, Rugby Section Chairman, the Secretary of the National Sports Board, Mr. Colin Cachia, gave Overseas permission to use the rugby pitch at the Marsa on Saturdays and Sundays for Club games, and on Mondays, Wednesdays and Fridays during the week for schoolboy training. Later in the season certain restrictions were imposed on the use of the pitch on training days, and on the odd occasion, such as the weekend of the 11th/12th December, we were unable to use the pitch due to local soccer being played there. During the season the Services did not need to use the Marsa for their home games. 41 Commando, with a Club House at R.A.F. Safi, now had their own pitch at Hal Far, and the R.A.F. still had their own pitch at Safi. The Colleges, University and Tal Handaq all used the one pitch at the Marsa with their games being played Monday to Friday. Through the good offices of the Naval Sports Officer, Lt. Dixon, and the R.N. Representative on the Rugby Section Committee, C.P.O. M. Kirk, the Overseas Club looked after the marking of the Marsa pitch and general care of the posts etc. During this season the Overseas Club had every reason to be grateful to the Representatives of the 3 Services who sat on the Rugby Section Committee. Not only for work done for the Club, but also for advice in Committee, and for the continued spirit of co-ordination of Overseas and Service Rugby.

The most important aspect of the season was the continued interest and improvement in the game shown by St. Edward's College and De la Salle College, and the starting of the game at the Royal University of Malta. The Colleges and S.C.S. Tal Handaq had joint training sessions during the week at the Marsa under Mr. Ricketts and Mr. Charnley. The University players were well coached by Marcel Cassar and not only provided 'B' team opposition themselves, but were keen enough to play for Overseas 'B' team on the occasion, also to join in Overseas Training. The first game played by the University (R.U.M.) team was on the 25th November versus Overseas 'B' at the Marsa and this was great credit to Marcel. Mr. Charnley undertook to deal with coaching and other requirements of the various College Rugby sections. In November he informed the Rugby Section Committee that with 4 Colleges/School/R.U.M. in Malta there was the basis of a Junior League, and by January he reported that Tal Handaq, De la Salle and St. Edward's were now playing each other fairly regularly. The R.U.M. players proved too big for schoolboy rugby. The only disappointment was that St. Aloysius College, although interested, did not field a team, in spite of Mr. Sharp, Rugby Section Chairman, approaching the College suggesting schoolboy coaching. In March, Mr. Charnley ran an inter-College/School competition with St. Edward's, De la Salle and Tal Handaq taking part, and this proved a great success. At the time of the competition the R.U.M. were unable to field a side. Mr. Charnley said that the objectives in promoting a school's competition had been achieved.

At the start of the season the Rugby Section Committee looked into the possibility of an Overseas party making a return visit

142

to Makarska, near Split, Yugoslavia, at the invitation of the
Energoinvest Rugby Club. The cost proved prohibitive.
Investigations had also been going on into a more economical
tour to Messina and in answer to initial enquiries by Mr.
Ewan MacPherson, Rugby Section Secretary, the Centro Universitario
Sportivo (CUS), Messina, invited Overseas to tour. This offer
was accepted. After a great deal of further correspondence,
telephone calls and telegrams on the part of Jack Sharp, Ewan
Macpherson and James Andrews (Vice-Captain), the tour was
finally arranged for the 13-17 April, 1977. Unfortunately,
after all their efforts, the tour had to be cancelled on the
11th April due to lack of support from Overseas members. At
the time of cancellation only 13 players were available and
this comprised 8 Overseas members, including Trevor Ricketts
hoping to make his second tour to Messina, and 5 guests from
41 Commando (3) and the R.A.F. (2). This had been looked upon
as the last possible chance for an Overseas XV to make a tour.
The money to enable the tour to be made, a total of £475, had
been raised by a series of raffles, mostly at film nights, profit
from a disco in November, and from tickets, cabaret and raffle
at the Rugby Section Dinner Dance. Added to this the Steering
Committee (on run down of Club) had recommended to the General
Committee that a grant of £475 be made towards the expenses of
the proposed tour. At the suggestion of Mr. Sharp, 6 volunteers
for the tour who had been inconvenienced to a significant extent
by the cancellation were given complimentary tickets for the
Club's Annual Dinner Dance, at a cost of £130, also tankards
and ties were bought for those leaving (£10.95). The remainder
of the money raised was donated to the Cricket League Tour to
Corfu. Earlier in the season two U.K. Teams, the West Midlands
Police and Merthyr R.F.C., contacted Overseas requesting they
tour Malta possibly at Easter. These contacts came to nothing.
Fortunately, H.M.S. Hermes were visiting Malta at Easter, 1977
and enjoyable games were played against the Hermes and the
Glamorgan on the 9th and 10th April, also H.M. Yacht Britannia
on the 24th April.

During the summer of 1977 the Team Captain, Brian Charnley,
and Bill Wood left Malta, and so the Overseas XV lost two of its
most consistant players and leading try scorers of the two seasons,
1975-77, added to which Brian had been one of the recognised
goal kickers. Both had represented Overseas in Combined XV's
and Bill played for the Navy (Malta) and usually in any Combined
Service XV's in Malta. Brian, who had been in charge of school-
boy rugby coaching and other requirements of the College rugby
sections during 1976/77 would also be missed in future school
rugby development. As Team Captain he had represented Overseas
on the J.S.R.C. and for his second and final year he had been a
Vice-President of the Club. Both men hard to replace.

SOCCER SECTION 1976/77

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 16th September, 1976

Again the Soccer Section had a difficult year in putting out a team in both the Major and Minor Leagues. As with all sections of the Club, the Soccer Section was increasingly feeling the effects of the imminent withdrawal from Malta. In spite of this, in the words of the President, Trevor Ricketts, in his end of season report, the Soccer Section, under the general leadership of Jeff Bonner, again managed to fulfil their obligations in the Services' League and equip themselves fairly well, a tremendous spirit spread throughout the whole team. Jeff himself confirmed this in saying that as one can see from results, football was a struggle this year, but I think we all enjoyed ourselves nevertheless.

HOCKEY SECTION 1976/77

Chairman P. Marchant
Hon Secretary D. Walker
Hon Treasurer P. Marchant
Hon Social Secretary D. Walker
Team Captain C. Fitches
Vice-Captain D. Walker

Overseas Hockey XI started off the season in fine style by beating 234 Signal Squadron. However, this high standard was rarely emulated again during the season for various reasons, mainly the unavailability of players. Indeed, it became increasingly difficult to meet our league commitments, although this was at times because the opposition cancelled matches, and it was not always possible to accommodate the offered return fixtures.

The high standard was again produced in the Services Knock-out Cup. On the way to the final we defeated 234 Signal Squadron by 5-1 and St. Angelo by 3-1, and in the final we held the powerful 41 Commando to a goalless draw at full time, only to be defeated in extra time by sheer stamina.

Due to the gradual withdrawal of different Service Units from Malta the League was sadly depleted with only 5 teams taking part, namely, Overseas, 234 Signal Squadron, St. Angelo (Navy) R.A.F., and 41 Commando. Opposition was difficult to find, and at the end of the season 4 league fixtures were unplayed.

When at full strength Overseas Hockey Team for 1976/77 ably led by Charles Fitches, was probably one of the strongest and most successful teams in the Section's history. Our fast and hard hitting forward line included John Whitehead, who set the standard for the team and was our leading striker and goal scorer, ably supported by Ken Dobell. The team this year did not include any lady members.

Players for 1976/77 were: C. Fitches (Captain); D. Walker, (Vice-Captain); P. Marchant; J. Whitehead; M. Crossfield; K. Dobell; G. Davey; H. Ritchie; T. Ricketts; J. Slide; S. Newman; D. Longlands. Tal Handaq Boys, D. North; S. Oliver; M. Beresford.

Left Malta in July, 1977: K. Dobell, S. Newman, D. Longlands, D. North; M. Beresford.

Hockey League - 'Overseas'
P4 - W1 - L3

CRICKET SECTION 1977

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 3rd March.

Section Committee

Chairman          M.F. Plummer

Hon. Secretary    M. Newton

Hon. Treasurer    M. Caseley

Hon. Social Secretary   J. Hughes

Team Captain      G. Davey

Vice-Captain       D. Walker

Selection Committee   G. Davey, D. Walker, J. Sharp.

New Overseas members included an Australian, a Sri Lankan and a Pakistani, all teachers at the Libyan Polytechnic. Unfortunately, we had lost the services of Mike Shaw, described as the best wicket keeper on the Island.

Overseas started off the 1977 cricket season on a high note by winning the traditional curtain raiser, the league 6-a-side K.O. Competition, on the 23rd April. We entered 3 teams out of a total of 20. Unfortunately, our standard was inconsistent due to the fact that our team was severely weakened at times by key players being unavailable. Consequently, in spite of several good wins when at full strength, we finished the league 5th out of 8. League honours were carried by 41 Commando who were worthy winners. The 8 League teams came from the Army, the Royal Navy, Overseas, 41 Commando, with the R.A.F. and the M.S.C. each producing 2.

Sat   30 Apr vs 41 Cdo      Lost   41Cdo 200-6, Overseas 115-9

Sat   14 May vs Army      Won   Overseas 176-4, Army 107

                                   Ricketts 100

Sat   21 May vs RAF Penguins     Won   Overseas 176-6, Penguins 168-8

Sat   28 May vs MSC Nomads   Won   Nomads 147-9, Overseas 152-5

Fri   3 Jun vs MSC                  Lost   Overseas 174-9, MSC 175-5

Fri   1 Jul vs RAF Penguins       Lost   Overseas 165-6, Penguins 166-5

Wed   6 Jul vs Royal Navy    Won   Overseas 244-6, R.N. 113-9

Sat   9 Jul vs MSC                 Won   MSC 112-9, Overseas 114-8

Tue   19 Jul vs RAF Puffins       Lost   Overseas 149-7, Puffins 150-2

Overseas League Record for 1977 P14 - W7 - L7

Once again our most consistent scorers were our opening batsmen, Gerry Davey and Trevor Ricketts. Both men represented Overseas on the Malta Select XI on 4 occasions, and performed with distinction. Alain Latham was our best bowler, taking 21 wickets in the league on a wicket which favoured the batsmen.

In the single wicket competition Gerry Davey was beaten by Ray Stringer in the final. Ray was himself an Overseas Player, but represented 41 Commando in this competition.

On the 11th September, for the second year running, we reached the final of the Government Tourist Board Trophy, only to be defeated by the R.A.F. Puffins by two wickets in a very exciting match. Our opponents in rounds 1 and 2 were the M.S.C.

147

and the Navy respectively. In defeating the Navy, Gerry Davey scored 104, and Trevor Ricketts 99, out of a total score of 246-4.

Throughout the season 8 talented cricketing sides toured Malta, for the most part old friends, starting with the Speedbirds C.C. in May. The other visitors were Mendip Acorns in June, followed closely by newcomers the Sheffield Cricket Lovers from Yorkshire. At the end of August came Old Vigornians from Worcester and in September the Nottingham Select and the Blighters. In October the season was brought to a close by the Mendip Acorns again, the Forty Club and Bill Frindall's XI. All the touring sides played Combined Service and/or Combined Civilian teams, and each touring side played different individual teams. For the Cricket Festival in October, we had no less than 3 Overseas players selected for the Malta squad, plus two other members who were playing under another flag. Overseas played against Nottingham Select on the 24th September, and we were the only side to register a win over them. We also played against Mendip Acorns on the 15th October, and in this game we were narrowly beaten. Both these touring sides contained county players.

Sat 24 Sep vs Nottingham Select                          Won Nottingham 237-7, Overseas 241-4: Davey 119

Sat 15 Oct vs Mendip Acorns                         Lost Overseas 194, Mendip Acorns 195-3

Overseas 2nd XI played 4 matches, their opponents being the Navy (twice), Malta Sports Club 2nd XI, and Tal Handaq.

The Malta Cricket League tour to Corfu, 22nd August to 2nd September, was a great success, and in spite of some very patriotic umpiring, the tourists managed to win 2 out of 5 games played. The touring party included 5 Overseas members, viz, Trevor Ricketts, Mike Newton, Dave Smith, Gerry Davey, and Brian Leonard. I am told that some of the tactics employed to ensure a home win were quite amusing though apt to spoil the game from a cricket point of view. However, the fact that the tour was enjoyable is borne out by the fact that the Overseas President, Trevor Ricketts, has threatened to retire in Corfu.

As in all sections of 'Seas' team spirit remained high throughout what was possibly the penultimate season for the Cricket Section, indeed, under the Captaincy and example of Gerry Davey, and the Vice-Captaincy of Dave Walker, the spirit and standard have never been higher. With all players available the Overseas XI of 1977 had a very powerful look.

Going back to 1973, the year Overseas became a Sports Club, in mentioning those members who have given a great deal to Overseas Cricket Section, on and off the field, to the fore would have to come Trevor Ricketts and Mike Newton. Trevor, as ever, the driving force behind Seas, and a prolific scorer of runs, was Chairman and Vice-Captain in 1973, and Captain for two years, 1974-75. Mike Newton, Secretary for 3 years, 1974-75 and 1977, Captain 1976 and Vice-Captain 1975. One member who has missed watching very few Overseas matches over many years is Jack Sharp. Jack, whose encouragement is always welcome, was elected on the Selection Committee for 1977. Others, always there, and who contributed a great deal to Overseas, to mention only a few, Ralph Doley, one of the Founder Members of the Cricket Section in 1965, Captain 1973; Peter Wright; Dave Taylor; Mike Shaw; Lew Finnis; Treasurer 1973-75; Alan Latham, Chairman 1974-75; Mike Caseley, Chairman 1976, Treasurer 1977; Mike Plummer

Social Functions 1976/77

As with all sections of the Club, the Social Life suffered with the gradual run-down of membership, and the Social Secretary Mr. John Hughes, did not find it easy to keep things going. Nevertheless, the season proved to be very full, and very successful. Club nights, especially on film nights, were well supported by members. The films, again provided by Jack Sharp were shown fortnightly throughout the winter months, increasing to one per week during March (1977) in order to raise funds for the proposed rugby tour to Messina. The Social Secretary attempted, to no avail, to get members to accept invitations to other clubs. Functions held during the year included a Bonfire Party & Disco on the 14th November, 1976 and a Children's Christmas Party on the 21st December, 1976. Both were held at the Club House and were very successful. The Children's Party was run efficiently by Mike Newton and Alan Latham, with Bill Wood taking on the vital part of Santa Claus.

The Social life was livened by three successful and enjoyable Dinner Dances and also the main Club function of the year, the Annual Dinner Dance. The Cricket Section dance on the 13th November, 1976, and the Soccer Section dance organised by Tom Jordan, Soccer Section Social Secretary, on the 11th December, 1976, were both held at the Crystal Hotel, Bugibba, and the Rugby Section dance on the 1st March, 1977 was held at the Whisper Knight Club, Mosta. The Rugby Section event ended with an impromptu cabaret consisting of Trevor Ricketts and Bill Wood singing and Alex Darminin playing the piano, followed by that nightmare of all Club proprietors where rugby followers are concerned, the passing around of a rugby ball, produced by Team Captain, Brian Charnley in preparation for the week-end game. The Club Annual Dinner Dance was held at the Malta Sports Club on Saturday, 30th April, 1977, and was a great success enjoyed by 105 members and guests. The venue for the Annual Dinner Dance was chosen for sentimental reasons, as well as the fact that functions held there have always been a success. It was felt by the President and Committee that it would be nice to return to the place which had been our home for such social occasions for many years, in view of the very depressing fact that this could be the last to be held by the Club. The season ended with the usual round of parties given by or for the members leaving and this included Overseas Farewell 'Do' for John Hughes, also for Brian Charnley, Team Captain, on Thursday, 30th June, 1977. John left Malta on the 23rd July, and this was the Club's loss. Not only had he been Social Secretary of the Main Club for the 2 years, 1975-77, but also Social Secretary of the Rugby and Cricket Sections during the same period, plus Social Secretary for the Hockey Section in 1976/77, and he gave a great deal of his time and energy to ensure that all the functions he arranged were a success, socially and financially. John also enjoyed his game of rugby. Brian has been mentioned in the Rugby Section 1976/77. Although, as Social Secretary, John Hughes was the front man, a great deal of credit for a successful season must be given to the Bar Manager, Martin Crossfield, also to James Andrews, Hon. General Treasurer, and who, as General Manager of Andrews Feeds, looked after the Club House premises on behalf of the firm, and did most of the buying and delivering of stock.

Steering Committee for the Run-Down of the Club

At the A.G.M. on the 22nd September, 1977, the President of the Club, Mr. T.N. Ricketts, asked all members to support the Club and to make this, our possible final year, one to remember - be it in celebrations or high standards on the field. He also asked members to accept the findings of the Steering Committee and to support them in whatever they might suggest.

The Steering Committee made two recommendations to the new Committee at the A.G.M., both recommendations being discussed at the General Committee Meeting held on the 24th October, 1977.

  1. To donate a suitable trophy to be competed for annually by the local schools and the University.
  2. To provide for the renovation of one of the Marsa changing rooms, with a commemorative plaque in the name of the Overseas Rugby & Sports Club.

On the first recommendation, the President asked for a delay in its discussion until the level of schools participation be

150

known - the Rugby Section was asked to activate discussion when this became known. The second was held in abeyance in view of the fact that one of the changing rooms had already been improved.

In the early part of the 1977/78 season the Steering Committee continued its deliberations into the possibility of the Club surviving in some form after the British presence was withdrawn from Malta by the 31st March, 1979. By January, 1978, no concrete recommendations had been made by the Steering Committee as to the future of the Club. This delay was due in part to the fact that the Minister of Sport, Mr. L. Sant, was showing an interest in sports in general in Malta, and as far as Overseas was concerned, in rugby in particular, and in part to the encouraging results from the Club's efforts to interest the playing of rugby by the University and Colleges in Malta. As opposed to this encouraging interest, the Steering Committee had to weigh up the many problems, to try to decide as to whether it was practical to keep the Club alive after the withdrawal, before putting forward any proposal. The Club would be left in the hands of the few members left behind after the Service schools close in July, 1978, and even more so after March, 1979.

In February, 1978, the matter was 'more or less' taken out of the Steering Committee's hands and returned to the General Committee by the fact that a number of Maltese members of the Rugby Section strongly expressed a wish that the Overseas Club and Rugby Section should continue after the 1977/78 season. The General Committee agreed that all encouragement must be given to trying to keep rugby, and therefore the Club, alive, and at the suggestion of Jack Sharp, Rugby Section Chairman, two Maltese members, David Schembri and Marcel Cassar, were co-opted onto the General Committee to take part in any discussion on the future of the Club, particularly reference rugby. Both members were already serving on the Rugby Section Committee, David Schembri as liaison between the Club and the Government Schools, and Marcel Cassar as liaison between the Club and Private Schools, U.S. School, and the Royal University of Malta.

Although the Overseas General and Section Committees wished it otherwise, it was generally accepted, that with the withdrawal taking its toll of playing strength, 1977/78 was the last season for the Soccer and Hockey Sections, and the Cricket Section would close in July, 1978. It is interesting to note that all Committee Members of the Soccer and Hockey Sections, and all but one of the Cricket Section, are schoolmasters at the British Service schools in Malta, and they leave en bloc in July, 1978, when the said schools close down for the last time. Here I must stress, that because of the problems of printing and distribution whilst there are sufficient members still in Malta who might be interested in reading it, the writing of this history must be completed by the beginning of May, and final decisions regarding the sections mentioned in this paragraph must, of necessity, be made by the General Committee after this date.

For many years, first as Overseas Rugby Club, then as Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, we have made continuous efforts to create interest in rugby amongst the Maltese people and therefore, the fact that there should be such a strong wish amongst the Maltese members to keep 'Overseas' alive as a Rugby Club, was most pleasing and rewarding. Although problems had been increasing over the years as the Services gradually withdrew as a general policy, and would increase further when the Service schools close down in July, 1978, the testing point, as to whether the Club can

survive, even as a Rugby Club, will come when the Services finally and completely withdraw at the end of March, 1979. The main problems to be overcome will be our own lack of membership and so the ability to put out a XV when required, the lack of opposition, and referees. After March, 1979, Overseas will be the only senior team on the Island, and in 1977/78 the only referees to officiate in senior games at least, have been British Servicemen. At junior level in the Colleges, particularly over two seasons, 1976-78, the interest in rugby has increased, and this must surely be where the answer lies. The Club will also need the blessing of the Minister of Sport in order to continue to use the rugby pitch at the Marsa.

With the knowledge that in July, 1978, almost all members of the General Committee, including the President, would be leaving Malta, the General Committee has decided to call an Extraordinary General Meeting of all interested members on the 8th June, 1978. The purpose of this meeting is to discuss the future composition of the Club and to elect Committee Members to cover the vital interim period prior to the next A.G.M., normally held in September.

Terminal Awards

With so many Members leaving Malta during the present season it was apparent that to present all with the normal 'going away tankard' would be beyond the Club's means. To alleviate the problem the President advised the Sections to bear in mind the criteria, that those members qualifying should have performed good service to the Club, either as players or in the sphere of administration, not just be good players.

CLUB TIES

A further, and perhaps final order, for Club Ties was placed with Alex Brook Ltd., London. The design chosen was a single Club motif, white on navy blue, incorporating 30 years. A tie for members to value and to remind them of a great Club.

Long Serving Members

To try to write about all members leaving in this final year (definitely final for many) is an impossible task. Besides the numbers leaving, there are those who have taken office whilst I have been away from Malta, and I have not had sufficient written material to draw from. In saying this, I am thinking of such members as Charlie Fitches, who to say the least, must have been a very good and competent General Secretary to have taken over from such a person as Trevor Ricketts. However, I would like to mention the following long serving members.

Frank Kitson

On the 4th January, 1978, a dinner was given in Frank's honour shortly before he left Malta after 18 years as a valued member of Overseas. As one of his contemporaries, Jeff Bonner, wrote, certainly a very sad loss to Club, School, and indeed to anyone that knew him. It is easier to list the service Frank gave to the Club, although I have previously mentioned him as an outstanding player in 1962/63.

Jack Sharp

Our President, Trevor Ricketts, aptly described Jack Sharp as the father figure of the Club. How true. Jack has taken such an active part in running the Club for so long that it is difficult to imagine the Club being without his always available advice and 'know-how'. No one has done more for the Club than Jack. For the Club's sake, it is unfortunate that Jack is retiring in June this year, and although not certain of his movements, will perhaps find it impossible to take on a permanent office in what is surely the most difficult year in the Club's history. Having said this, all his many friends wish him and his wife Dorothy all happiness and good health in the future, and thank them both for what they have readily given to the Club over the years, and perhaps more so for personal friendship and kindness.

Although I have listed below many of the offices undertaken by Jack, it is impossible to name the many diverse ways he has helped the Club. It is impossible to overestimate his contact with the Maltese Ministry, particularly the Minister of Sport, on the Club's behalf, for the very many times he has acted as host to Overseas Committees, Members and other functions, his direct contact with the Colleges appertaining to rugby participation, and not least for providing all the necessities for Film Evenings at the Club House.

Trevor Ricketts

On a previous page, when I wrote about Trevor being elected an Hon. Life Member, I gave details of all the sterling work he had done, and has continued to do, for Overseas and sport in general in Malta. I reiterate what I said on that occasion. Trevor has given a certain vitality and efficiency to Committee work in his 7 years as Hon. Secretary/Hon. General Secretary, and I believe this has been mirrored in the Committee and the regard in which the Club is held.

Trevor was elected President at the 1976/77 Annual General Meeting, and he celebrated his first year in office by, once again, playing for all sections of the Club. Trevor's term as President has coincided with the run-down of the Club, and this is doubly sad for a person who has done so much to keep the name of Overseas in such high regard in the sporting world on the Island. It is also unfortunate for Overseas that Trevor leaves Malta in July, 1978, but decisions taken before that date will decide the future of the Club, and under his Chairmanship I believe the right decisions will be made.

The start of the 1977/78 season, a season which was generally believed to be the last, started in a most unusual way. The Minister of Sport, Mr. L. Sant, in order to promote rugby in Malta, invited a team of ex Italian internationals, S.S. Vecchia Roma, to play games in Malta against the Combined Services, on the 23rd September, and a Maltese Select, on the 25th September. Normally, no rugby is played in Malta until the ground is softened by rain, later in the year as that might be, and the pitches at this time were like concrete. However, two weeks of watering made the pitches playable, although still described as hazardous.

The Maltese Select/S.S. Vecchia Roma game was sponsored by the Minister of Sport, and he invited a Spanish Coach, Senor Gonzales, now resident in Italy, to prepare the Maltese Select players for the great day. The Maltese Select XV, formed by the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, consisting of as many Maltese players as possible, lost a hard but very enjoyable game 18 points to 10. Mr. Sant was present during the whole of this game and was presented to both teams before the kick off. After the game we were honoured by Mr. S. Inglott from the Ministry of Sport visiting Overseas Club House. On the 23rd September, the Combined Services beat S.S. Vecchia Roma by 20 points to 19.

Maltese Select: J. Gerada, M. Cassar, A. Mamo, A. Darmanin, F. Roberts, B. Gibson, D. Schembri, E. Macpherson, A. Hempensdall, D. Watson, D. Tarrant, R. Fabri, S. Mangion, J. Adourian, J. Andrews (Captain), M. Crossfield, C. Borda, T. Long

In June, 1977, Overseas sent a letter to the Minister of Sport giving him a brief history of rugby in Malta and its future prospects. In acknowledging this letter the Minister suggested that a meeting be arranged. A similar letter was sent by the President to the Chairman of the Joint Services Sports Board, Colonel Seabrook. In his reply, the Colonel said he recognised the valuable work done by the Club in promoting rugby in Malta. The meeting took place in September, when a representative of the Ministry of Sport met representatives from Overseas and other rugby bodies interested in the game in Malta. Those present included Jack Sharp, James Andrews and Ewan Macpherson, of Overseas Club, and Paul Miller, in charge of R.A.F. rugby, also.

referees (Malta).

Prior to the start of the season, Mr. J. Sharp, Rugby Section Chairman, applied for and obtained permission from the Minister of Sport for Overseas to use the rugby pitch at the Mtarfa on Wednesday, Saturday and Sunday afternoons. Through the good offices of the Naval Sports Officer, Lt. Walker, the R.N. Representative on the Rugby Section Committee, C.P.O. M. Kirk, looked after the marking on the pitch.

The season started in earnest for Overseas on the 15th October with a game against H.M.S. Fearless, and even then the ground was described as being extremely hard. As in the previous season, the only teams to provide regular 1st team opposition were the R.A.F. and 41 Commando (Army), but perhaps the most noticeable difference was the lowering of the playing standards through lack of playing strength. This was particularly so with 41 Commando, no longer the dominant side of old. ‘B’ team opposition came mainly from the R.A.F. ‘B’ side, with single appearances by the Army ‘B’, St. Edward's College, De La Salle College, and a Services ‘B’ side. For Overseas it was not a great season resultwise, again the problem was lack of players who would commit themselves to playing regularly, although on the days when we had our best side out we looked as good as any team on the Island. It proved to be another frustrating season for Overseas as we fast became deplete of players as members left the Island with no replacements filling vacancies.

What I have written in the previous paragraph is consistent with all problems created by the run-down and imminent withdrawal of the British Forces from Malta, in the sphere of rugby during this season. That is one side of the coin. The other speaks of the hard work, and the constant living of rugby, by Jack Sharp (Chairman), James Andrews (Captain) Ewan Macpherson (Secretary and Vice-Captain), Marcel Cassar (B Team Captain) and David Scherini, in not only fielding a team throughout the season, but also in building a side for the future. The season started with the possibility that 1977/78 was to be the final rugby season for Overseas, and it ended with a determination, that in spite of the withdrawal, there was a future for Overseas, at least rugbywise, and for continued rugby in Malta. The main reasons for this optimism were (A) At a time when U.K. membership was decreasing there was a welcome increase in the number of Maltese players of reasonable standard in the Overseas teams. (B) The expressed wish of a number of the Maltese members that the Club and the Rugby Section should carry on in 1978/79. (C) The interest the Minister of Sport, Mr. L. Sant, had shown in promoting senior and junior rugby in Malta. I have spoken in this paragraph only of the work done by the Rugby Section Committee members, but all credit is due to our President, and the General Committee, where Section work is discussed, for the work done to keep the Overseas flag flying rugbywise.

In spite of the interest shown by the Minister of Sport, and the repeated offer by Overseas of coaching assistance, the interest shown by the Maltese Colleges during 1977/78 was disappointing, as only St. Edward's College fielded a team on a regular basis. The University had internal problems, although individual players still retained an interest in the game. At St. Edward's College, under the instruction of Father Ferro, the game was spreading, with about 60 boys in different age groups being coached in the game. De La Salle College also fielded a

196

team. At the Rugby Section A.G.M. David Schembri and Marcel
Cassar had been elected to sit on the Rugby Section Committee
to liaison with the Government and Private Schools respectively,
and both did a great deal to further the game in Malta. Jack
Sharp, Rugby Section Chairman, had also nominated David Schembri
and Marcel Cassar to the Minister of Sport as being able to do
much to assist him in his efforts to 'establish' the game of
rugby in Malta. In October, 1977, in an effort to interest the
Government Secondary Schools, David Schembri talked to the
Official in Charge of the Secondary Schools Federation who had
indicated a willingness to let rugby be tried out providing
Overseas produced 6 months coaching programme in advance,
and undertook to provide coaching. In turn the Overseas President
wrote to the Federation offering coaching assistance. To end the
season, the Minister of Sport intends to promote a Youth Tournament
for under 16s in May, 1978.

Recently I spoke with Father Ferro of St. Edward's College.
Besides telling me about the 3 rugby teams at the College, i.e.
under 13s, under 16s and 16+, he also told me something about
rugby in Malta in the past. It was most interesting. Father
Ferro told me he was in the R.M.A. for 30 years, and in 1923
he started playing rugby in Malta for a Service team called
the 'Pirates'. He played for the Pirates for 11 years until
forced to stop by ill health.

The highlight of the 1977/78 season in Malta was the visit
of the touring side from U.K., Moseley R.F.C., between the 23rd-
29th March, 1978. Arrangements had been made for them to play
4 games over the Easter period. The touring party of 39 members,
led by Tour Manager, Andy Petrie, and Moseley Club Secretary,
John Butt, included 32 players from their 3rd, 4th and 5th teams,
with a sprinkling of ex 1st team players. They made their own
arrangements for the tour and stopped at St. Paul's Court,
Bugibba, St. Paul's Bay. Moseley had previously toured Malta
in twice, 1975, and on the present tour they certainly found a
difference in the strength of the local teams, all weakened by
the loss of players. The tourists, proving far too good for
the opposition, won all 4 games. They played impressive rugby
and their handling and passing of the ball in the high winds
was excellent, as indeed was their backing up in all phases of
the game and speed to take advantage of opponents mistakes. I
was fortunate to be present at all 4 games and I was most
impressed with the spirit of the Overseas and Malta XVs,
individual talent, and the fact that, at a time when they were
needed most, there were 6 or 7 Maltese players on the field.
The Malta XV was formed from Overseas and the Services. For
Overseas and the Malta XV the players who stood out were the
talented and speedy back, S. Thomas, David Schembri in the
forwards, and great credit to the Captain, James Andrews, who
played at scrum half, a very unfamiliar position for him. For
Moseley, the star was their scrum half, Brian Powell. Overseas
entertained Moseley at the Malta Sports Club immediately after
the game on Saturday, 25th, followed by liquid refreshment in
Overseas Club House. Here David Schembri proved to be an entertainer
after the style of Charlie Rice, and Overseas proved they
could win, even it was only the gents and ladies boat races.
After the two Service games at Safi the tourists were entertained
in the R.A.F. Club at Safi.

Fri 24th Mar  R.A.F.          0 vs Moseley 33    Safi
Sat 25th     Overseas         6 vs Moseley 36    Marsa
Sun 26th     Malta XV         0 vs Moseley 49    Marsa
Mon 27th     Combined Services 4 vs Moseley 36   Safi

Referees: P. Miller, R. Eaton, M. Kirk A.N. Other

Overseas Team: S. Mangion, A. Darmanin, S. Thomas, S. Groom, M. Crossfield, P. Shannon, J. Andrews (Captain), E. Macpherson (Vice Captain), C. Borda, D. Holt, W. Ellul-Bonnici, D. Schembri, N. Caruana, R. Foulsham, D. Tarrant.

The Island Sevens, sponsored by the R.A.F. were held at Safi on the 19th March. Overseas entered 2 teams and our 'A' team was unfortunate to be beaten in the final of the Cup Competition by the R.A.F. 'A', 10 points to 8. Tal Handaq won the Plate Competition.

The last game of the season for Overseas was on the 14th May, 1978 when we beat H.M.S. Fearless 20-4.

In what is perhaps the last 'full' season of senior rugby in Malta, I would like to comment on the marvellous relationship between Overseas and the Services in organizing senior rugby on the Island, on an individual basis, and through the Joint Services Rugby Committee. Overseas is represented on the J.S.R.C. by the Team Captain, and its credit to this body that such a full fixture list has been kept, especially in the last two years, with so few resident teams. This co-operation has existed since the Club was formed in 1946, and it has given rugby in Malta a sound base to work from. I have said it is perhaps the last full season, because, in spite of the wish to keep Overseas going as a Rugby Club, I have been told by both Navy and R.A.F. organizers that it will be very difficult, if not impossible, for either Service to put out teams next year. If I have not always given due praise to the different services for their part in the Rugby life of Malta, it is only because of the lack of time and space, and I have had to keep to the history of Overseas.

I have already mentioned the hard work done by members of the Committee, but others who also deserve praise are those, such as Charlie and Doris Borda, who are always there when called on. I certainly did not expect to see Charlie play rugby again after a serious operation two years ago. Doris has been looking after the jerseys all season, and is constantly working for the club. I am also thinking of such good members as Margaret Mcpherson, and Carol Crossfield, who along with Doris Borda have done much work preparing food for social functions at the club, and also cleaning and tidying up before and afterwards. I must include also Dorothy Sharp, Maria Schembri, Margaret Newton and Liz Andrews for the constant support they give the Club. Of the Committee, it is hoped that Jack Sharp, in his retirement, will be available at times to give advice. Unfortunately, Ewan Macpherson, Secretary, leaves Malta in October, 1978, although fortunate, with his experience of rugby and the running of the club, he will be there to tide the Club over the next A.G.M., usually held in September. For the future, a great deal will rest on the shoulders of James Andrews who has done so much for the Club over two seasons, even though he has threatened to hang up his boots, the rugby experience and club knowledge of David Schembri, Marcel Cassar, Charlie Borda, and others, and most important, those who are elected at the Extra- ordinary General Meeting to be held in June, 1978 to form an interim Committee, and perhaps form the next Committee at the A.G.M. I wish Overseas well in the future.

I wish to acknowledge the great help given to me by Jack Sharp, James Andrews and Ewan Macpherson, in collecting information about Overseas Rugby Section and Rugby in Malta, whether it be by correspondence, making Section minutes and records available to me, or in person.

SOCCER SECTION

In asking Jeff Bonner, Hon. Secretary, Soccer Section, to check details for the year 1977/78, he was kind enough to do so, and at the same time he expressed the view that I had not named enough players. Accordingly he wrote an excellent short history of the Section and at the same time giving details of players going back to 1966. I believe many present and past members will be interested in Jeff's work, and although he has repeated some details already covered, I will copy it in its entirety.

First I will give the usual yearly report.

SOCCER SECTION 1977/78

nual General Meeting, 15th September, 1977.

Chairman           T.N. Ricketts
Hon. Secretary     J.J. Bonner
Hon. Treasurer     D.G. Smith
Hon. Social Secretary T.G. Jordan
Team Captain       J.J. Bonner
Vice-Captain       D.G. Smith

In what appears to be the final year in which the Soccer Section will function, their fortunes have been very mixed. In the Major League, the Corinthians did exceptionally well, winning 8 out of 12 games played, whilst in the Minor League, the U.K. Civilians have been able to win only 1 out of 13 games played. This has kindly been put down to the fact that there was too much experience and not enough leg power. The Minor League games were played when the younger players were not available during the week. During this season we were very dependant on the R.A.F. at Safi for a pitch.

As with the other sections, the question being asked is whether the Soccer Section will cease to exist at the end of the 1977/78 season. All the Committee and most of the players return to the U.K. in July, 1978. Even if the few remaining players kept the Soccer Section in being, as a Club policy, there is still the fact that the leagues and cups, as organized by the J.S.T.F.A. (Malta), and in which the Section's teams are entered, will fold up when the Services withdraw in March, 1979.

In a team which has contained so many good and experienced players, and whose spirit has always matched its skill, it is difficult to pick out any individual for performances on the field. For the last 3 years the team has battled against dwindling numbers, added to the fact that the average age has far exceeded most of their opponents and mainly their skill has given them points. As other experienced players have left, the backbone of the team has remained Jeff Bonner, Trevor Ricketts and Dave Smith. This year Trevor celebrates his 10th year as Chairman of the Section. Jeff Bonner and Dave Smith, Captain and Vice-Captain respectively, for 3 years, have also held the following Section Offices. Jeff Bonner, Social Secretary for 2 years, 1973-75, and Hon. Secretary for 3 years, 1975-78. Dave Smith, Hon. Treasurer for 2 years, 1976-78.

For details of the Soccer Section's achievements, also league and cup results, 1975-78, I am indebted to Trevor Ricketts and Jeff Bonner.
