SOCCER SECTION
PLAYERS - PAST AND PRESENT

by Jeff Bonner

In all probability this will be the last season for the Soccer Section, and before giving detailed report on 1977/78, I would like to comment briefly on its history.

As far as the Soccer Team is concerned it would be most inappropriate to mention only the Overseas for it has only borne that name since the expansion of the Rugby Club in 1973. Prior to that it played under the name of the United Kingdom Based Civilians Football Club (U.K.B.C.), which was founded about 1963. Unfortunately, we know very little of the early days although reliable sources believe that it was a strong and successful team. In the period 1966-70 the team was drawn from various sources. They included Mike Upton, George Hepplestone, Rex Watson, Charlie Rice and Peter Miller from the University of Malta, Phil Dobson from Dingli Wireless Transmitting Station, John Whitehead, a local businessman and Mike Roberts and Trevor Ricketts representing the teachers who have always figured prominently in the team. In 1968 Trevor Ricketts, then playing on the right-wing was elected Chairman and has held the distinction of remaining in that position since that time.

The period 1970-74 was the most successful in the Club's history with victories in the Inter-Services 6 a-side Competition, the Minor League, the Minor League Cup and consistently high placing in the Major League with the newly formed Corinthians Team. The Captains during this run were Mike Upton, Dennis Locke and Jim Glover and several talented and colourful characters had now appeared in the team. In goal we were served very well by Mike Upton, Ralph Daley and Trevor Ricketts respectively. Defenders included the evergreen Phil Dobson, John Williams, Pete Joerns, Bob Tisdale and Mike Novak - the ultimate deterrent, who was guaranteed to stop anything that moved. With such a strong defence behind them, our midfield players were able to use their considerable talents to the full, among them Dennis Locke and Jim Glover, both skilful and excellent Captains, Eddie Pearson and Charlie Rice. Up front John Whitehead and Gorry...

Page 161

Porter operated on the wings and the attack was spearheaded by Peter Wright and Jeff Bonner, who between them put the finishing touches to what was a consistently high standard of football from the entire team. In the best season they scored 68 goals each and Peter Wright who was an outstanding striker with the most lethal left foot in the League, scored over 150 goals in his four seasons with the Club.

In 1974 the structure of the team changed yet again with the departure of many fine players. Other players as always came forward to fill their places, the best of these being Dave Smith, but unfortunately the team was unable to match the previous high standard. With the University no longer providing any players and Dave Cooper the sole survivor from Dingli, the number of players available diminished and in recent years the bulk of the Overseas team has come from the teachers. Among them were David Nield, Paul Goss, Tom Jordan, Brian Charnley, Mike Caseley, Jim Slide, and Mike Newton. Four other players who fully deserve a mention were Derek Ward, our two German players Eric Keifer and Dieter Herrud and Andy Holland who as well as being a very solid defender, also provided a venue for several excellent social functions at the Crystal Hotel where his parents Eddie and Margaret Holland, always entertained us in magnificent fashion.

And now in our final season we have tapped yet another source of players, the De La Rue factory in Malta which provided four very talented Geordies, Peter Carnie, Tommy Cummin, Bob Allsopp and Ronnie Feenen. Unfortunately for the Overseas, as games were largely played on Wednesday, working commitments rarely made it possible for us to field a full strength side, and therefore the team's poor showing in the Minor League was not really indicative of its true ability. The Corinthians however, finished second in the Major League, winning eight out of their 12 games and tribute must be paid to the strength and maturity shown by the Tal Handaq boys who played in this team. Among these were John Russell, who started the season as a defender but eventually proved particularly effective as a striker, Andy Basson a brave and consistently reliable goalkeeper, Andy Madge a skilful midfield and forward, Derek Bonner who was always a welcome addition to the forward line when not required by Floriana and Stuart McKee who although being the youngest in the team, improved with every game and eventually was generally acknowledged to be one of the best sweepers in the League. Other newcomers to the side were Roy Swift, who although having been seen on Malta cricket pitches for several seasons, unfortunately only made known his considerable footballing talent at this very late stage, Rodney Aird-Mash, Tony Rafferty and Dick Owen. Of the established players, Trevor Ricketts and Paul Goss continued to do good work in their unchallenged roles as Overseas goalkeeper and right back respectively, and David Nield had an excellent season being equally at home as sweeper, midfield or on the left wing. Up front Jeff Bonner, the team Captain since 1975, took his tally of goals to over 300 in eight seasons, while the outstanding player in the team was once again Dave Smith.

who has dominated the midfield for the Overseas in the four
seasons he has been with them.

The Overseas Soccer Section has over the years relied
very heavily on the more 'mature' and 'experienced' players
and many members of the team had thought that he had 'hung
up his boots' for good before arriving in Malta and letting
it be known that he 'used to' play football. This is further
illustrated in our remarkably consistent average which in
1973 was 33 and in 1978 had crept up to 34, unusually high
figures for a football team to say the least. Nevertheless,
this could well be a factor that has made the soccer team
such an enjoyable one to play for, and one which has had
considerable success during its 15 years existence. It is
particularly pleasant then to see on this last season the
Corinthians providing such an excellent farewell performance.

HOCKEY SECTION 1977/78

Chairman P. Marchant
Hon. Secretary D. Walker
Hon. Treasurer P. Marchant
Hon. Social Secretary D. Walker
Team Captain D. Walker
Vice-Captain M. Crossfield

In spite of the loss of a number of players, and a depleted Service League, Overseas continued to field a side. Even so, the gradual withdrawal of the Services from Malta was beginning to bite, and it was difficult to obtain fixtures. The Services League now contained only 4 teams, i.e. Overseas, The Navy (combined with the Commandos), the R.A.F., and the Army. To try to counteract this, the Overseas Hockey Section Secretary, Mr. David Walker, wrote to the Hockey Association Malta in an attempt to enter an Overseas team in the Malta Hockey League, but our application was rejected. The reason given was that the Association could not waive their rule that there could not be more than two non-Maltese players in any team.

As the season started there was continued difficulty in arranging matches in the Services League, also friendlies outside the league. In spite of this, a number of friendlies were played, including games against the Malta club 'Young Stars' and a local club from Qormi. The Young Stars, Malta League Champions in 1976/77, mainly Maltese teachers, defeated Overseas twice. Our relations with the Maltese clubs were very cordial.

Overseas took part in a 6 a-side competition organized by Luxol, a Maltese club which is sponsored by Pepsi-Cola, and succeeded in reaching the quarter final. The Hal Handaq XI won the Plate. During this competition, the game in which Overseas defeated Valliere (this year's Malta League leaders) appeared on Malta T.V. Overseas also took part in a 6 a-side Knockout Competition, organized by the White Hart Hockey Club, on Sunday, 2nd April. This was the first time we had been invited to take part. The competition took place at Corradino Recreational Sports Ground.

The Overseas XI was much changed from the previous seasons, and it was not always possible to field a full strength side. When it was possible, Overseas were a match for any Service side (although results rarely reflected this), and for many Maltese sides too. Even so, without 4 schoolboys from Tal Handaq we would not have been able to field a team, for besides those players who left in July, 1977, Charles Fitches and Gerry Davey were unable to play for medical reasons. We had hoped to persuade some Maltese players to join us, but with our exclusion from the Malta League there was no attraction for them, and so, to the end, we remained a U.K.-based Civilian/Tal Handaq side.

Three Overseas players, Dave Walker, John Whitehead, and Steve Oliver, were selected to play for a Combined XI (Navy, R.A.F. and Overseas) to play against the Malta XI on Sunday, 5th March, 1978. This was no mean achievement for Steve Oliver, who at 17 years of age, had already played ...

for Overseas for 2 years, and had developed into a skilful player, winning the Club award as the 'Outstanding Player of 1977/78'. He was also Captain of the Tal Handaq XI.

In what is the final year of the Hockey Section it is almost impossible to say too much in praise of the small band of men who have formed the Hockey Section Committee, particularly Peter Marchant and Dave Walker, who, since 1975/76 have shouldered most of the offices of the section between them. Also, prior to 1975/76, the same must be said of Dave Taylor and Dave Ditcham. Always fighting against loss of players and paucity of fixtures, and at the same time improving their standard on the field.

In the summer of 1978, all the present Hockey Section Committee, and almost all Section players, will leave Malta. I am informed by Dave Walker, that the last function arranged for the Hockey Section is a Dinner Dance at the Arches, Mellieha, on the 28th April, 1978. This will be the last social occasion and will signal the end of the Overseas Hockey Section.

My Thanks to Dave Walker for details from his Section reports, for vetting and bringing up to date work done, and to Trevor Ricketts and Committee, for access to Committee minutes, in writing the last 3 years of Hockey Section history.

CRICKET SECTION 1978

Annual General Meeting, Club House, 23rd March, 1978

Section Committee

Chairman M.F. Plummer
Hon. Secretary M. Newton
Hon. Treasurer D. Smith
Hon. Social Secretary M. Newton
Team Captain G. Davey
Vice-Captain D. Walker

With the 1978 cricketing season for Overseas not yet underway, and with the necessity to finish this history in order to get it to print, I can give no details of the Club’s cricketing activities for this season. This is doubly unfortunate as it is generally believed that the Overseas Cricket Section will close in July, 1978, at the end of the League programme. This is extremely sad as an Overseas Cricket XI has been part of the Malta cricket life since 1965, and has given pleasure to many, players and spectators alike. It only remains for me to wish the Cricket Section a successful and enjoyable year’s cricket.

EXTRAORDINARY GENERAL MEETING OF THE CLUB

HELD AT 21, FLAGSTONE WHARF, ON THURSDAY, 8th JUNE,1978

AGENDA - FUTURE OF THE CLUB

At this meeting, it was agreed by 25 votes to 1 that the Club should continue under the same name and with the same objectives. The meeting recognised that the main emphasis of the Club activities would revolve around the Rugby Section. This was especially so, as the Forces School Teachers would be leaving the Island next month. The Overseas Cricket, Soccer and Hockey Sections were supported almost entirely by these teachers and therefore, had no chance of continuity on the Island.

The meeting re-iterated that the Rugby Section, on the other hand, is well supported by quite a number of Maltese with Messrs D. Schembri, C. Borda, W. Ellul-Bonnici, N. Caruana, S. Mangion, T. Agius-Ferrante, M. Cassar and A. Darmanin forming the nucleus. Also, St. Edward's and De La Salle are progressing rugbywise under the guidance of Father Ferro and Mr John Taylor and if further encouragement is given, the University and Polytechnic should provide teams. There is, therefore, no reason why rugby should not continue on the Island with the main drive coming from 'Overseas'.

At the E.G.M. an interim Committee for the 1977/78 season had to be elected owing to the departure from Malta of Messrs Ricketts (President); Latham (Membership Secretary); Crossfield (Bar Manager); and Newton (Social Secretary).

It was recognised by the meeting that positions held by Messrs U. Davey, J. Bonner, D. Walker, P. Marchant, T. Jordan, D. Smith, B. Leonard, M. Plummer and M. Caseley would not be refilled.

After a vote of thanks was accorded to the above (and in particular to Trevor Ricketts for his long, invaluable service) for the great work they had done for the Club and the time which they had devoted to the furtherance of their particular sport or sports, the following elections were made:

  • President: C.J.M. Andrews
  • Social Secretary: D. Schembri
  • Membership Secretary: C. Borda
  • Bar Manager: C. Borda

The positions held by Secretary and Treasurer did not have to be altered as Messrs Macpherson and Andrews were remaining until the end of the season.

Mr Cyril Fox would continue to provide his wise counsel as Vice-President and Chairman of the Special Steering Committee.

Finally, Mr Jack Sharp would, the meeting hoped, continue (for as long as he remained in Malta) to be Chairman of the Rugby Section, which after all would be the backbone of the Club.

The meeting closed confident that "A true sporting spirit will continue to be fostered on the Island of Malta by Overseas".

OVERSEAS RUGBY
AND SPORTS CLUB
1946-1982
THE FINAL CHAPTER
1978-1982
TO
THE HISTORY OF THE CLUB
COMPILED BY NORMAN MORGAN

Foreword by Cyril Fox

In his foreword to the History of the Overseas Rugby & Sports Club published in 1979, Trevor Ricketts, as the then President of the Club, paid a fitting tribute to Norman Morgan for producing such a wonderful documentary history of the Club since the year of its formation in 1946. This was a veritable encyclopaedia of rugby football played in Malta and showed Norman's dedication and devotion to the sport. Its 183 pages, packed with such detailed information, was a grand tribute to his love of the Club. And now the final Chapter, compiled with his customary meticulous regard for detail to bring us up-to-date with the closing to 1982.

When his duties finally took him away from us in 1976, we were sad indeed to lose him, but though far away he never lost his interest in the Club and now we are more than grateful for this his "swan-song", which will make interesting reading for years to come for those of us who still have fond memories of our days in Malta and the fellowship in sport which we were privileged to enjoy.

Though in my younger years I played hockey rather than rugger, when I retired to Malta in 1968 I found my allegiance changed and I spent many enjoyable hours cheering 'Seas from the touchline and then after the match celebrating (or otherwise) in the Clubhouse.

I sincerely hope that there will be a wide circulation of Norman's book.

Acknowledgements

The author wishes to acknowledge with thanks the following:-

Overseas Committees for making available all Committee and Annual General Meeting Minutes.

The Hon. Secretaries for forwarding Minutes; Messrs. E. Macpherson (1978), F. Roberts (1978-79) and G. Attard (1979-82).

The Hon. Secretaries, also Messrs. C. Fox, J. Sharp and J. Andrews for corresponding and providing material.

Miss. H. Martin and Ms P. House for proof reading.

Messrs. C. Fox and J. Andrews for checking copy, suggesting additions and providing material for same.

P R E F A C E

The history of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, Malta, was completed up to and including the Extraordinary General Meeting on the future of the Club held on Thursday, 8th June, 1978. This meeting had been called in view of the fact that the withdrawal of the British Forces and UK Based Civilians from Malta, then due to take place on the 31st March, 1979, placed in jeopardy the existence of the Club, and in the extreme, the continuation of the game of rugby on the Island.

The Members at this meeting decided that the Club should continue under the same name, with the same objectives, and that the main emphasis of the Club's activities would revolve around the Rugby Section. Sadly, although with no alternative under the circumstances, the Cricket, Soccer and Hockey Sections were closed.

The very fact that this final chapter to the History of 'Overseas' is written informs readers that, in spite of all efforts by a dedicated few, the Club was finally forced to close. The Closure, or 'Winding-up', took place at the Annual General Meeting held on the 24th October, 1980. This placed the Club under a Caretaker Committee which held its last meeting on the 11th January, 1982.

From the time it was first accepted that the Overseas Club might be forced to close, Overseas Committees have loosely referred to its closure, and events leading up to it, as the 'Winding-up'. In this chapter I have referred to the A.G.M. on the 24th October, 1980, as the 'Winding-up', but not the 'Closure'. From this date the Club was in the hands of a Caretaker Committee, and although the chances were remote, there was still in the hearts of a few the possibility that the Club could be revived. As one Committeeman wrote, "RIP Overseas RUFC laid to rest end of 1980. Now awaits the resurrection, but doubtful if it can be resuscitated". I have referred to the last Committee Meeting of the Caretaker Committee, and so of the Club, held on the 11th January, 1982, as the 'Closure'.

As in the main history, I have written of events in chronological order within the year they happened. On the other hand, I have completed that part of the history on any subject considered to be of sufficient importance, and covering a number of years, whilst writing about the year in which it was initiated.

The Winding-up, when it came, was due basically to lack of sufficient rugby playing members interested enough to turn out on the day, and of enough teams to give any impetus to the playing of rugby in Malta. There were of course a number of other serious problems which caused the closure. Under the circumstances the knowledgeable believed this to be inevitable, but at the E.G.M. on the 8th June, 1978, there was great determination to succeed, not only to keep the Club alive, but to make rugby a Maltese game. The hard core of dedicated Maltese members, named in that part of the history dealing with the E.G.M.s, supported by the Overseas Committee, made this seem possible. This determination made the season of 1978/79 full of interest and rewarding in the initial interest and keenness shown by the Maltese, specially the schoolboys.

PART I

OVERSEAS CRICKET SECTION

Before passing on to the rugby season of 1978/79, I will mention the Cricket Section. Even as the future of the Club was being decided at the E.G.M. of the 8th June, 1978, the Overseas Cricket Section was playing in its last season at the Marsa.

The season started with a 6-a-side Tournament on the 6th May. Overseas entered two teams which were knocked out in the 1st and 2nd rounds respectively. League fixtures started on the 14th May when Overseas recorded a large win against the Army. The overall league results for Overseas were 9 played, 4 won and 5 lost. Overseas ended the season on top - what a way to go - in winning the "cup" for the first time in 8 years. I believe the memory of Overseas cricketers is best kept by quoting an extract from Cyril Fox's commentary written for 'Malta Life' in August, 1978:

"Triumph at long last for the Overseas Cricketers, who deservedly won the Government Tourist Board Trophy in their last Match at the Marsa ground on July 16th. This coveted trophy (in previous years known as the Governor-General's Cup) is played on the same lines as the Gillette Cup and is competed for by all the cricket teams on the Island. Over the years the Overseas XI's have been finalists and semi-finalists but never the outright victors. But a splendid team effort ably directed by their skipper, Gerry Davey, gave them a glorious finish to their 1978 season.

And so sad to relate it was the Overseas cricketers' last appearance in the middle where they have been playing regularly since 1965. Originally, according to the recently published "History of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club", the cricket team was formed as an activity to keep members of the Rugby Club in touch throughout the summer months. Now, with the closing of the Service schools and the schoolmasters leaving the Island, Overseas have lost the mainstay of their XI and we say good-bye to such stalwarts as Trevor Ricketts, Gerry Davey, Mike Newton, Alan Latham and Mike Caseley, who have been the principals of the cricket scene for the past several seasons.

If I was to name the Man of the Match I would have great difficulty in deciding between the two Mikes. Newton opened with a robust knock of 45 and then went on to take 4 M.s.c. wickets for 20. Caseley, who came in at No. 8, defied the bowling to score 32 of the most valuable runs, and then bowled 13 overs to take 4 for 54. Both equally winning contributions. Batting first, Overseas scored 159 for the loss of 9 wickets and this proved to be 32 too many for their opponents. Other highlights of the game to me were Gerry Davey's clouting the ball for 15 runs off one over and then skying the ball for the wicket-keeper to have ample time to trot out to square leg to collect a valuable wicket, and Trevor Ricketts being clapped to the wicket on the last of his many appearances on the pitch in his eleven years in Malta.

For the M.s.c., Roy Swift had a good match (50 not out and a couple of wickets) and Rosser and Easton shared six wickets between them. The Club had had a tough fight the previous day to beat R.a.F. Penguins in the semi-final, whilst Overseas were in good form to beat the Army by 9 wickets with Newton again in the runs with a contribution of 64."

CALYPSO DIVING CLUB

At the Extraordinary General Meeting of the 8th June, 1978, under the heading 'The Future of Overseas Rugby and Sports Club', the President, Mr. T.N. Ricketts, opened the subject for discussion from the floor. Amongst many other suggestions from members, Mr. Derek Holt, Chairman of Calypso Diving Club, Malta branch of the British Sub Aqua Club, suggested that the 'Malta Calypso B.S.A.C.' might consider amalgamation in order to boost membership to mutual benefit, as currently many Overseas members were Sub Aqua members. This was the first time that the idea of amalgamating the two clubs was mooted in Committee. The benefits to both clubs were immediately realised: a home for the Diving Club and the boosting of Overseas membership, with a possible increase in rugby playing members. The Calypso Club had a membership of 30, 12 of whom were already members of Overseas.

At an Overseas Committee Meeting held on the 28th June, 1978, it was decided that the matter should be discussed in full at the Annual General Meeting scheduled for September, 1978. Mr. C. Fox was asked to chair a Special Sub-Committee in conjunction with the Calypso Club.

The Special Sub-Committee, consisting of Mr. C. Fox, Chairman, Mr. E. Macpherson, Overseas Secretary and Calypso Club committee member, Mr. D. Holt, Calypso Club Chairman and rugby playing member of Overseas, and Mr. J. Sharp, Overseas Vice-President, met on the 17th July, 1978. The Sub-Committee's terms of reference were to consider a proposal made at the E.G.M. of the Club held on the 8th June, 1978, for the affiliation of the Calypso Diving Club to the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, and to report back to the General Committee.

At this meeting the Chairman reported that there was nothing in the Rules of the Overseas R. & S.C. to provide for the affiliation of another club, such as the Calypso Diving Club. A possible method would be for the sporting activities of Overseas to be extended to include a Sub-Aqua Section, but this would mean the loss of the name Calypso and he had been informed that this was not generally acceptable to the members of that Club. It would also mean the calling of an E.G.M. to amend the Rules. Finally the Special Sub-Committee produced the following recommendations:-

  1. That all members of the Calypso Diving Club be enrolled as members of the Overseas Rugby & Sports Club on payment of the current annual subscription and that the Calypso Diving Club be entitled to use the Overseas Club room as in the past the Sections(Cricket, Soccer and Hockey) had so done.
  2. That, with the permission of Andrews Feeds Ltd., the Calypso Diving Club might regard the Club room as their Headquarters.
  3. That consideration be given for social activities being organised jointly by Overseas and Calypso members.
  4. That the Calypso Diving Club be invited to nominate one of their members to serve on the General Committee of Overseas.

The recommendations of the Special Sub-Committee were adopted by the Overseas Committee on the 18th September, 1978, and endorsed at the Annual General Meeting of the Overseas R. & S.C. held on the 21st September, 1978. Also at the A.G.M. it was proposed and adopted to co-opt a representative from the Calypso Sub Aqua Club, namely the Chairman, Mr. D. Holt, to the new Overseas Committee. From this point, where membership is spoken of, it is the overall membership of Overseas unless otherwise indicated. According to the recommendations of the Special Sub-Committee, all Calypso members must enrol as Overseas members, but not vice versa.

Socially and financially, with both Overseas and Calypso using Flagstone Wharf as their Club House, it was to the benefit of Overseas. Joint ventures were undertaken to encourage joint interest, variety was provided to Overseas activity, and there was an increase in much needed revenue at the Club House. As has already been stated, from the outset a number of Overseas officials and players were active members of both clubs, and it was always hoped that more Calypso members would be encouraged to take an active part in the game of rugby. At the Annual General Meeting held on the 27th September, 1979, Overseas Membership Secretary, Mr. D. Schembri, reported that the loss of members from British Services personnel was made good by the Calypso Club joining Overseas. In fact the Diving Club provided 75% of the overall membership which then stood at 92.

Throughout 1979 the Calypso Diving Club had problems of its own to contend with. In February, 1980, the Calypso representative was able to report to the Overseas Committee that after a short lean period the Club had managed to solve the main problems. The main problems had been the lack of qualified Instructors, which temporarily stopped new members joining Calypso Club, and the lack of a good swimming pool for training purposes. The situation as regards Instructors was solved after a course was held in Malta in April, 1979, and a number of club members scored positive results. The Coach/Instructors exam was held during Easter and for this purpose the club brought over the B.S.A.C. Coaching Director from London. In April, 1980, the Calypso Diving Club changed its affiliation from the B.S.A.C. to the Federation of Underwater Activities.

Calypso Representatives on the Overseas Committee changed as follows:

March, 1979 Mr. J. Micallef
June, 1979 Mr. L. Spagnol
December, 1979 Mr. L. Vella Brincat
February, 1980 Mr. J. Micallef
Mr. L. Vella Brincat

These changes are taken from Overseas Committee Minutes and show the month that the Representative first sat on the committee. In February, 1980, Mr. L. Vella Brincat was joined by Mr. J. Micallef, and both sat on the Committee to the Closure.

At the Annual General Meeting the President, Mr. J. Andrews, recorded with regret the closing of the Cricket, Hockey and Soccer Sections, and noted that the Club name remained Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, thus leaving the possibility for further expansion in the future. In fact, to the end, there was no further expansion. As has been stated, the Calypso Diving Club did not become a section of Overseas although their representative sat on Overseas Committee and their members were Full Members of Overseas Club. With the closing of the sections it was accepted by members attending the A.G.M. that the Club should revert to its original form, i.e., no separate Cricket, Hockey and Soccer Sections, and that the President should thus chair all meetings. This was reverting Overseas to the form it took before the A.G.M. of the 20th September, 1973, when it was changed from a pure Rugby Club to a Rugby and Sports Club. This meant a change in the Club Rules. In making these changes it was also taken into consideration that the British Services would be leaving Malta at the end of March, 1979, and thus, for the first time since the Club was founded, the need for the Services to be worded into the rules no longer existed. It was decided to up-date the normal Full Membership qualifications, since the Service and UK Based Civilian qualifications were hardly valid any longer. The subscriptions were raised from £1M-00 to £1M-50.

I reproduce in full the Rules as formed at the A.G.M., 1978, and except for the fact that the word 'Malta' had to be taken out of the name of the Club, they were the Rules in use at the closure.

RULES OF THE OVERSEAS RUGBY AND SPORTS CLUB, MALTA, G.C.

SEPTEMBER, 1978

  1. That the name of the Club be: THE OVERSEAS RUGBY AND SPORTS CLUB, MALTA.
  2. That the object of the Club is to foster a true sporting spirit on the island of Malta by providing facilities for:
    • (a) All players who wish to play for the Club.
    • (b) Non-playing sports enthusiasts who may support the Club and join in the social life.
    • (c) Student members, who are still in full time education, who wish to become playing members of the Club.
  3. That the management of the Club shall be entrusted to a General Committee of such officers as shall be elected at the Annual General Meeting. Liaison with the representatives of the Services shall be effected by means of the Joint Services Representatives in each sport.
  4. That the General Committee of the Club shall consist of:
    President
    Vice-Presidents
    Hon. General Secretary
    Hon. General Treasurer
    Bar Manager
    Social Secretary
    The officers to hold office for one year and to be elected by members at an Annual General Meeting.
  5. That the General Committee shall have powers to fill any vacancies which may arise in their number during the course of the year, have full power to co-opt as may be found expedient, and to delegate any of its duties to such other committees as may be necessary.
  6. A quorum for the General Committee shall consist of one third of the Committee.
  7. The Annual General Meeting to be held in September and the financial year to end on the 31st August.
  8. Members to be given 14 days' notice of a General Meeting. Items for inclusion on the agenda to reach the Hon. General Secretary not later than seven days prior to the meeting. Extraordinary General Meetings may be called by ten or more members or by a majority vote of the General Committee.
  9. The Club cannot accept liability for any loss, accident or injury which may occur on the field of play or on the Club premises.
  10. That the sanction of two thirds of the number of members present and voting at the Annual General Meeting or Extraordinary General Meeting is required for the passing of any resolutions to alter the rules.
  11. Membership fees:
    • (a) Playing member Annual subscription £M1 • 50c
    • (b) Social member               "               £M1 • 50c
    • (c) Student member               "               50c
    • (d) Temporary membership  10 cents per match
          a and b only have full voting rights.
  12. That these rules be placed on the Club notice board, and a copy forwarded to each member.
  13. That, in the event of the Club winding up, the Committee in office at that time should be given authority to use any surplus funds in the furtherance of the name of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, Malta, G.C.

14. New members must be proposed and seconded by existing members and elected by the General Committee.

15. Membership will cease if:

  • (A) A member gives notice in writing to the committee to cancel his membership.
  • (b) A member fails to pay his annual subscription by 31st December and the committee removes his name from the list of members.
  • (c) A member is guilty of misconduct and in the opinion of the committee his membership should be cancelled.

16. Members may admit guests to the club premises.

The names and addresses of these guests must be recorded in the visitors' book and members are responsible for the conduct of their guests.

17. No entrance fee is payable for admission to the club premises either for members or their guests.

18. The club premises may be open to members and their guests on any evening from 4.30 p.m. to 1.00 a.m., providing a committee member be present.

19. No beer, wine or spirits will be sold to any member or guest under 16 years of age.

DELETION OF 'MALTA' FROM CLUB NAME

In November, 1978, the Maltese Government passed legislation which forbade the use of the word 'Malta' by clubs, publications, etc, without government permission. This was discussed in committee on the 2nd October, 1978, and it was decided to ask legal advice as to whether the word 'Malta' in the Club's name clashed with this legislation. On the 16th October, 1978, after receiving advice from Andrews Feed's solicitor against use of the word, Overseas Committee decided that the rules of the Club be altered so that the name of the Club no longer contained the word 'Malta'. No approach was made to the Prime Minister's office to ask to be an exception.

PLAYING SEASON 1978/79

In order to give as much background to the problems facing Overseas, and indeed all rugby enthusiasts, Maltese and British, in their attempt to keep the Club alive and the game played in Malta, I will give as much detail as possible of the different factors involved.

At the start of the playing season, including Overseas, there were still three major rugby sides. In order to have better fixtures and to give more people the chance to play rugby the Servicemen made two teams. Salerno Company 41 Cdo, as a unit, formed one of the Service teams, whilst the other was called Army Elements and consisted of R.A.F., Army and Royal Marines. It would appear that these Service teams were not as well defined as the season progressed and the time came near for the Service withdrawal.

The number of teams was increased by the visit to Malta of H.M. Ships Britannia, Alacrity, Ark Royal and Fearless in October/November, and London in March for the British withdrawal. With the initial increase in teams the season started off very well with plenty of rugby being played. Together with the promise of schoolboys' participation, the future looked promising.

The Overseas Committee spared no effort in not only making 1978/79 a successful season, but also in looking to the future by attempting to build up an Overseas team which would of necessity have to comprise mostly Maltese players. Also, everything possible was done in the effort to keep up interest in the schools, colleges and the Maltese Services, with the Overseas Team Captain acting as Liaison Officer in this field.

On the 1st October Overseas placed an advert in the Sunday Times (of Malta) which said 'RUGBY; ANYBODY WISHING TO PLAY OR WHO IS INTERESTED TO LEARN PLEASE CONTACT T. AGIUS FERRANTE'. Over 30 local men turned up, and the hope was to maintain this interest, although training players from scratch proved a slow job. A number of these recruits were from the Polytechnic. On the 10th January, 1979, it was reported that Overseas, St. Edwards, Army Elements, Salerno and some RAF players enabled a game to be played at Marsa most Saturdays. On the same date it was reported that 'recently 12 Maltese played for Overseas'. Throughout the season, admittedly with the help of Service players, and the B Team being boosted by a few 1st Team players, Overseas was able to field two teams.

Every effort was made by Overseas to promote interest in the University, the Colleges of St. Edwards, De la Salle and St. Aloysius, and the Polytechnic. An approach was made to any school which showed interest, together with an offer of coaching. The Colleges and schools were represented on Overseas Committee. Unfortunately, the only college to successfully and continuously field a team was St. Edwards under the guidance of Father Ferro. Throughout the 1978/79 season, in spite of interest shown, De la Salle and St. Aloysius did not field a team. St. Edwards gave reason to believe that interest would continue to be shown in rugby in Malta, and they were rewarded by a number of victories over Overseas 'B' Team. The schoolboys team called the Minestrones, comprised of schoolboys being educated abroad, once again proved an attraction and a hope for the future. The Minestrones played over the Christmas and Easter holidays. A number of schoolboys were keen to play for Overseas and were given every encouragement.

The Armed Forces of Malta played no active part in the 1978/79 season, although in May, 1979, Marcel Cassar, Army Rugby Representative, reported that he had been trying for some time to organise a Services (Malta) rugby team. Marcel was asked by Overseas to represent the Armed Forces on Overseas Committee but he was unable to accept.

Two competent referees, Paul Miller (Head of referees in Malta) and Bob Eaton, both in the R.A.F., officiated Overseas' games until they left Malta early January, 1979. Both were willing to give coaching and lectures in schools and to those amongst the Maltese who were interested, also to run a referees course. Derek Holt from the Royal Marines offered his services in assistant coaching. When Bob Eaton left in January, Overseas Team Captain, David Schembri, stressed the need for referees. As the Service referees left Malta, the schools representative from St. Edwards, Dave Howells, offered to referee at least school matches. Fortunately, for the 1979/80 season, two competent referees joined Overseas, namely Dave Gribbon (May, 1979) and Jim Young (January, 1980). Jim Young was also a qualified coach. For the 1979/80 season the Armed Forces of Malta also provided a referee.

Back to the 1978/79 season. Permission having been given to Overseas by the Maltese authorities to use the pitch at Marsa on Thursdays for training, and Saturdays and Sundays for games, training started in September. No indoor training took place throughout the season although the Club approached both the Ministry of Sport and the Ministry of Education for use of one of the ex-British Service gymnasiums. The first game of the season, in spite of the ground being rock hard, was played on the 14th October against H.M.S. Britannia. After this game, during the social gathering of the teams in the Overseas Club House, the Cup for the 'Most Improved Player for 1977/78' was presented to V. Ellul-Bonnici. Though it meant a great deal of work for Overseas Committee, no outstanding

Rugby Season 1978/79 Report

Problems arose during this season, and except for a period in January and February there were games most Saturdays or Sundays. The last game that an Overseas XV was ever to play against a British Service XV was on Saturday, 24th March, 1979, versus H.M.S. London. A memorable but sad occasion. After the British Services left Malta at the end of March, the rugby season came to a close with 2 games versus the Minestrones and St. Edwards College.

Besides the games against H.M. Ships, the highlights of the season were the visit of the touring side, Tallyuain Rugby Club, from Guent, the 7-a-side Tournament, and undoubtedly the tour by 'Seas to Sicily.

From all reports, the 7-a-side Tournament sponsored by Farsons, and organized by Overseas, was a success, even though rain and wind spoilt it from the spectators’ point of view. The schoolboys put up an excellent show though unfortunately they were picked to play against the Royal Marines 'A' Team, winners of the competition. Most information is to be gained from a newspaper report, and I quote:

"A 7-a-side tournament was held at the Marsa on Saturday, December 23, at which six teams competed for prizes presented by Simonds Farsons Cisk Ltd. It was encouraging for the future of Rugby on the island to see two good school sides (one from St. Edwards and one made up of boys schooling in UK) and also quite a number of Maltese players.

It was most unfortunate that a strong wind and a heavy rain spoilt the enjoyment of the spectators for the second half of the tournament. Nevertheless some entertaining fast Rugby was played in difficult conditions by the two Comando sides, the schools' teams and the Overseas.

Due to the weather conditions the presentation of the trophies, a silver salver and cups to the winners, and silver coasters to the runners-up, was postponed until Boxing Day, when Mr. A. Tabone, Marketing Manager of Simonds Farsons, made the presentations at the Overseas Club. Mr. Dave Schembri, Captain of the Overseas, presented Mr. Tabone with an Overseas Club tie."

From correspondence and personal contact hopes were high that 1978/79 season would exceed all others in the number of touring sides to visit Malta. Overseas Committee spared no effort or trouble in trying to attract the potential tourists. At one time or another Overseas Committeemen were in touch with no less than nine clubs who showed interest in visiting Malta, viz. Moseley RFC, SS Vecica Roma, Sun Life Assurance Company's UK team called Wimbledon Rugby Club, British Airways Rugby Club called Trefaers, Beudas RFC, Tallyuain Rugby Club, Selkirk RFC, John Evans XV, and Siciliflora Rugby Club from Milazzo. However, in spite of the hours of Committee work and correspondence, the records show that only Tallyuain RFC visited Malta in the 1978/79 season. For one reason or another all the others dropped out.

Tallyuain Rugby Club, from Guent, Wales, arranged to tour Malta between the 28th November and the 5th December. Unfortunately, their flight was delayed three days at Luton, and consequently they could only fit in the one game against Overseas on Sunday, 3rd December. Tallyuain played good rugby, beating Overseas 23-10, although the home side was not disgraced. Jack Sharp (who has worn a trench alongside the rugby pitch at the Marsa running the line for Overseas), stated his delight that 'Seas played so well, scoring two tries in the 2nd half. Rugby aside, the tour was not the success hoped for. The opinions expressed were that the visitors were all great singers, but not the most social crowd, and rather "standoffish". However, the main thing is that Overseas appreciated the good game of rugby.

The Overseas tour of Sicily, between Wednesday, 28th February, and Sunday, 4th March, 1979, was a great success and certainly provided a boost to rugby in Malta. As the correspondent in the Times (of Malta) wrote, after playing various combinations of 41 Cdo R.M and Overseas against each other for the past two months, it gave the low spirited players on the island a new lease of life.

9

There were problems, such as accommodation and the type of pitches, but they were all taken with a great sense of humour, and a grand time was had by all the touring party. If space allowed, I would quote Dave Schembri's report in full, it is a masterpiece of fact and humour. A good report, already commented on, was written in the Times by 'a correspondent' whose name was unknown to me, but I am told he was one of the Commandos.

There were problems, as expected under the circumstances, of getting sufficient players to travel, but on the final count 16 players made up the touring party, 11 Servicemen and 5 civilians. They were ably led (perhaps astray according to Dave's own report) by Dave Schembri (Captain) and Derek Holt (Vice-Captain). It was a great effort by Dave Schembri, Derek Holt, Charlie Borda and Francis Roberts, and of course the whole Overseas Committee.

The party travelled to Catania by the ferry 'Malta Express' and from there by train to Milazzo, which was to be their base whilst on tour, and where they were to meet their first opponents, Sicilflora Rugby Club. Signore Santino Cordraro, who was the main liaison man between the two clubs, had met them at Catania. The team was divided into groups and accommodated in three different houses, including one belonging to Signore Franco DeBartollo, the Milazzo President.

The first game, against Sicilflora, was played on the afternoon of Thursday, 1st March, on a pitch, if one can call it that, consisting of grit and volcanic ash with large stones showing through. On first seeing this pitch, the players must have been as horrified as were the players of the previous Overseas team to visit Sicily in January, 1968 (Page 67 of The History of the Club). The posts consisted of metal T.V. poles. The opposition proved to be a weak side, with little knowledge of the game, and it was one-sided in 'Seas' favour. Overseas won the game 54 points to nil.

The tourists had two days for sightseeing and the main feature seemed to be a trip by hydrofoil to the volcanic island of Lipari, a distance of 10/15 miles. A worthwhile trip as the place was very beautiful.

The second match was against Clan Rugby Club of Messina at 0830 hours on Sunday, 4th March. This early start was caused by the problem of the Club having to share a pitch with a local football side who refused to let them use it on the Saturday afternoon as originally planned. Overseas had to be at Catania at 1200 hours the same day to catch the return ferry to Malta, and so, by the time the posts had been installed, there was only time for 'halves' of 25 and 20 minutes. It proved altogether a different match, although played on the same type of gritty surface, for Clan Rugby Club were a bigger and better organised side than Sicilflora. For the most part the game was fairly even but the home side eventually won 16-6.

Sicilflora 0 Overseas 54
Clan 16 " 6

Touring Party: D. Schembri (Captain), D. Holt (Vice-Captain), N. Revert, C. Borda, D. Evans, J. Rundle, F. Roberts, A. Muckle, S. Mitchell, M. Buffins, I. Jackson, T. Worth, M. Sturgeon, C. Dickens, N. Caruana, M. Hammond.

Club House and Social Activities

The year 1978/79 proved to be the last full rugby playing season before the closure, and consequently to be the last year with a fairly full social calendar. The initial decision to close the Club was taken in April, 1980, and the Club House was given up in June, 1980. During May, 1980, the last social event organised at Committee level was held and so I will write of the Club's social life up to this point.

To the end, the Annual Dinner Dance was the important social event of the year, and the last three, all at different venues, followed the normal successful pattern bringing all rugby minded people on the Island together socially. The 1978 Annual Dinner Dance, venue Old Villa Rosa (85 attended), 20th May, organized by Michael Newton, was not quite the last social function to be held before the retiring Committee Members and UK Based Teachers left Malta. The cricket "Farewell to Overseas" dance was held at the Marsa Sports Club on the 8th July, 1978, and the occasion was used to say farewell to all Overseas leavers. For the 1979 Annual Dinner Dance a very enjoyable evening was organized by Charles and Doris Borda, venue St. Thomas Tower, Marsascala, 17th March. The occasion was used to present a plaque to referee Paul Miller in appreciation of his services to the Club. Finally, the last Annual Dinner Dance to be held, again organized by Charles and Doris Borda, venue Capua Court Hotel (51 attended), 2nd May, 1980, was the last social event to be organized at Committee level.

The three other social occasions in 1978/79 were the functions held to say farewell to Ewen & Margaret MacPherson and James & Liz Andrews, and the Christmas 'Island Rugby Fancy Dress' dance held at St. George's Social Centre, 29th December, 1978. The latter was run as an Overseas event with profits going to both Overseas and Calypso Clubs. The farewell to Ewen & Margaret was in the form of a dinner at the Astoria Hotel, on Saturday, 14th October, 1978, given by both Overseas and the Calypso Clubs. A farewell film and a farewell dinner were given in honour of James and Liz Andrews in May, 1979. The film show was given by Jack Sharp at the offices of KRS in Valletta, and the dinner was at the Astoria Hotel. As a token of appreciation the Committee presented James with a Maltese Silver Dghaisa and Liz with a Mdina Glass Tray. Guests of honour at the Dinner were Dave Gribbon, successor to James at Andrews Feeds, and Mr. & Mrs. Charles Pace. At this time, although leaving Malta at the end of May, James was still President of the Club.

Every effort was made to make use of the Club House during both the winter rugby season and during the summer when the Calypso Club was more active. The Bar was run efficiently by Charles and Doris Borda, helped at times by a roster of volunteers. Up to Christmas 1978, Charles reported a successful and active season, both with the Rugby Section and with Calypso Sub-aqua Club Members. From then on use of the bar declined, except for film nights, which were well attended and most successful, and latterly with the BSAC lecture nights. For 1979/80 Charles reported that barwise it was not a good year and the bulk of sales was thanks to Calypso members. Early in the 1978/79 season two games nights were held in the Club House. The first, organized by the Social Secretary, Dave Schembri, with the RAF, was poorly attended by 'Sea members. The second, organized by the Calypso Club, was a success.

Thanks to Jack Sharp and Charles Pace, films were provided by the M.U.f.c., later known as K.R.S., when the Maltese Government banned the commercial use of the word 'Malta, for film nights held weekly at the Club House during the winter months of 1978/79 and 1979/80. The same 'team' were instrumental in getting a pay box telephone installed in the Club. Later, after this type of phone proved too expensive for its limited use, an ordinary private telephone was installed in its stead. Costs for the latter type of phone were met by Andrews Feeds, in return Andrews were allowed to use it should the need arise. During 1978/79 structural alterations were carried out inside the Club House, both to provide more space and for better projection of films, with costs being met by £ funds raised from the social events.

Andrews Feeds. The labour was carried out by contractor Mr. M. Agius, Club members and Andrews Feeds.

The last minuted social event to be held in the Club House by Overseas, prior to relinquishing it, was a Social Evening on the 8th February, 1980, when Overseas hosted important people with whom the Club had had contacts. The list of guests for this occasion included such people as the Minister of Sport, the Directors of Andrews Feeds and the Directors of Simonds Farsons Cisk. Arrangements for this function were made by a sub-Committee consisting of Ian Agius-Ferrante, Charles Borda, and Charles Mock.

For a number of years, due to the extension of Dockyard planning, there had been the threat of 20 Flagstone Wharf being demolished. In April, 1979, came a further threat when James Andrews, President of Overseas, but also the General Manager of Andrews Feeds, owners of the premises, informed Overseas Committee that the continued availability of the premises as a Club might be in the balance owing to a re-organization to be made by the Mill. James left Malta in May, 1979, returning to Belfast. In July, 1979, when Jack Sharp spoke in Committee concerning the possible disposal of the Andrews property at Flagstone Wharf, he paid tribute to James Andrews for his efforts, both in Malta and in Belfast, to ensure that it did not happen to the detriment of Overseas. Thanks to the efforts of both James Andrews, and his successor at Andrews Feeds, Dave Gribbon, Overseas retained use of Flagstone Wharf up to June, 1980, when the rundown to the Club Closure had started, and need for a Club House for Overseas no longer existed. The Calypso Diving Club had by this time been offered the use of the Metropole Cinema as a Club House. The furniture from Overseas Club House at Flagstone Wharf was given to the Calypso Club, ostensibly on loan.

DEPARTURES FROM MALTA

Inevitably, with the large numbers of Overseas players and committeemen, including Calypso Club members, leaving Malta in the months leading up to the final British Forces withdrawal in March, 1979, many left without being mentioned in dispatches. Besides Ewan MacPherson and James Andrews, the longer serving members of the Club, those leaving included Francis Roberts, Secretary, Derek Holt, rugby player and Calypso Representative, and Paul Miller, Referee's Representative. Also, in January, 1979, the President mentioned that Mal Hunter, Bob Eaton (Referee), Bob Lee and Steve Groom had regrettably left Malta. All these had given a lot of service to the Club, both as officials and players.

EWAN MACPHERSON

After 3½ years with Overseas, as a very keen rugby player and official, Ewan left Malta at the end of October, 1978. Ewan was also a member of the Calypso Diving Club, and as he said himself, he had a foot in both camps. The service given by Ewan to Overseas is best described by James Andrews in Correspondence to me. I quote:

"Ewan, through his efforts, by example on the field during matches, and in preparation and coaching in training, did more to improve 'Overseas' rugby (Particularly forward play) in their last few years, than anyone. His contribution on the social side, linking Calypso Club with Overseas, was vital also."

JAMES ANDREWS

James Andrews left Malta on the 30th May, 1979, after 4 years as a rugby player and official with Overseas. Besides his work in keeping Flagstone Wharf open to Overseas as a Club House, James was a capable Team Captain and player, and also a very efficient President and Chairman. On leaving Malta James continued as President up to the AGM in September, 1979, with Cyril Fox chairing all meetings.

MEMBERSHIP

The last recorded Membership for 1977/78 was on the 18th April, 1978, before the Calypso Diving Club members increased numbers. This came to 103. For 1978/79, with the departure of the British Services at the end of March, 1979, it had been expected that Membership would drop drastically. Fortunately, as David Schembri, Membership Secretary, was able to report at the A.G.M. on the 27th September, 1979, the loss of members from Service personnel was made good by Calypso members joining Overseas. On this date, the Calypso Section made up 75% of the overall membership which stood at 92. The last ever recorded Membership of Overseas Rugby and Sports Club before the Closure, when the total stood at 70 paid-up Members, was on the 18th February, 1980.

MALTA CAVALIERS

On returning to UK late summer 1978, Trevor Ricketts, Life Member of Overseas, was determined to keep the ex-members of Overseas together, and in some way keep the memory of the Club alive. At the Annual General Meeting, 27th September, 1979, the Chairman, Cyril Fox, reported that Trevor had revived the old Overseas Cricket XI as the Malta Cavaliers. The Cavaliers meet for approximately one week each year in late summer when a short Tour is undertaken. The Tour in 1980 was made to Hampshire where they played 4 games. During this tour, on behalf of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, Cyril Fox presented the Cavaliers with a cheque for £50 from the Overseas funds.

extended to one of our Maltese Members who has given service to the Club, and
that as far as possible the activities of the Club should be run by the young

PLAYING SEASON

The rugby season of 1979/80 in fact turned out to be the last season in which
an Overseas XV took to the field. Inevitably it proved, after the British Forces
left Malta, in spite of valiant efforts to keep the game going, there were too
many insurmountable problems for rugby to continue in Malta. The first crack
appeared in Committee on the 31st January, 1980, and so, first, I will complete
the history to this point. From the 31st January decisions made in Committee
gradually planned the Club's Winding-up and then Closure, and in spite of these
decisions, a rearguard action was fought by the few rugby enthusiasts to save the
game in Malta.

In April, 1979, after the British Forces pulled out, Overseas Secretary,
George Attard, reported that within the Club there was a strong determination to
carry on, although the immediate problem was the almost complete lack of
referees. This problem was fortunately remedied. In May, 1979, the President,
Mr. J. Andrews, said it was very difficult to put one completely in the picture
as circumstances were changing so quickly. One minute one felt pessimistic
about the future of rugby in Malta, and the next, one could be very optimistic.
In June, 1979, George Attard again reported that the members were looking to the
future.

The reason for this optimism was the belief that a number of teams would be
formed to provide opposition. There was the strong possibility that the Armed
Forces of Malta would form one or two teams under the guidance of Marcel Cassar,
the Army Representative. St. Edwards College and De La Salle College were keen

14

to provide opposition. It was even mentioned that the little town of Senglea would form a team. In May, 1979, the Kuwait Rugby Team had contacted Mr. Charles Bezzina, the Minister of Sport, showing interest in a tour to Malta in November, 1979. With the visit of the Kuwait Club, Overseas hoped to encourage other teams to tour in Malta and so organize a Tournament. The Minister of Sport agreed to help, to provide free transport and accommodation at reduced prices, as long as Overseas saw to the overall organization. The President expressed his belief that, knowing the enthusiasm of Tim Agius-Ferrante, George Attard, David Schembri and Charles Borg, there would be good rugby during the 1979/80 season.

Early in the 1979/80 season Overseas players made use of the old R.A.F. gym at Luqa for indoor training. With permission from the Minister of Sport, Overseas again used the Marsa pitch. The rugby season started for Overseas on the 20th October with a game against the Armed Forces of Malta (No. 3 Battery) which Overseas won by 14 points to nil. Unfortunately, after this game, due to changes within the Force itself, the Army could not again field a team. Then the main blow fell. On the 25th October, 1979, torrential rain fell on Malta, flooding the Marsa pitch and covering it with four or five inches of mud. There was hope that with the use of a spiked roller the pitch could be saved, but even so, at the time it was not available for matches. The Marsa grounds were expected to be out of use for a number of months. Through the kindness of Colonel Spiteri, Commanding Officer of the Armed Forces of Malta, the Safi pitch was made available for Overseas games. Overseas then played two games against St. Edwards College, losing both, the first by 16 points to nil, and even having to borrow players from St. Edwards to field a team in the second. The final game played by an Overseas XV was over the Christmas (1979) period when they beat a Minestrone team by 30 points to 10.

The Kuwait Rugby Club was unable to tour Malta and so the November Tournament had to be cancelled. Of the other potential teams, De la Salle College did not play any game against Overseas, and there was no further word of Senglea forming a team. Early in the season, a serious injury to one of the De la Salle players caused the College to ban rugby. From this it can be seen that the main problem for Overseas was lack of opposition, and, as a consequence, diminishing interest among the players. It was also found that Safi was remote, there were transport difficulties, players failed to turn out, and matches had to be cancelled at short notice. One must also remember that, on top of the problems of fielding a team, the future of Overseas Club House, the focal point for rugby on the Island, hung in the balance.

The season ended on the 19th April, 1980, when a 7-a-side Tournament, won by St. Edwards College, was held at Safi. 5 teams competed, Overseas (2), St. Edwards (2), and the Minestrones.

15

PART II

THE WINDING-UP OF OVERSEAS

The internal problems facing Overseas were discussed in Committee on the 31st January, 1980. Mr. J. Sharp, Vice-President for many years, felt so strongly about the situation that he urged the Committee members to terminate Overseas' activities in grand style and with dignity rather than let the Club peter out through neglect. Other members, including Mr. C. Fox, also a Vice-President of long standing, and Mr. G. Attard, Secretary, whilst agreeing with Mr. Sharp's sentiments, believed that with an extra effort from each member of the Committee the Club would not only survive but also recuperate. At this stage there was still the possibility that De la Salle College would field a team.

A further cancelled game and the ban on rugby at De la Salle College, both points which forced Overseas Committee once again, on the 18th February, 1980, to discuss not only the future of Overseas, but also the very survival of the game in Malta. Mr. Sharp expressed the opinion that Overseas Committee should not make a decision on the future of the game in Malta, this should be taken at a meeting which all interested parties were invited to attend. Consequently, it was decided to call a Public Meeting of all interested parties to discuss the "Future of Rugby in Malta". A Sub-Committee was formed comprising J. Sharp, Press Adverts; D. Gribbon, Questionnaires; D. Schembri, Press Write-up; and G. Attard, Circular, to organize the proposed meeting.

The Public Forum was held in the Club House on the 27th March, 1980. The invitation was to all those interested in playing rugby, whether experienced or not. In spite of an excellent press coverage, only 27 people attended. Of this number four were senior members of the Club, four played for St. Edwards, and there was a mere handful of new faces.

After this meeting a renewed interest was shown by some University students and as a result two coaching sessions were held at the University by John Young, but insufficient students - three on the first occasion, and only one on the second - turned up. The Sevens Tournament was held in April. It was at this stage, the final blow for Overseas, that the Directors of Andrews Feeds intimated that the Marsa Wharf was due for industrial development, and that regretfully they would be re-occupying their premises at 21 Flagstone Wharf in a few months' time.

The outcome of the Public Forum was discussed at the Overseas Meeting on the 14th April, 1980. The President, Mr. Tim Agius-Ferrante, expressed the general opinion of the Committee in saying that, although some interest was shown, it was not enough to justify continuing the functioning of the Club. The Team Captain, Dave Schembri, was reluctant to admit that the game could not go on. Nevertheless, with the greatest reluctance, the Committee at this meeting on the 14th April, had no alternative but to recommend the winding-up of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club, w.e.f., the end of the current season. The President accepted Mr. Fox's offer to draw up the necessary proposals to close down the Club.

The decision to close the Club was announced publicly at the Annual Dinner Dance held at the Capua Court Hotel on the 2nd May, 1980. At the same time it was learned that the Directors of Andrews Feeds would require the return of the Club House almost immediately, and arrangements had to be made forthwith for the packing up and removal of the Club property normally kept there. At a later Committee Meeting it was decided to let Calypso make use of the Club House furniture as being on loan from Overseas.

At a Committee Meeting on the 5th May, 1980, the President informed the Committee that regretfully he had made the decision to resign from Office. At the same time a letter of resignation was received from Vice-President D. Gribbon.

16

once again, Cyril Fox stepped into the breach and acted as Caretaker Chairman.

At a Committee Meeting held on the 13th May, 1980, Cyril Fox read out a prepared statement on the Winding-up of Overseas. This statement, termed "Overseas Rugby and Sports Club - Report on Winding-up, April, 1980", gave a comprehensive outline of the Club's history, the difficulties faced, and the reasons why the Club was being wound-up. Even at this meeting the diehards, including Dave Schembri and Charles Borda, momentarily gained a breathing space when the Caretaker Chairman said that it might not be out of place to recommend the deferment of the decision taken on April 14th to close the Club down. A new spark had renewed interest outside the Club after Sevens had been held on the 19th April. However, Mr. D. Alexander, Vice-President, more knowledgeable than most on rugby matters, described the end of season Sevens as a mere flash-in-the-pan. It was decided to hold a further meeting on the 23rd June to give Messrs. J. Young, D. Schembri and C. Borda time to assess the possibilities of rugby in Malta.

On the 23rd June, 1980, a final discussion took place to finish the business of the Club in preparation for the Annual General Meeting. J. Young, D. Schembri and C. Borda reported that following their contacts with interested bodies there existed the possibility that various teams could be formed, including one from Calypso, but there was nothing concrete. The Chairman then reminded the Committee that the decision to close down Overseas had been taken.

At a Committee Meeting on the 22nd September, 1980, it was accepted that, as the decision to close down Overseas had been taken, irrespective of whether rugby would still be played in Malta, it was the present Committee's duty to call an A.G.M.

Important decisions made:-

  1. The A.G.M. to be held on Friday, October, 24th, 1980, at 7 p.m. at the Metropole Theatre, kindly made available by the Calypso Club.
  2. The present Committee would seek nomination and re-election as Caretaker Committee at the A.G.M.
  3. To freeze all funds (£140) and deposit them into a suspense account under the control of three trustees viz., C. Fox, J. Sharp and G. Attard.
  4. The Committee agreed to present the Club's regalia (plaques and banners) to St. Edwards College for as long as the college continues to function.
  5. The 7-a-side Trophy is to be formally presented to St. Edwards as the winners of last season's competition.

At a Committee Meeting held on the 13th October, 1980, it was decided to distribute the remaining Club possessions as follows:-

  1. Rugby balls to be kept by D. Schembri.
  2. First Aid kit to Calypso Club.
  3. Training films to the British High Commission.
  4. Remaining Club Histories to J. Young, G. Attard and Farsons Ltd.
  5. Remaining Club Ties to the three Vice-Presidents, namely, C. Fox, J. Sharp and D. Alexander.
  6. Club Records to be retained by G. Attard, Secretary.

It is of vital importance to have item No. 6 recorded.

17

ST. EDWARDS COLLEGE

At this point I would like to put on record the sustained efforts over a number of years, with corresponding good results, which St. Edwards College has given, both to support Overseas, and to promote rugby in their own right in Malta. I think special praise must go to Father Ferro as the driving force. There is no doubt that De la Salle and St. Aloysius Colleges also played their part, but without the same results. If ever rugby is revived in Malta it will have to be with the three Colleges, the University and the Armed Forces as the core.

PART III

THE CLOSURE

ANNUAL GENERAL MEETING, 1980

The final Annual General Meeting of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club was held in the new Club House of the Calypso Diving Club, the Metropole Theatre, B'kara, on Friday, 24th October, 1980.

Members present 14.

In view of the forthcoming closure, and the vital decisions appertaining to it, I will print in full the three Motions submitted at the A.G.M. by the General Committee, and which had previously been promulgated in an A.G.M. Notice to Members:

  1. In view of all the circumstances, the General Committee has no alternative but to recommend the winding-up of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club as from the date of this General Meeting of Members.
  2. In accordance with the terms of No. 13 of the Club Rules, the surplus funds be put in a Suspense Account.
    The Committee proposes that three Trustees be elected to review the financial position not later than the end of September, 1981. The Committee has agreed that the three Trustees should be Messrs. C. Fox, J. Sharp and G. Attard.
  3. That a Caretaker Committee of the present nine members viz. C. Fox, J. Sharp, J. Young, J. Micallef, C. Borda, L. Vella Brincat, D. Schembri, C. Mock and G. Attard be elected to safeguard the interests of the Club and to consider the use of these funds in the furtherance of the object of the Overseas Rugby and Sports Club should a favourable occasion arise.

Mr. C. Fox asked the Secretary, Mr. G. Attard, to read the Notice convening the Meeting. The Members present then confirmed the Committee's decision to appoint Mr. Fox as Chairman.

The Chairman read out a detailed report outlining the history of the Club and the reasons for its imminent winding-up.

After the normal Committee Reports for the 1979/80 season were given, the Secretary reported that no amendments had been forwarded to him regarding the three resolutions as promulgated in the Notice.

All three resolutions were read out and accepted unanimously.

PRESENTATION OF CLUB'S REGALIA

Details of this special ceremony were given to me by Mr. C. Fox. To get the true feeling of those attending I will quote Cyril's account:

"The final ceremony of the winding-up of Overseas took place at St. Edward's College in November, 1980, when, at the kind invitation of the Headmaster (Mr. A. Cachia Caruana), the members of the Caretaker Committee attended a Drinks

Party at the College. The Prefects and senior boys of the School XV were entertaining our party and were most attentive in keeping our glasses re-charged.

Mr. Cyril Fox, as President/Chairman, led the Overseas party and thanked the Headmaster for his hospitality and for his invaluable co-operation during the past several years, when his boys had played such an active part on the Marsa pitch. In his speech Mr. Fox made reference to the services which Mr. Charles Mock, the School's sports master, had given to Overseas in his coaching and physical training classes. He also singled out Tim Agius-Ferrante, a former Head Boy at Tal Handaq School, who had given yeoman service to Overseas, both on the field and in the committee room. Then came the handing-over ceremony. Mr. Fox, on behalf of the club, handed over all the trophies, plaques and banners which had been collected over the years and had been decorating the Club House (and as members will recall we had a goodly collection). The Headmaster was very gracious in his reply. A pleasant, though sad occasion, which ended an era of rugby football in Malta."

CARETAKER COMMITTEE

The Caretaker Committee met initially on the 10th November, 1980, and during 1981 'minuted meetings' were held at infrequent intervals. Informal meetings were also held. Meetings and a monthly social gathering took place at the offices of K.R.S. in Zachary Street, Valletta.

On the 10th November, Cyril Fox and George Attard were elected Chairman and Hon. Secretary respectively. Tim Agius-Ferrante was co-opted onto the Caretaker Committee to become Hon. Treasurer. At this meeting the Chairman reminded those present that the Club had been placed in moth balls, so to speak, until September, 1981, when the final depositions would be made. The Caretaker Committee's first moves were to implement decisions made in Committee previous to the A.G.M. as regards the new arrangements of Club funds, also presentations. The following organisations had to be officially informed of the winding-up of Overseas: Andrews Feeds, the Press, St. Eduards, the University, Insurance, the Armed Forces, the Ministry of Sport, the Police and the R.F.U.

Jack Sharp continued living in Malta until his return to England at the beginning of 1982. But right up to the date of his departure he kept his interest in Overseas and regularly held his well-known and always appreciated drinks and film evenings. His invitations always included the ladies and with Jack and Dorothy the Committee kept the spirit of fellowship in the great sport of rugby football going to the end.

The final meeting of the Caretaker Committee was deferred to the 11th January, 1982. The main item on the agenda at this meeting was to dispose of the balance of the Club funds as required by the resolutions passed during the A.G.M. and according to the three Trustees' recommendations. The Overseas Rugby and Sports Club did not have a large amount of money to dispose of and a great deal of thought must have been put into its method of disposal. The funds, in accordance with the Trustees' recommendations, were distributed as follows:-

1. Secretarial expenses and postage £10-00

2. Grant to K.R.S. film operator Mr. J. Calleja -

We have been most grateful to Jack for his generous hospitality for which he has always refused to accept contributions, but feel we might recognize one of his employees.

£10-00

3. Sub-Aqua Club - Calypso Divers £25-00

were accepted into membership in 1979.
This grant is to go towards the upkeep of their new Club premises. At their request a plaque is to be made to commemorate their association with Overseas.£15-00

4. St. Edwards College £25-00

This school has always shown keen support towards rugby in Malta. The donation is for the College's Sports Fund.

5. Rugby Football Union £37-00

The Chairman referred to the intentions of the Committee as far back as 1972 and quoted in the 'History' pp 86-87:
"In furtherance of Junior Rugby to commemorate the name of Overseas Club." A donation of £Stg50-00 is to be made.

6. History of the Club £18-00

or £Stg25-00. Norman Morgan is to be asked to prepare a short postscript to cover the activities of the Club over the past two or three years, up to the decisions of this Committee. Copies of this postscript are to be sent to all members of the Committee and others concerned.

£140-00

The Trustees agreed to make arrangements to see that their recommendations were implemented.

So ended a great Club.

The Chairman, Cyril Fox, also gave up his residence in Malta and left for home in England in June, 1982. The last of the expatriates. Now, having achieved his 80th birthday, Cyril can sit back and enjoy rugger on the television. Since his return he has received a most kind letter from Mr. R.H.G. Weighill, the Hon. Secretary of the R.F.U.

A copy of Mr. Weighill's letter to Cyril Fox is included in this Final Chapter.

Always first and foremost a Rugby Club, but latterly also a Sports Club, Overseas promoted rugby in Malta for 36 years and it is to be hoped left seeds of the game to be developed in future years.
